And the fifth condition for the validity of the opening takbir is the specification of the prescribed prayer at the beginning of starting. So if he intends a fard (prescribed prayer) and starts it, then forgets and thinks it is a supererogatory prayer, and completes it thinking it is supererogatory, it is a fard that drops his obligation. This is because the valid intention is required to accompany the first part. Similarly, the opposite would be supererogatory. And it is not required to intend the number of rak'ats. So if he intends Fajr as four or Zuhr as three, and completes it as required, it is valid. The requirement of specification includes the imam, the follower, and the one praying alone because of the multiplicity of fard prayers, both on time and makeup. So he must specify what he wants, because their causes are different, and the obligatory differs according to them. So he intends, for example, the Zuhr of today or the Zuhr of the time. If he intends just 'Zuhr' without adding something that specifies it, it does not suffice, because maybe he has a missed prayer. It is not specified. However, in Fatawa al-Attabi, he said: The correct view is that it does suffice. End. And if he intends only the word 'fard', it also does not suffice because fard prayers are diverse. As for if he intends 'the fard of the time' within the time, it suffices except for Jumu'ah, as we will mention. Outside the time, it does not suffice because after the time exits, the fard of the time is 'Asr, not Zuhr. This is in al-Diraya. If the time has left and he forgot, it does not suffice in the correct view, as in al-Fath. It is better to intend 'Zuhr of today' whether the time is in or out, due to the diversity of obligations. In Jami' al-Kardari: He intends the fard of Jumu'ah, not the fard of the time, because it is disputed. And if he combines a missed prayer and a present one, he does not become a starter of either. For example, intending 'Asr and Zuhr in 'Asr time. In al-Muntaqa: If there is ample time, he becomes a starter of Zuhr. In al-Khulasa: If he intends two missed obligatory prayers, it is considered for the first of them. And he explained in al-Muhit that the second is not valid except after performing the first. The author of al-Bahr said: This only stands if order (tartib) is obligatory between them. End. I say: This is the interpretation, because he said in Khayr Mathlub: If he intends two fard prayers, he does not become a starter of either. It is interpreted as when order has been dropped, as neither has priority over the other, harmonizing the two supererogatory? End. And if he combines a fard and a supererogatory, he becomes a starter of the fard according to Abu Yusuf, because the fard is stronger than the supererogatory, so the supererogatory intention is overruled and only the fard remains.
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage discusses the fifth condition for the validity of the opening takbir: specifying which fard prayer one intends (ta'yin al-fard). The reason is that there are multiple obligations (ada and qada), so the worshipper must know which one he is performing. The ruling applies to the imam, the follower, and the one praying alone. The text gives examples: if one forgets and mistakenly completes as supererogatory, it still counts as fard because intention at the start is what matters. Intending the number of rak'ats is not required. The text warns against vague intentions: merely intending 'Zuhr' does not suffice because it might not specify whether it is the current Zuhr or a makeup; however, there is a minority view from al-Attabi that it suffices. Intending 'fard' alone also does not suffice. Within the time, intending 'fard of the time' works except for Jumu'ah. Outside the time, it does not suffice. The recommended wording is 'Zuhr of today' to cover all possibilities. For Jumu'ah, one should intend 'fard of Jumu'ah' specifically. The text also deals with combining multiple intentions: if one intends two fard prayers (e.g., a makeup and current prayer), he does not validly start either; if he intends two missed prayers, it counts for the first one only if order is obligatory. If he combines a fard and a nafl, according to Abu Yusuf, the fard intention prevails.

Key Terms
الترتيب (al-tartib): Obligation to perform prayers in order; missed prayers must be made up before the current prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Yusuf, what happens when someone combines a fard and a nafl in one intention?
A) Both prayers are invalid.
B) Only the nafl is valid.
C) Only the fard is valid.
D) Neither prayer counts; the intention is void.

Key Takeaway
Combining two fard prayers in one intention is generally invalid; combining fard and nafl results in the fard prevailing.

Specifying Intention Not Required in Supererogatory Prayers
Ruling on ta'yin in nafl with application to sunan and tarawih

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on specifying intention (ta'yin) in supererogatory prayers and identify the practical precautions recommended by later scholars.

Core Idea
In Hanafi fiqh, you need not specify which nafl prayer you intend—the general intention suffices.

This passage from Nur al-Idah and its commentary addresses a frequent practical question: when performing supererogatory prayers, must you explicitly intend which one? The ruling is clear—ta'yin is not required—but later scholars add nuances for tarawih. Let's explore the reasoning and the recommended precaution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
Extract the primary legal statement: specification (ta'yin) is not required in supererogatory prayers (nafl). This is the mutun position, declared the most correct (asahh).
The text uses 'ولا يُشْتَرَط' — a strong negation of conditionality.
2
Understand the scope
Note that the ruling includes all sunan, both mu'akkadah and ghayr mu'akkadah, and also tarawih according to the majority (amma mashayikhina).
Even the highly emphasized sunnah of Fajr is included.
3
Examine the intra-Hanafi disagreement on tarawih
Some Hanafis (reported by Qadi Khan) held that ta'yin is required for tarawih and that each pair (shaf') needs a separate intention. Understand their reasoning: tarawih is a specific prayer.
This shows the later scholarly development.
4
Determine the relied-upon view and precaution
The commentator sides with the majority: no ta'yin needed, and the whole tarawih is like one prayer. However, due to conflicting authentications, the precaution (ihtiyat) is to intend tarawih, sunnah of the time, or night prayer.
This balances the madhhab's position with practical caution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يُشْتَرَط التَّعيينُ في النَّفْلِ) أطلقه فشمل سنة الفجر، وهو الأصح كغيرها من السنن المؤكدات، وكذا التراويح عند عامة مشايخنا، وهو الصحيح، وسيأتي، لأن السنن نوافل، وهي غير مضمومة قبل الشروع فيها، ولا أسباب للسنن، لأنها لتكميل الفرائض، بخلاف الفرائض والواجبات كما بيناه . كذا في ( الدراية». وقال « قاضي خان» في فصل التراويح: اختلف المشايخ في السنن، والتراويح، الصحيح أنها لا تتأدى بنية الصلاة ونـيـة التطوع، لأنها صلاة مخصوصة، فيجب مراعاة الصفة للخروج عن العهدة، وذلك بأن ينوي السنة أو متابعة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وهل يحتاج لكل شفع من التراويح، أن ينوي، ويعين قال بعضهم: يحتاج، لأن كـل شـفـع صـلاة، والأصح أنه لا يحتاج، لأن الكل بمنزلة صلاة واحدة، قال صاحب ( البحر » : فقد اختلف التصحيح، فلذا قال في « منية المصلي : والاحتياط في التراويح أن ينوي التراويح، أو سنة الوقت، أو قيام الليل، انتهى.
And specification (ta'yin) is not required in supererogatory prayer (nafl). He (the author) gave it absolutely, so it includes the sunnah of Fajr, and this is the most correct view, like other confirmed sunnahs, and likewise tarawih according to the generality of our scholars, and it is the correct view, and it will come (later), because sunnahs are supererogatory, and they are not guaranteed (by intention) before commencing them, and there are no causes for sunnahs, because they are for completing the obligatory prayers, contrary to obligatory prayers and necessary acts as we have explained. Thus in al-Diraya. And Qadi Khan said in the chapter of tarawih: The scholars differed regarding the sunnahs and tarawih. The correct view is that they are not performed by the intention of prayer and the intention of supererogatory act, because they are specific prayers, so it is necessary to observe the description for discharge of responsibility, and that is to intend the sunnah or following the Prophet (peace be upon him). And is it necessary for each pair (shaf') of tarawih to intend and specify? Some said: it is necessary, because each pair is a prayer. The most correct view is that it is not necessary, because the whole is like one prayer. The author of al-Bahr said: The authentication differed. Hence it is said in Minyat al-Musalli: The precaution in tarawih is to intend tarawih, or the sunnah of the time, or night prayer. End.
Source pages p. 226

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the matn of Nur al-Idah, expanded by the commentator. The core ruling is that specifying the exact type of prayer (ta'yin) is not required in supererogatory prayers (nafl). This applies to all sunnah prayers, including the confirmed sunnah of Fajr, as well as tarawih. The reasoning is that sunnah prayers are essentially supererogatory (nawafil) and are not guaranteed (i.e., they do not become obligatory simply by intending them). Unlike obligatory (fard) and necessary (wajib) prayers, which require specific intention to discharge the obligation, sunnahs are performed for completion of the obligatory prayers. The commentator then notes a difference among later Hanafi scholars regarding tarawih: Qadi Khan reports that the correct view is that merely intending prayer or supererogation is insufficient because tarawih is a specific prayer; one must intend the sunnah or following the Prophet. There is also a dispute about whether each pair of rak'ahs needs a separate intention. The relied-upon view (al-sahih) is that it does not, as all pairs are like a single prayer. Due to conflicting authentications, the author of Minyat al-Musalli advises precaution: to intend tarawih, the sunnah of the time, or night prayer.

Key Terms
التعيين (al-ta'yin): Specifying the exact type of prayer in the intention (e.g., intending specifically the Fajr sunnah vs. just any prayer).
النفل (al-nafl): Supererogatory prayer, including sunnah mu'akkadah and optional prayers.
التراويح (al-tarawih): Special night prayers performed during Ramadan, consisting of 20 rak'ahs (in the Hanafi school) with salutations after every two rak'ahs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on specifying intention (ta'yin) in supererogatory prayers according to the relied-upon view in this text?
A) It is required for all supererogatory prayers
B) It is not required
C) It is required only for tarawih
D) It is required for sunnah mu'akkadah but not for others

Key Takeaway
Specifying intention is not required in supererogatory prayers, but precaution in tarawih is to intend tarawih or the sunnah of the time.

Obligation of Standing (Qiyam) in Obligatory Prayers
Ruling with proof: obligation, conditions, and definition of qiyam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of qiyam in fard and wajib prayers, identify the conditions that excuse a person from standing, and explain the Hanafi proofs from Quran, hadith, and ijma.

Core Idea
Standing is a binding pillar in obligatory prayers but is dropped when one cannot stand and perform bowing/prostration together.

In this passage, the commentator establishes a fundamental Hanafi ruling: standing (qiyam) is a required pillar in every fard and wajib prayer. However, this obligation is not unconditional—it depends on the ability to also bow and prostrate. The passage also defines the minimum standard of standing, provides the Quranic and hadith evidence, and lists specific excuses that lift the requirement. Understanding these details ensures correct prayer performance for those with valid hardships.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is qiyam (standing) during prayer. According to the matn, it is fard (obligatory) in every fard (obligatory) or wajib (necessary) prayer. Note that the commentator treats wajib like fard for this ruling.
The ruling applies to both fard and wajib prayers, not just the five daily fards.
2
Recognize the conditions for the obligation
The obligation is conditional on being able to stand AND able to bow and prostrate. If a person can stand but cannot perform ruku' and sujud, standing is not required.
This is a key qualification: ability must cover all three actions.
3
Apply the exceptions and excuses
The text gives specific examples: a person with urinary incontinence who can control it by sitting but not by standing; a person who is too weak to recite while standing; and a person who cannot go out for congregation due to weakness. In all cases, the person prays sitting with recitation at home according to the mufta bihi view.
These excuses are based on the principle that hardship brings ease in Shariah.
4
Examine the evidence (dalil)
The primary proof is Quran 2:238: 'And stand before Allah devoutly obedient.' The imperative indicates obligation. Additionally, the hadith 'The sick person prays standing; if he cannot...' and consensus (ijma) support the ruling.
The Quranic command is general; it is specified to prayer because standing is not obligated outside of prayer.
5
Define qiyam and distinguish pillars
The minimum qiyam is defined as standing such that when one extends his hands, they do not reach the knees. Qiyam is an original pillar (rukn asli), while recitation is an additional pillar (rukn zaid). The imam bears the recitation for followers but not the standing.
This distinction has practical implications: followers must still stand even if the imam recites for them.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَ) يفترض ( القِيَامُ) في كل صلاة مفروضة أو واجبة، لأن الواجب بمنزلة الفرض فيه للقـــادر عليه وعلى الركوع والسجود، ولا يفوته بقيامه شرط طهارة ، ولا قدرة القراءة، وقيدنا بهذه القيود لما سنذكره (۳) من أنه لو تعسر عليه القيام، أو قدر على القيام، وعجز عن الركوع والسجود، لا يلزمه القيام، ومن به سلس بول بحيث لو قام نزل، وإن جلس احتبس يصلي جالساً، ولو ضعف عن القراءة بالقيام أو بالخروج للجماعة، يصلي قاعداً بالقراءة في بيته على المفتى بـه، وسقط القـيـام للعـذر، لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَقُومُوا لِلَّهِ قَنِتِينَ ﴾ [البقرة: ۲۳۸] أي مطيعين ولم يجب القيام في غير الصلاة، فتعين أن يكون الأمر بالقيام في الصلاة، وعليه انعقد الإجماع أيضاً ، وقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: «يُصَلِّي المريض قَائِمَا، فَإِنْ لَمْ يَسْتَطِعْ ، إلخ، دليل على لزوم القيام أيضاً، ثم القيام ركن أصلي، والقراءة ركن زائد، إذ هي زينة القيام، ولهذا يتحمل الإمام القراءة، دون القيام، كما في «مجمع الروايات»، واتفقوا على ركنيته، وحد القيام أن يكون بحيث إذا مد يديه لا تنال ركبتيـه كـمـا في « الســراج الوهاج»، وقوله (في غَيْرِ النَّفل) متعلق بالقيام، فلا يلزم القيام في النفل، لأن مبناه على التوسع كما سنذكره (۱) ، إن شاء الله تعالى
And standing (qiyam) is obligatory (yufarad) in every obligatory (mafrudah) or necessary (wajibah) prayer, because the wajib is like the fard in it for the one able to do it and able to bow and prostrate, and his standing does not miss the condition of purity or ability to recite. And we restricted it with these restrictions for what we will mention later: that if standing is difficult for him, or he is able to stand but unable to bow and prostrate, standing is not required of him. And one who has urinary incontinence such that if he stands it flows, but if he sits it stops, he prays sitting. And if he is weak from reciting while standing or from going out for the congregation, he prays sitting with recitation in his house according to the mufta bihi (relied-upon view). And standing is dropped due to excuse, because of His statement: 'And stand before Allah devoutly obedient' [Al-Baqarah 2:238], i.e., obedient. And standing was not obligatory outside of prayer, so it is determined that the command is for standing in prayer. And upon this consensus has been made. And his statement (peace be upon him): 'The sick person prays standing; if he cannot...' is also evidence for the necessity of standing. Then standing is an original pillar (rukn asli), and recitation is an additional pillar, for it is the adornment of standing; hence the imam bears the recitation but not the standing, as in Majma' al-Riwayat. And they have agreed on its being a pillar. And the definition of standing is that when he extends his hands, they do not reach his knees, as in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. And his statement 'in other than supererogatory' (fi ghayr al-nafl) is attached to standing, so standing is not required in supererogatory prayer, because it is built on leniency, as we will mention, if Allah wills.
Source pages p. 226

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, establishing the obligation of standing (qiyam) in every fard and wajib prayer. The commentator explains that 'wajib' is treated like 'fard' for this ruling. However, the obligation is conditional upon ability: one must be capable of standing, bowing, and prostrating simultaneously. If standing is difficult, or if one can stand but cannot bow and prostrate, standing is dropped. Examples include the person with urinary incontinence who can control it by sitting, and the weak person who cannot recite if standing or cannot go to the mosque. The primary proofs are the Quranic verse (Al-Baqarah 2:238) commanding standing in prayer, and the hadith of the sick person praying standing if able. Consensus (ijma') also supports this. The commentator distinguishes between standing as an original pillar and recitation as an additional pillar. The imam's recitation suffices for the followers, but the imam cannot bear their standing. The definition of adequate standing is when one's outstretched hands do not reach the knees. Finally, standing is not required in nafl prayers, as they are built on ease.

Key Terms
القيام (al-qiyam): Standing upright during prayer. The minimum is such that outstretched hands do not touch knees.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Standing fully erect without any bending
B) Such that when one extends his hands, they do not reach his knees
C) Such that one's head is level with the imam
D) Standing on both feet without support

Key Takeaway
Qiyam is a binding pillar in fard and wajib prayers for those able, but valid excuses (such as inability to bow/prostrate, incontinence, or weakness) drop this requirement.

Obligation of Recitation in Prayer: Fard and Additional Pillar
Ruling that qira'ah is fard with proofs and refutation of opposing views

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the evidence for the obligation of recitation in prayer and explain why it is classified as a rukn za'id (additional pillar) in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Recitation is fard by Quran, hadith, and consensus, but it is an additional pillar that drops for the follower.

In this passage from Imdad al-Fattah, the commentator explains that recitation of the Quran in prayer is not merely recommended but obligatory (fard). He provides the key proofs—the Qur'anic verse from Surah al-Muzzammil and the prophetic hadith—and defends the Hanafi position against dissenting voices. Most importantly, he introduces the Hanafi distinction between original pillars (arkan asliyya) and additional pillars (arkan za'ida), classifying recitation as the latter, which explains why it can be omitted for the follower (muqtadi) without invalidating the prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its definition
The passage opens by stating that recitation is obligatory (fard). It defines recitation's reality (haqiqah) as making oneself hear one's own pronunciation. Understand this baseline before proceeding to the evidence.
This definition is important for later discussions of the minimum required recitation (e.g., one verse).
2
Locate the primary proofs (dalil)
The author cites three proofs: the Quranic verse 'faqra'u ma tayassara min al-Qur'an' (Al-Muzzammil 73:20), the hadith 'thumma iqra' ma tayassara ma'aka min al-Qur'an', and the consensus (ijma') of the Salaf. Examine how each proof supports obligation.
The verse's imperative ('faqra'u') is the strongest textual indicator.
3
Refute the metaphorical interpretation of the verse
Some exegetes claimed the verse means 'pray' not 'recite,' citing the context of night prayer. The author responds that the real meaning (haqiqah) takes precedence over metaphor (majaz), and the context actually supports the real meaning because 'wa aqimu al-salah' follows, distinguishing recitation from prayer.
This is a standard Hanafi usul principle: al-haqiqah muqaddamah 'ala al-majaz.
4
Analyze the response to opposing views
Opponents (Abu Bakr al-Asamm, Isma'il ibn 'Ulayyah, etc.) argued recitation is recommended based on 'Umar's hadith and Zayd ibn Thabit's statement. The author counters that the consensus overrides these weak reports, and 'Umar's case is interpreted as forgetfulness or following an imam.
The consensus of the Salaf is considered a decisive proof in Hanafi methodology.
5
Understand the Hanafi classification of recitation as rukn za'id
The passage divides pillars into original (asli) and additional (za'id). Original pillars never drop except for necessity (e.g., standing). Additional pillars can drop in some cases without necessity. Recitation is an additional pillar because it drops for the follower (muqtadi) in congregation according to Hanafi fiqh.
This classification reconciles the absolute obligation with the concession for the follower.

وَ) يفترض ( القِرَاءةُ)، وحقيقتها : أن يسمع نفسه نطقه، كما ذكرناه في بحث التحريمة وكانت القراءة فرضاً لقوله تعالى: ﴿فَاقْرَهُ وَاْ مَا تَيَسَّرَ مِنَ الْقُرْءَانِ ﴾ [المزم : ٢٠] ولقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: « ثم اقرأ ما تيسر معكَ مِن القُرآنِ ) وعلى فرضيتها انعقد الإجماع، وذكــره الزيلعي وغيره، وصح الاستدلال بالآية، لأن المراد منها قراءة القرآن بحقيقته، ويدل عليه السياق، وهو قوله [ تعالى ] عقيبه : ﴿وَأَقِيمُوا الصَّلَوَة ﴾ [المنت : ٢٠]، وهذا تفسير بحقيقتها، والحقيقة مقدمة على المجاز، فهو مقدم على ما قال بعض المفسرين بأن المراد من الآية الصلاة، بدليل السياق، وهو قوله تعالى: ﴿ إِنَّ رَبَّكَ يَعْلَمُ أَنَّكَ تَقُومُ أَدْنَى مِن ثُلُيَ الَّيلِ [ المنتك : ٢٠] إلى قوله: ﴿عَلِمَ أَن لَّن تُحْصُوهُ فَنَابَ عَلَيْكُمْ أَي: علم أن لن تقدروا على حفظ ساعات الليل فرفع عنكم وجوب القيام المقدر، فاقرؤوا ما تيسير أي: فصلوا ما تيسر عليكم من صلاة الليل، عبّر عن الصلاة بالقراءة لأنها بعض أركانها، وكانت صلاة الليل المقدرة فرضاً، ثم انتسخت إلى المقدر، ثم انتسخت أصلاً بالصلوات الخمس انتهى. لأنـه تفسير بالمجاز والأول بالحقيقة، وتأيد بالحديث المبين للفرائض بقوله : « ثم اقرأ ما تيسر » (۳). على أن هذا في الواقع سنة ،الإجماع، وهو يكفي للسند، فإن القراءة ركن في الصلاة بالإجماع، ولا خلاف فيه لأحد ممن يتبع، ولا يلتفت إلى قول أبي بكر الأصم لأنه خرق لإجماع السلف، وكذا الجواب عن قول ( إسماعيل بن علية » و « الحسن بن صالح » و « سفيان بن عيينة » : ليست القراءة بفرض في الصلاة، بل هي مستحبة، لما روي عن عمر بن الخطاب له : « أَنَّهُ صلَّى المغرب فلم يقرأ فيها فقيل له، فقال: كيف كان الركوع والسجود قالوا: حسناً، قال: فلا بأس إذا ) رواه الشافعي وغيره، وعن زيد بن ثابت قال : القراءة سنة ) ، رواه البيهقي، واختلف في كون القراءة ركناً، فذهب الغزنوي صاحب ( الحاوي القدسي إلى أنها ليست كن، والجمهور أنها ركن، غير أنهم قسموا الركن إلى أصلي، وهو : ما لا يسقط إلا لضرورة، وزائد وهو ما يسقط في بعـض الـصـور مــن غـيـر تحقق ضرورة، وجعلوا القراءة من هذا القسم، فإنها تسقط عن المقتدي بالاقتداء عندنا، وعن
And recitation (qira'ah) is obligatory. Its reality is that he makes himself hear his own pronunciation, as we mentioned in the discussion of takbir al-tahrimah. And recitation was made obligatory by the statement of Allah: 'So recite what is easy from the Quran' [Al-Muzzammil 20] and by the statement of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Then recite what is easy for you from the Quran.' And upon its obligatoriness consensus has been made, as mentioned by al-Zayla'i and others. And the deduction by the verse is sound, because what is meant by it is recitation of the Quran in its real sense, and the context indicates that: His statement afterwards: 'And establish prayer' [Al-Muzzammil 20]. This is an interpretation by its reality, and the reality is given precedence over metaphor. So it takes precedence over what some exegetes said: that the verse means prayer, citing the context: 'Indeed, your Lord knows, [O Muhammad], that you stand [in prayer] a little less than two-thirds of the night' [Al-Muzzammil 20] up to His statement: 'He knows that you will not be able to do it, so He has turned to you [in mercy], i.e., He knows that you will not be able to keep track of the hours of the night, so He has lifted from you the obligation of standing that was estimated. So recite what is easy, i.e., pray what is easy for you from the night prayer. He expressed prayer by recitation because it is part of its pillars. And the estimated night prayer was an obligation, then it was abrogated to the estimated, then it was abrogated entirely by the five prayers.' End. Because it is an interpretation by metaphor, while the first is by reality. And it is supported by the hadith that clarifies the obligations: 'Then recite what is easy.' Moreover, this is in fact the sunnah, consensus, and it is sufficient as evidence. For recitation is a pillar in prayer by consensus, and there is no disagreement about it among those who follow. And no attention is paid to the statement of Abu Bakr al-Asamm because he broke the consensus of the Salaf. Likewise the response to the statement of Isma'il ibn 'Ulayyah, al-Hasan ibn Salih, and Sufyan ibn 'Uyaynah: 'Recitation is not an obligation in prayer; rather it is recommended.' Based on what was narrated from 'Umar ibn al-Khattab: 'He prayed Maghrib and did not recite, so it was said to him. He said: How were the bowing and prostration? They said: Good. He said: Then there is no problem.' Reported by al-Shafi'i and others. And from Zayd ibn Thabit: 'Recitation is sunnah.' Reported by al-Bayhaqi. And they differed regarding whether recitation is a pillar. Al-Ghaznawi, author of al-Hawi al-Qudsi, held that it is not a pillar, while the majority held that it is a pillar. However, they divided the pillar into original (asli): that which does not drop except for necessity, and additional (za'id): that which drops in some cases without actual necessity. And they made recitation of this type, as it drops from the follower (muqtadi) by following in our school, and from...
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, establishing that recitation of Quran in prayer is obligatory (fard). The commentator defines its reality as making oneself hear one's own utterance. The primary proofs are the Quranic verse 'faqra'u ma tayassara min al-Qur'an' (Al-Muzzammil 20) and the hadith 'thumma iqra' ma tayassara ma'aka min al-Qur'an'. Consensus (ijma') is also cited. The commentator then refutes the interpretation that the verse refers to prayer (salat) rather than actual recitation, arguing that the real meaning (haqiqah) takes precedence over metaphor. He also refutes the opinions of Abu Bakr al-Asamm, Isma'il ibn 'Ulayyah, al-Hasan ibn Salih, and Sufyan ibn 'Uyaynah, who held that recitation is merely recommended (mustahabb). Their proofs (the hadith of 'Umar and the statement of Zayd ibn Thabit) are countered by the overwhelming consensus. Finally, the passage discusses whether recitation is a pillar (rukn). Al-Ghaznawi said it is not, but the majority consider it a rukn, though they divide the rukn into original (asli) and additional (za'id). Recitation is an additional pillar because it can drop in some cases, such as for the follower (muqtadi) in Hanafi fiqh. This classification reconciles the position that recitation is obligatory yet can be omitted in specific circumstances without invalidating the prayer.

Key Terms
القراءة (al-qira'ah): Recitation of Quran in prayer, defined as making oneself hear one's own pronunciation.
ركن أصلي (rukn asli): Original pillar: a component of prayer that never drops except for genuine necessity, e.g., standing.
ركن زائد (rukn za'id): Additional pillar: a component that can drop in some cases without actual necessity, e.g., recitation for the follower.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is recitation classified as an additional pillar (rukn za'id) rather than an original one?
A) Because it is not mentioned in the Quran
B) Because it can drop in some cases, such as for the follower
C) Because it is not required for the imam
D) Because it is recommended, not obligatory

Key Takeaway
Recitation is fard in prayer by clear evidence, but as an additional pillar, it drops for the follower, reconciling obligation with practical concession.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Obligation of Recitation in Prayer and Its Sufficient Minimum
Establishes obligation and minimum recitation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the obligation of recitation in prayer (fard), identify its reality as hearing oneself, and explain the Hanafi position on the minimum verse that suffices, including the ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Recitation is a fard pillar of prayer; its minimum is a two-word verse per Abu Hanifa, but caution prefers a longer amount.

In this passage, the author of Imdad al-Fattah establishes the obligation of Quranic recitation (qira'ah) during prayer as a fard component, citing clear proofs from the Quran and Sunnah and invoking consensus. He then addresses a practical question: what is the minimum amount of recitation that fulfills this obligation? The answer involves a nuanced intra-Hanafi disagreement, highlighting how legal principles and caution intersect in worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its evidence
First, note that the passage declares recitation as fard (obligatory). Identify the Quranic verse (73:20) and the hadith cited, and understand how they are used: the imperative 'اقرأ' indicates obligation per Hanafi usul.
The author also invokes ijma' (consensus) to strengthen the proof.
2
Analyse the refutation of alternative interpretations
The author refutes those who interpret the verse as referring to prayer metaphorically, arguing that the literal meaning (haqiqah) takes precedence. Also note the dismissal of opinions that recitation is mustahabb.
This step shows the method of tafsir and tarjih between haqiqah and majaz.
3
Understand the distinction between essential and additional pillars
The passage explains that recitation is a rukn but classified as 'additional' (za'id) because it drops in certain cases (follower, latecomer). Grasp the two considerations: it is a rukn because its omission invalidates the essence, yet additional because the Lawgiver may relax it.
This is a unique Hanafi conceptual tool to reconcile the status.
4
Trace the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on minimum recitation
Abu Hanifa holds that a short verse of two words suffices (Zahir al-Riwayah). Abu Yusuf and Muhammad require a long verse or three short ones equivalent. Identify the basis: custom ('urf) and precaution (ihtiyat) for the Sahibayn.
Note the reported retraction of Abu Hanifa regarding single words or letters.
5
Evaluate the tarjih and practical consequence
The author notes that the Sahibayn's view is preferred in al-Asrar for caution. Consider the thamarah al-khilaf: the stricter view requires longer recitation, while the original Hanafi position allows a minimal verse.
The mufta bihi may vary; many later fatwas adopt the precautionary view.

يوصف بالزيادة لأن التسمية إنما هي باعتبارين، فتسميته ركناً، باعتبار قيام ذلك الشيء به في حال، بحيث يستلزم فواتـه انتفاء الشيء، وزائداً، لأن الصلاة ماهية اعتبارية، فيجوز أن يعتبرها الشارع تارة بأركان وتارة بأقل منها، والمنافاة بينهما إنما هي باعتبار واحد، والزائد ما لا يخلفه بدل، أو الزائد هو: الجزء الذي إذا انتفى كان الحكم المركب باقياً بحسب اعتبار الشرع، وعلى هذا لو حلف لا يصلي فأحرم وقام وركع وسجد بلا قراءة حنث، [ و ] كانت القراءة فرضاً، فتصح بها الصلاة، (وَلَوْ) قرأ (آية) قصيرة مركبة من كلمتين فقط كقوله تعالى: ثُمَّ نَظَرَ [المدثر : ۲۱]، أو من كلمات كقوله تعالى: قُتِلَ كَيْفَ قَدَرَ [الار [الا: ١] أو حروف * الشورى : 1]، كهيعص ) يسمى عشق فر : ١] فقد اختلف المشايخ فيه، قال في شرح الطحاوي» و «جامع الإسبيجابي : يجوز ويكره، وقد صح رجوع أبي حنيفة رحمه الله عن إجزاء آية مثل الاسم، فلا يجوز مِنَ القُرْآنِ بِقَليل» ، وهذا أقرب إلى القواعد الشرعية، فإن المطلق فيها ينصرف إلى الأدنى على ما عرف قاله « الزيلعـــي»، ونظــر فيـه بعضهم بأن المطلق ينصرف إلى الكامل في الماهية. انتهى. وقال أبو يوسف ومحمد: الفرض قراءة آيـة طويلة، أو ثلاثة آيات قصار تعدل آية طويلة وهو رواية عن أبي حنيفة؛ لأن قارئ ما دون ذلك لا يعد قارئاً عرفاً، فشرطت الآية الطويلة أو ثلاث قصار تحصيلاً لوصف القراءة احتياطاً، وإنما حرم قراءة الآية القصيرة وما دون الطويلة على الجنب احتياطاً أيضاً لعين الحقيقة، ورجحه في « الأســرار»، والاحتياط أمر حسن في العبادات، وإذا قرأ نصف آية طويلة في ركعة والنصف الآخر في الأخرى فيـه اختلاف، وعامتهم على الجواز ، ولو قرأ نصف آية مرتين أو كلمة واحدة مراراً حتى بلغ قدر آيـة تـامـة فإنه لا يجوز، ومن لا يحسن إلا آية لا يلزمه التكرار في ركعة ، فيقرؤها في الركعة الثانيـة مـرة
And recitation. We will mention it, if Allah wills. And recitation is obligatory. Its reality is that one hears one's own utterance, as we mentioned in the discussion of the takbir. Recitation was fard due to His statement: 'So recite what is easy of the Quran' (73:20) and his statement, peace be upon him: 'Then recite what is easy of the Quran.' And consensus has been established on its obligation, mentioned by al-Zayla'i and others. The deduction from the verse is sound because what is meant by it is recitation of the Quran in its reality, and the context indicates that, which is His statement after it: 'And establish prayer.' This is an interpretation in its reality, and reality takes precedence over metaphor. So it is preferred over what some exegetes said that the meaning of the verse is prayer, due to the context of His statement: 'Indeed, your Lord knows that you stand [in prayer] less than two-thirds of the night' up to 'He knew that you would not be able to do it, so He turned to you,' meaning: He knew that you could not preserve the hours of the night, so He lifted from you the obligation of standing as estimated. So 'recite what is easy' means: pray what is easy for you of the night prayer. He expressed prayer by recitation because it is part of its pillars. The estimated night prayer was fard, then it was abrogated to the estimated, then it was abrogated entirely to the five prayers. End. Because it is an interpretation by metaphor, and the first is by reality. And it is supported by the hadith clarifying the obligations: 'Then recite what is easy.' And this is in reality sunnah. Consensus, and it suffices as support, for recitation is a rukn in prayer by consensus, and there is no disagreement about it from anyone who follows. And no attention is paid to the saying of Abu Bakr al-Asamm because it violates the consensus of the predecessors. Likewise the answer to the saying of Isma'il ibn 'Ulayya, al-Hasan ibn Salih, and Sufyan ibn 'Uyayna: recitation is not fard in prayer, but rather recommended, due to what was narrated from 'Umar ibn al-Khattab that he prayed Maghrib and did not recite, so it was said to him, and he said: 'How were the bowing and prostration?' They said: 'Good.' He said: 'Then there is no problem.' Narrated by al-Shafi'i and others. And from Zayd ibn Thabit: 'Recitation is sunnah.' Narrated by al-Bayhaqi. And there is disagreement about whether recitation is a rukn. Al-Ghaznawi, author of al-Hawi al-Qudsi, held that it is not a rukn, but the majority held that it is a rukn. However, they divided the rukn into essential: that which does not lapse except for necessity, and additional: that which lapses in some forms without actual necessity. And they made recitation of this category, for it lapses from the follower by following according to us, and from the one who catches the bowing by consensus. And it is not said: How can it be an additional rukn when it is internal to the essence and cannot be described as additional? Because the naming is based on two considerations. So it is called a rukn due to the thing's establishment in it in a state such that its omission necessitates the absence of the thing, and additional because the prayer is an conceptual essence, so the Lawgiver may consider it sometimes with pillars and sometimes with less. The contradiction between them is only from one aspect. And the additional is that which has no substitute. Or the additional is the part that, if missing, the compound ruling remains according to the consideration of the Law. Based on this, if someone swore not to pray, then he said the takbir, stood, bowed, and prostrated without recitation, he would break his oath. And recitation is fard, so prayer is valid with it. And if he recited a short verse consisting of only two words like His statement: 'Then he looked' (74:21), or of words like His statement: 'Cursed is he who estimated' (74:19), according to Abu Hanifa without disagreement among the scholars, as in al-Dirayah, and it is Zahir al-Riwayah, due to His statement: 'So recite what is easy of the Quran' without excess, except that less than a verse is excluded. And it includes the verse that is one letter, but the correct view is that it is not permissible with it. So we said: As for the verse of one word like His statement: 'Dark green' (55:64) or a word whose name is a letter like His statement: 'Sad' (38:1), or two letters like 'Ha Mim' (40:1), 'Ta Sin' (27:1), or letters like 'Kaf Ha Ya 'Ayn Sad' (19:1) which is called 'Ayn Sin Qaf' (??), the scholars have differed. It is said in Sharh al-Tahawi and Jami' al-Isbijani: permissible but disliked. And it has been established that Abu Hanifa retracted from deeming a verse like a name sufficient, so prayer is not valid with it according to the most correct view, because he is customarily not a reciter. And al-Quduri said: The correct from the school of Abu Hanifa is that whatever is included under the name of Quran is permissible, and it is the saying of Ibn 'Abbas, for he said: 'Recite what you have of the Quran, for nothing of the Quran is little.' And this is closer to the legal principles, for the absolute therein refers to the minimum as known, said by al-Zayla'i. And some objected to him that the absolute refers to the complete in essence. End. And Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: The fard is recitation of a long verse, or three short verses equivalent to a long verse, and it is a narration from Abu Hanifa, because the reciter of less than that is not customarily considered a reciter. So a long verse or three short ones are required to achieve the quality of recitation out of precaution. And recitation of a short verse and what is less than a long one is forbidden for the junub out of precaution also for the essence of reality. And it was preferred in al-Asrar, and precaution is good in acts of worship. And if he recited half a long verse in one rak'ah and the other half in another, there is disagreement, and the majority permit it. And if he recited half a verse twice or one word repeatedly until it reached the measure of a complete verse, it is not permissible. And one who knows only one verse is not required to repeat it in a rak'ah, but recites it in the second rak'ah once.
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah deals with the obligation of Quranic recitation (qira'ah) in prayer. The author first establishes that recitation is fard (obligatory) by citing the Quranic verse 'So recite what is easy of the Quran' (73:20) and a hadith where the Prophet instructs to 'recite what is easy.' He also invokes consensus (ijma'). He refutes the interpretations of some exegetes who claim the verse refers to prayer itself, arguing that the literal meaning (haqiqah) takes precedence over metaphorical interpretation (majaz). He dismisses the views of Abu Bakr al-Asamm and others who considered recitation merely recommended (mustahabb), citing the consensus of the Salaf. The passage then addresses whether recitation is a rukn (pillar) of prayer. While the majority consider it a rukn, they distinguish between essential (asli) and additional (za'id) pillars; recitation is considered an additional pillar because it drops in certain cases (e.g., for a follower or one who catches the bowing). This does not contradict its being a rukn, as the classification depends on consideration. The main focus is the minimum amount of recitation that suffices. According to Abu Hanifa, a short verse of two words (e.g., 'thumma nazara') is sufficient, and this is the position of Zahir al-Riwayah. However, he reportedly retracted regarding a verse of a single word or isolated letters, making such recitation invalid. The two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, require a long verse or three short verses equivalent to a long one, out of caution (ihtiyat) because a reciter of less is not customarily called a qari. This view is preferred in the work al-Asrar. The passage also touches on cases of reciting half a verse across two rak'ahs (permitted by majority) and repeating words to equal a verse (not permitted). For a person who knows only one verse, it is not required to repeat it in the same rak'ah; rather, he recites it in the second rak'ah.

Key Terms
القراءة (al-qira'ah): In prayer, the recitation of Quranic verses aloud or silently that is a fard component (rukn). Its reality is that one hears one's own utterance.
الركن الأصلي والزائد (al-rukn al-asli wa al-za'id): The essential pillar (asli) never drops; the additional pillar (za'id) may drop in some circumstances (e.g., recitation for follower). Both are necessary in normal circumstances.
الآية (al-ayah): A verse of the Quran. The minimum verse that suffices in prayer is a contentious issue: Abu Hanifa says two words; Sahibayn say a long verse or three short ones.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the most correct view in the Hanafi school (as presented in the passage), what is the status of a prayer in which a person recites only the single word 'ص' (Sad)?
A) Valid, because it is a Quranic letter
B) Invalid, because Abu Hanifa retracted from deeming such recitation sufficient
C) Valid, because the Sahibayn allow it
D) Invalid, because recitation is not fard

Key Takeaway
Recitation is a fard rukn in prayer; its minimum is a two-word verse per Abu Hanifa, but caution (ihtiyat) recommends a longer amount as preferred by the Sahibayn.

Defining the Extra Pillar (Rukn Za'id) and the Minimum Quranic Verse in Prayer
Explaining the concept of an extra pillar and applying it to basmalah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the Hanafi concept of rukn za'id, explain its application to basmalah, and state the relied-upon ruling on the minimum verse valid for prayer.

Core Idea
An extra pillar has no substitute; its omission does not invalidate the act, but its presence is wajib.

This passage from the sharh presents a core Hanafi legal concept: the extra pillar (rukn za'id). You will learn what distinguishes a rukn from a rukn za'id, why basmalah is classified as such, and how this concept interacts with the minimum recitation in prayer. The ruling on what constitutes a valid minimal verse involves an internal Hanafi dispute, which we will trace.

Guided Path
1
Define the extra pillar
The passage gives two definitions: that which has no substitute, or whose absence leaves the composite ruling intact. Understand both and how they differ from an integral pillar (rukn).
Note: An integral pillar's omission invalidates the act; an extra pillar's omission does not.
2
Apply the definition to basmalah
Basmalah is called a pillar because its existence is necessary for the completion of the act from one perspective, but it is extra because prayer can be defined without it and still be valid.
This dual perspective resolves the apparent contradiction.
3
Trace the implication for oaths
The passage uses an oath example: if someone swears not to pray and then prays without recitation, the oath is broken (recitation is fard) but the prayer is valid (recitation is not a rukn). This illustrates the practical effect of the extra pillar concept.
Recitation is fard (wajib) but not a rukn, so its omission requires compensation (sajdah as-sahw) but does not invalidate.
4
Identify the ruling on minimum verse
According to Abu Hanifa, any verse, even a short one of two words, suffices. The dispute is about verses consisting of a single word or letter.
Zahir al-Riwayah upholds the two-word minimum as sufficient.
5
Evaluate the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifa originally allowed a single-word/letter verse but later retracted; some mashayikh say it is permissible but disliked; al-Quduri affirms the original view. The mufta bihi is that it does not suffice.
The text says 'al-ashah' (most correct) that it is not permissible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو آية .. المدرك في الركوع بالإجماع، ولا يقال: كيف يكون ركناً زائداً وداخل الماهية لا يوصف بالزيادة لأن التسمية إنما هي باعتبارين، فتسميته ركناً، باعتبار قيام ذلك الشيء به في حال، بحيث يستلزم فواتـه انتفاء الشيء، وزائداً، لأن الصلاة ماهية اعتبارية، فيجوز أن يعتبرها الشارع تارة بأركان وتارة بأقل منها، والمنافاة بينهما إنما هي باعتبار واحد، والزائد ما لا يخلفه بدل، أو الزائد هو: الجزء الذي إذا انتفى كان الحكم المركب باقياً بحسب اعتبار الشرع، وعلى هذا لو حلف لا يصلي فأحرم وقام وركع وسجد بلا قراءة حنث، [ و ] كانت القراءة فرضاً، فتصح بها الصلاة، (وَلَوْ) قرأ (آية) قصيرة مركبة من كلمتين فقط كقوله تعالى: هُم نَظَرَ [الم : ۲۱]، أو من كلمات كقوله تعالى: قُتِلَ كَيْفَ قَدَرَ [الار : ١٩] على قول أبي حنيفة بلا خلاف بين المشايخ فيه، كما في ( الدراية» وهو « ظـاهـر الـروايـة» لقوله تعالى: اقر، وأما تسَرَ مِنَ الْقُرْءَانِ﴾ [الم : ٢٠] من غير فَضْل، إلا أنّ ما دون الآية خارج منه، وشمل الآيــة الـتـي على حرف، ولكن الأصح أنه لا يجوز بها فلذا قلنا: وأما الآية من كلمة كقوله تعالى: دَهَامَّتَانِ [الرحمن: ٦٤] أو كلمة مسماها حرف وهو قوله تعالى: وص [ : 1 ] [ القلة : ١]، أو حرفان حم [ ] طس [الا: ١] أو حروف * الشورى : 1]، كهيعص ) يسمى عشق فر : ١] فقد اختلف المشايخ فيه، قال في شرح الطحاوي» و «جامع الإسبيجابي : يجوز ويكره، وقد صح رجوع أبي حنيفة رحمه الله عن إجزاء آية مثل الاسم، فلا يجوز بها الصلاة على الأصح؛ لأنـه عاداً لا قارئاً، وقال القدوري: إنَّ الصحيح من مذهب أبي حنيفة أن ما يتناوله اسم القرآن يجوز، وهو قول ابن عباس فإنه قال: «اقْرَأْ مَا مَعَكَ مِنَ القُرْآنِ فَلَيْسَ شَيْءٌ مِنَ القُرْآنِ بِقَليل»
And even a verse... The (basmalah) is a pillar in bowing by consensus, and it is not said: How can it be an extra pillar when what is inside the essence is not described as extra? Because the naming is according to two perspectives: it is called a pillar because that thing exists in it in a state such that its omission necessitates the negation of the thing, and it is called extra because prayer is a legal construct (i.e., not a physical reality), so it is permissible for the Lawgiver to consider it sometimes with pillars and sometimes with less than that. The contradiction between these two is only from one perspective. The 'extra' is that which has no substitute, or it is the part whose absence leaves the composite ruling remaining according to legal consideration. Based on this, if someone swore not to pray, and then he said the opening takbir, stood, bowed, and prostrated without recitation, he would break his oath, because recitation was obligatory; but the prayer would be valid (since recitation is not a pillar). (And if) he recites a short verse composed of only two words, like His statement: 'thumma nathar' [Al-Muddaththir: 21], or of words like His statement: 'qutila kayfa qadara' [Al-Mursalat: 19], then according to Abu Hanifa there is no disagreement among the mashayikh, as in 'al-Diraya', and it is the Zahir al-Riwaya, because of His statement: 'Read' and 'So recite what is easy from the Quran' [Al-Muzzammil: 20] without specifying a length, except that less than a verse is excluded from it, and it includes the verse that is one letter, but the correct view is that it is not permissible with it, so we said: As for a verse that is one word, like His statement: 'mudhammatan' [Al-Rahman: 64], or a word whose name is a letter, like His statement: 'Sad' [Sad: 1], or two letters like 'Ha Mim' [Ghafir: 1] or 'Ta Sin' [Al-Naml: 1], or letters like 'Kaf Ha Ya 'Ayn Sad' [Maryam: 1], the mashayikh differed. It is said in 'Sharh al-Tahawi' and 'Jami' al-Isbijabi': it is permissible but disliked. And it has been authentically reported that Abu Hanifa retracted from the sufficiency of a verse like a name, so prayer is not permissible with it according to the most correct view, because he is habitually someone who utters a word, not a reader. Al-Quduri said: The correct view from Abu Hanifa's madhhab is that whatever the name 'Quran' applies to is permissible, and this is the saying of Ibn Abbas, for he said: 'Recite whatever you have of the Quran, for nothing of the Quran is little.'
Source pages p. 228

Commentary
This passage is a definition and ruling statement from the sharh. It first clarifies the legal concept of an 'extra pillar' (rukn za'id). In Hanafi usul, a pillar is integral to the essence of the act, but something can be called a 'pillar' because its existence is necessary for the act to be valid from one perspective, yet 'extra' because the act's essence could be defined without it. The example given: basmalah in prayer is a rukn (pillar) for the beginning, but it is 'extra' in the sense that prayer can be valid without it if one recites something else. The key definition: 'extra' means that which has no substitute, or whose absence still leaves the composite ruling intact legally. Then they apply this to the case of an oath: if one swears not to pray, but performs prayer without recitation, the oath is broken because recitation is fard (obligatory), but the prayer is valid because recitation is not a rukn (so the prayer is valid despite missing a wajib). Next, the passage discusses the minimum verse for recitation. According to Abu Hanifa, any verse, even a short one of two words, suffices. This is the Zahir al-Riwayah position. However, there is disagreement about verses consisting of a single word or single letter. Some mashayikh say it is permissible but disliked. It is reported that Abu Hanifa retracted his view and said such a verse does not suffice because it is not considered recitation by custom. Al-Quduri prefers the original view that whatever is called Quran suffices, citing Ibn Abbas. This shows the internal Hanafi development and the deference to later authorities.

Key Terms
ركن زائد (rukn za'id): A pillar whose omission does not invalidate the act because it has no substitute, e.g., basmalah in prayer
الزائد ما لا يخلفه بدل (al-za'id ma la yukhallifuhu badal): An extra element is that which has no substitute

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi definition, what is an 'extra pillar' (rukn za'id)?
A) A pillar that is recommended but not required
B) A pillar whose omission invalidates the act due to lack of substitute
C) A pillar whose omission does not invalidate the act because it has no substitute or its absence still leaves the ruling intact
D) A pillar that is only for the first rak'ah

Key Takeaway
An extra pillar is an element that is obligatory but not integral to the essence of an act; its omission does not invalidate the act, but compensation may be required.

The Minimum Recitation: A Hanafi Internal Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on minimum Quran recitation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on the minimum Quran recitation in prayer, identify the proof for each, and apply the mufta bihi view.

Core Idea
What counts as 'reciting the Quran'? Custom defines the minimum, not just any part of the text.

This passage delves into a critical debate within the Hanafi school: how much Quran must one recite for the wajib recitation in prayer to be fulfilled? The dispute revolves around the definition of 'qira'ah' (recitation) and whether it is measured by the literal text or by customary practice. Understanding this internal difference reveals how later Hanafi scholarship refined earlier positions through the concepts of 'urf and ihtiyat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three positions within the Hanafi school
List the three views: Abu Hanifa's original (any verse, even one word/letter), his retracted view (no single word/letter suffices), and the Sahibayn's view (one long verse or three short verses).
The retraction is a reported change of opinion, making it an intra-school development.
2
Examine the textual evidence for each
Abu Hanifa's original relies on the general command 'faqra'u ma tayassara' (recite what is easy). The Sahibayn and the retraction appeal to custom ('urf): one who recites a single word is not considered a reciter. Al-Quduri cites the absolute name 'Quran' and Ibn Abbas' statement.
The evidence is both Quranic and based on legal maxims about absolute and customary meanings.
3
Trace the development and tarjih
Later Hanafi scholars preferred the retraction and the Sahibayn view as a precaution (ihtiyat) in worship. The text declares that the most correct (al-ashah) is that a one-word/letter verse does not suffice.
Precaution is a strong principle in 'ibadat.
4
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if someone recites only 'mudhammatan' (one word) or 'Sad' (one letter), is the prayer valid? According to the mufta bihi, no; according to the original view, yes.
A mufti must know which view is operative for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
على قول أبي حنيفة بلا خلاف بين المشايخ فيه، كما في ( الدراية» وهو « ظـاهـر الـروايـة» لقوله تعالى: اقر، وأما تسَرَ مِنَ الْقُرْءَانِ﴾ [الم : ٢٠] من غير فَضْل، إلا أنّ ما دون الآية خارج منه، وشمل الآيــة الـتـي على حرف، ولكن الأصح أنه لا يجوز بها فلذا قلنا: وأما الآية من كلمة كقوله تعالى: دَهَامَّتَانِ [الرحمن: ٦٤] أو كلمة مسماها حرف وهو قوله تعالى: وص [ : 1 ] [ القلة : ١]، أو حرفان حم [ ] طس [الا: ١] أو حروف * الشورى : 1]، كهيعص ) يسمى عشق فر : ١] فقد اختلف المشايخ فيه، قال في شرح الطحاوي» و «جامع الإسبيجابي : يجوز ويكره، وقد صح رجوع أبي حنيفة رحمه الله عن إجزاء آية مثل الاسم، فلا يجوز بها الصلاة على الأصح؛ لأنـه عاداً لا قارئاً، وقال القدوري: إنَّ الصحيح من مذهب أبي حنيفة أن ما يتناوله اسم القرآن يجوز، وهو قول ابن عباس فإنه قال: «اقْرَأْ مَا مَعَكَ مِنَ القُرْآنِ فَلَيْسَ شَيْءٌ مِنَ القُرْآنِ بِقَليل» ، وهذا أقرب إلى القواعد الشرعية، فإن المطلق فيها ينصرف إلى الأدنى على ما عرف قاله « الزيلعـــي»، ونظــر فيـه بعضهم بأن المطلق ينصرف إلى الكامل في الماهية. انتهى. وقال أبو يوسف ومحمد: الفرض قراءة آيــة طويلة، أو ثلاثة آيات قصار تعدل آية طويلة وهو رواية عن أبي حنيفة؛ لأن قارئ ما دون ذلك لا يعد قارثاً عرفاً، فشرطت الآية الطويلة أو ثلاث قصار تحصيلاً لوصف القراءة احتياطاً، وإنما حرم قراءة الآية القصيرة وما دون الطويلة على الجنب احتياطاً أيضاً لعين الحقيقة، ورجحه في « الأســرار»، والاحتياط أمر حسن في العبادات، وإذا قرأ نصف آية طويلة في ركعة والنصف الآخر في الأخرى فيـه اختلاف، وعامتهم على الجواز ، ولو قرأ نصف آية مرتين أو كلمة واحدة مراراً حتى بلغ قدر آيـة تـامـة فإنه لا يجوز، ومن لا يحسن إلا آية لا يلزمه التكرار في ركعة ، فيقرؤها في الركعة الثانيـة مـرة
According to Abu Hanifa there is no disagreement among the mashayikh, as in 'al-Diraya', and it is the Zahir al-Riwayah, because of His statement: 'Read' and 'So recite what is easy from the Quran' [Al-Muzzammil: 20] without specifying a length, except that less than a verse is excluded from it, and it includes the verse that is one letter, but the correct view is that it is not permissible with it, so we said: As for a verse that is one word, like His statement: 'mudhammatan' [Al-Rahman: 64], or a word whose name is a letter, like His statement: 'Sad' [Sad: 1], or two letters like 'Ha Mim' [Ghafir: 1] or 'Ta Sin' [Al-Naml: 1], or letters like 'Kaf Ha Ya 'Ayn Sad' [Maryam: 1], the mashayikh differed. It is said in 'Sharh al-Tahawi' and 'Jami' al-Isbijabi': it is permissible but disliked. And it has been authentically reported that Abu Hanifa retracted from the sufficiency of a verse like a name, so prayer is not permissible with it according to the most correct view, because he is habitually someone who utters a word, not a reader. Al-Quduri said: The correct view from Abu Hanifa's madhhab is that whatever the name 'Quran' applies to is permissible, and this is the saying of Ibn Abbas, for he said: 'Recite whatever you have of the Quran, for nothing of the Quran is little.' And this is closer to the legal principles, because the absolute there is directed to the minimum as known, said by al-Zayla'i. And some criticized him saying the absolute is directed to the complete in essence. End. And Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: The fard is to recite one long verse or three short verses equivalent to a long verse, and this is a narration from Abu Hanifa, because one who recites less than that is not considered a reciter customarily. So they conditioned a long verse or three short ones to achieve the description of recitation as a precaution. And they only prohibited reciting a short verse or less than a long one for the junub also as a precaution for the reality. And it is preferred in 'al-Asrar'. And precaution is good in acts of worship. And if one recites half a long verse in one rak'ah and the other half in another, there is disagreement, and the majority are on permissibility. And if one recites half a verse twice or one word repeatedly until it reaches the length of a full verse, it is not permissible. And one who only knows one verse is not required to repeat it in the same rak'ah; he recites it in the second rak'ah once.
Source pages p. 228

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute (ikhtilaf) on the minimum amount of Quran recitation required in prayer. Abu Hanifa's initial position (Zahir al-Riwayah) is that any verse, even a single word or letter, suffices, based on the general command 'faqra'u ma tayassara' (recite what is easy). However, later authorities report that he retracted that view, and the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that such minimal recitation does not suffice because it is not customarily considered 'recitation'. Al-Quduri insists the original view is correct and cites Ibn Abbas. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) take a more stringent view: the fard is one long verse or three short verses equivalent to a long verse, to ensure the quality of recitation. They apply this precaution to both prayer and the prohibition for a junub. The passage then discusses related cases: reciting half a verse across two rak'ahs (majority allow if intended as a continuation), repeating half a verse or a word to accumulate length (not permissible), and the duty of one who knows only one verse (no repetition in the same rak'ah, but recites it in the second rak'ah once). This shows the range of opinions and the internal Hanafi development.

Key Terms
آية قصيرة (aya qasira): A verse composed of at least two words, e.g., 'thumma nathar'
آية على حرف (aya ala harf): A verse consisting of a single letter, like 'ص' (Sad)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the most correct (al-ashah) Hanafi position, which of the following is the minimum acceptable recitation in prayer?
A) Any single letter, e.g., 'ص'
B) Any single word, e.g., 'مُدْهَامَّتَانِ'
C) A short verse of at least two words
D) One long verse or three short verses

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires a meaningful amount of Quran recitation in prayer, defined by custom, not just any part of the text.

Recitation in the First Two Rak'ahs vs. Last Two
Establishing that recitation is fard in two rak'ahs, with evidence and discussion of disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on recitation in fard prayer and identify the evidence and dispute regarding the number and specification of rak'ahs.

Core Idea
Recitation is fard in two rak'ahs of fard prayer; omitting it in one rak'ah invalidates the prayer.

In this lesson, we examine the obligation of recitation (qira'ah) during fard prayer. The Hanafi school holds that recitation is fard in two rak'ahs, not in every rak'ah. We will explore the evidence from hadith and the reasoning that specifies the first two rak'ahs as the default, while addressing the objections and alternative views.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what exactly is being ruled upon (recitation in fard prayer) and the hukm level (fard). Note that the ruling specifically says 'in two rak'ahs'.
The prayer becomes invalid if recitation is missed in more than one rak'ah.
2
Locate the evidence
Find the dalil: the hadith from Ali (RA) 'Recitation in the first two is recitation in the last two', and the athar from Ali and Ibn Mas'ud. Also note the qiyas between the first two rak'ahs.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut).
3
Understand the Hanafi reasoning
The first two rak'ahs are similar in all essential aspects; therefore if recitation is required in one, it is required in the other by qiyas. The last two rak'ahs differ (can be dropped in travel, different recitation), so they are not analogous.
Objections about differences in takbir and supplications are dismissed as non-essential.
4
Note the disputes
Zufar and Hasan al-Basri argue that one rak'ah suffices. Also intra-Hanafi: can the two rak'ahs be any two, or must they be the first two? The text leans to the first two being the best and the relied-upon practice.
The author reconciles by saying 'choice does not negate obligation'.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The operative ruling is that recitation is fard in two rak'ahs, and it is obligatory in the first two (though technically any two could fulfill the fard, the first two are specified by sunnah and athar).
Missing recitation in one of the first two invalidates the prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا علمت ذلك فالقراءة فرض (في ركعتي الفَرْضِ)، أي: في ركعتــيـن مــن الـفـرض غـيـر متعنتين، فإذا قرأ في ركعة فقط لا تصح الصلاة. وقال زفر والحسن البصري: تصح لأن الأمر لا يقتضي التكرار، قلنا: نعم، لكن إنما لزمت في الثانية أيضاً استدلالاً بالأولى لأنهما يتشاكلان من كل وجه، وأما الأخريان فيفارقانها في حق السقوط بالسفر وصفة القراءة وقدرها، فلا يلحقـان بـهـا، وفيه أثر علي وابن مسعود أنهما قالا : « اقْرَأ في الأوليين وسبِّح في الأخريين ) وكفى بهما قدوة. قاله الزيلعي، وفي ( البدرية : القراءة فرض في أحدهما بعبارة النص، وفي الثانية بدلالة النص، لأن الثانية مثل الأولى وجوباً وسقوطاً وجهراً و إخفاء. قال في ( الكافي»: لا يقال: اركعــوا واسجدوا أمر أيضاً، ومع هذا يكرر في كل ركعة؛ لأنه عليه الصلاة والسلام بينـــه فـي كـل الـركـعــات، وقال في القراءة: « القِرَاءةُ في الأوليين قراءة في الأخريين ) () رواه علي. وقال في شرح « الطحاوي » : قال أصحابنا القراءة في الركعتين فرض بغير عينهما إن شاء قرأ في الأوليين، وإن شاء قرأ في الأخريين، وإن شاء في الأولى والرابعة، وإن شاء في الثالثة والرابعة، وأفضلها في الأوليين، والظاهر أن الفرق بين اختيار القدوري والطحاوي يظهر في القضاء وسجود السهو تأمل كذا في «مجمع الروايات». قلت: وقد يقال: إن التخيير لا ينفي الوجوب، وإنما ذكر لبيان الصحة وأفضلية القراءة في الأوليين لا ينفي كون الفعل فيهما واجباً، فلا خلاف، انتهى. وقال في « الفوائــد » : فإن قيل: الركعة الأولى مع الثانية افترقا في تكبيرة الافتتاح والتعوذ والثناء، قلنا: المشابهة والمشاكلة في الكمية والكيفية فيما يرجع إلى نفس الصلاة وأركانها ، أما التكبيرة فشرط وهـو زائد، والتعوذ والثناء أيضاً زائدان ليسا من أركان الصلاة، فالافتراق فيهما لا يقدح في ثبوت المشاكلة. انتهى. وكذا استدل في « الاختيار » و « المستصفى»؛ لقوله : ( القراءة في الأوليين قـراءة في الأخريين ) (۳) أي: تنوب عنهما كقولهم لسان الوزير لسان الأمير.
And when you know that, recitation is fard (obligatory) in the two rak'ahs of fard, meaning in two rak'ahs of the fard prayer not specified. So if one recites in only one rak'ah, the prayer is not valid. Zufar and Hasan al-Basri said: It is valid because the command does not necessitate repetition. We reply: Yes, but it is required in the second rak'ah by inference from the first because they are similar in every respect. As for the last two rak'ahs, they differ from the first two regarding dropping (in travel) and the nature and amount of recitation, so they are not analogous to them. There is an athar from Ali and Ibn Mas'ud that they said: 'Recite in the first two and glorify in the last two.' They suffice as examples. Al-Zayla'i said this. And in 'al-Badriyya': Recitation is fard in one rak'ah by explicit text, and in the second by implication of the text, because the second is like the first in obligation, omission, loudness, and quietness. He said in 'al-Kafi': It is not said: The command to bow and prostrate is also a command, yet they are repeated in every rak'ah, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) explained it in all rak'ahs. He said concerning recitation: 'Recitation in the first two is recitation in the last two' related by Ali. And in 'Sharh al-Tahawi': Our companions said: Recitation in two rak'ahs is fard without specifying which two; if he wishes, he recites in the first two, or if he wishes, in the last two, or if he wishes, in the first and fourth, or if he wishes, in the third and fourth. The best is in the first two. Evidently, the difference between the choice of al-Quduri and al-Tahawi appears in qada' and sahw prostrations; ponder, as in 'Majma' al-Riwayat'. I say: It could be said that the choice does not negate obligation, but it is mentioned to show validity, and the superiority of reciting in the first two does not negate that the action in them is obligatory, so there is no disagreement. End. And in 'al-Fawa'id': If it is said: The first rak'ah differs from the second in the opening takbir, ta'awwudh, and thana', we say: The similarity is in quantity and quality regarding the prayer itself and its pillars. As for the takbir, it is a condition and extra, and the ta'awwudh and thana' are also extra and not from the pillars of prayer, so the difference in them does not detract from the similarity. End. And similarly, it is argued in 'al-Ikhtiyar' and 'al-Mustasfa' due to his saying: 'Recitation in the first two is recitation in the last two', meaning they stand for each other, like the saying 'the tongue of the minister is the tongue of the prince.'
Source pages p. 229

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding where recitation is obligatory in fard prayer. The author establishes that recitation is fard in two rak'ahs, without specifying which two, but by evidence from practice and hadith it is most virtuous and obligatory in the first two. Zufar and Hasan al-Basri argued that recitation in only one rak'ah suffices, but the Hanafi response uses qiyas: the first and second rak'ah are similar in essence, so if recitation is required in one, it is required in the other by analogy. However, the last two rak'ahs are different because they can be omitted during travel, and the recitation is different (subhana instead). Thus, the obligation is specifically in two rak'ahs, and the first two are designated by sunnah and athar of the Companions. The passage also refutes an objection about differences in takbir and supplications, clarifying that those are conditions or extras, not affecting the similarity of the pillars. Finally, it notes a difference of opinion whether the two rak'ah can be any two, but the preferred view is that they are the first two. The hadith 'recitation in the first two is recitation in the last two' is interpreted as meaning they stand in place of each other, but not that the last two have the same ruling. The core ruling: recitation in only one rak'ah invalidates prayer, and the first two are specified by custom and evidence.

Key Terms
فرض في ركعتي الفرض (fard fi rak'atay al-fard): Recitation is obligatory in two rak'ahs of the fard prayer, not necessarily the first two but by preference the first two

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, what happens if a person prays two rak'ahs of fajr and recites only in the first rak'ah?
A) The prayer is valid because recitation in one rak'ah is enough
B) The prayer is invalid because recitation is required in two rak'ahs
C) The prayer is valid but requires sajdah sahw
D) The prayer is valid only if he intended to recite in the second

Key Takeaway
Recitation is fard in two rak'ahs of fard prayer, and the first two are the default; omitting recitation in one of them invalidates the prayer.
