Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Recitation in the First Two Rak'ats of Fard Prayer is Obligatory
Expands the ruling on recitation in fard prayer with proofs and intra-school differences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on recitation in fard prayer, explain the proof from Quran and Hadith, and evaluate the counter-argument of Zufr and Hasan al-Basri.

Core Idea
Recitation is fard in two rak'ats of fard prayer; missing it invalidates the prayer.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi position on recitation during the obligatory prayer. While it is clear that recitation is required, the number of rak'ats and the specific evidence have been subjects of scholarly discussion. The text from Imdad al-Fattah Sharh Nur al-Idah clarifies the ruling, the proof, and the response to opposing views.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled on? It is recitation (qira'ah) in the fard prayer. The Hanafi ruling: it is fard (obligatory) in two rak'ats of the fard prayer.
The text specifies 'في ركعتي الفرض' — in two rak'ats of fard.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary evidence is the Quranic verse 'فَاقْرَءُوا مَا تَيَسَّرَ مِنَ الْقُرْآنِ' (So recite what is easy from the Quran). The Prophet's practice and statements also provide specification.
The hadith 'اقرأ في الأوليين وسبح في الأخريين' (Recite in the first two and glorify in the last two) from Ali and Ibn Mas'ud is cited.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'اقْرَءُوا' indicates obligation (wujub) according to Hanafi usul. The generality of 'مَا تَيَسَّرَ' includes any amount, but the Prophet's practice specifies that recitation should be in two rak'ats.
The Quranic proof is qat'i al-thubut but zanni al-dalala, so the ruling is considered a practical fard (fard amali).
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Zufr and Hasan al-Basri hold that recitation in one rak'ah suffices. Their argument: the command to recite does not necessitate repetition.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf? Actually, Zufr was a Hanafi, but his view differs. Also, Sahibayn differ on details of repeating verses.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response: although the command itself does not require repetition, the first two rak'ats are identical in all aspects related to prayer (obligation, dropping, jahr/ikhfa). Therefore, recitation becomes obligatory in both by qiyas on the similarity. The last two differ, so they are not included.
This argument is based on the principle of similarity (al-mushakalah).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في ركعتي الفرض، . أيضاً عند أبي حنيفة، قالوا: وعندهما يلزمه التكرار ثلاث مرات أي في كل ركعة، ومن يحسن ثلاث آيات إذا كرر واحدة ثلاثاً لا يتأدى به الفرض عندهما، كما في « المجتبى»، وفي « الخلاصة » : فيه اختلاف المشايخ على قولهما. وحفظ ما تجوز به الصلاة فرض عين ! لقوله تعالى: ﴿فَاقْرَءُوا مَا تَيَسَّرَ مِنَ الْقُرْءَانِ) [الملك: ٢٠]. وحفظ جميع القرآن فرض كفاية، وحفظ فاتحة الكتاب وسورة واجب على كل مسلم، وإذا علمت ذلك فالقراءة فرض (في ركعتي الفَرْضِ)، أي: في ركعتــيـن مــن الـفـرض غـيـر متعنتين، فإذا قرأ في ركعة فقط لا تصح الصلاة. وقال زفر والحسن البصري: تصح لأن الأمر لا يقتضي التكرار، قلنا: نعم، لكن إنما لزمت في الثانية أيضاً استدلالاً بالأولى لأنهما يتشاكلان من كل وجه، وأما الأخريان فيفارقانها في حق السقوط بالسفر وصفة القراءة وقدرها، فلا يلحقـان بـهـا، وفيه أثر علي وابن مسعود أنهما قالا : « اقْرَأ في الأوليين وسبِّح في الأخريين ) وكفى بهما قدوة. قاله الزيلعي، وفي ( البدرية : القراءة فرض في أحدهما بعبارة النص، وفي الثانية بدلالة النص، لأن الثانية مثل الأولى وجوباً وسقوطاً وجهراً و إخفاء. قال في ( الكافي»: لا يقال: اركعــوا واسجدوا أمر أيضاً، ومع هذا يكرر في كل ركعة؛ لأنه عليه الصلاة والسلام بينـــه فـي كـل الـركـعــات، وقال في القراءة: « القِرَاءةُ في الأوليين قراءة في الأخريين ) () رواه علي. وقال في شرح « الطحاوي » : قال أصحابنا القراءة في الركعتين فرض بغير عينهما إن شاء قرأ في الأوليين، وإن شاء قرأ في الأخريين، وإن شاء في الأولى والرابعة، وإن شاء في الثالثة والرابعة، وأفضلها في الأوليين، والظاهر أن الفرق بين اختيار القدوري والطحاوي يظهر في القضاء وسجود السهو تأمل كذا في «مجمع الروايات». قلت: وقد يقال: إن التخيير لا ينفي الوجوب، وإنما ذكر لبيان الصحة وأفضلية القراءة في الأوليين لا ينفي كون الفعل فيهما واجباً، فلا خلاف، انتهى. وقال في « الفوائــد » : فإن قيل: الركعة الأولى مع الثانية افترقا في تكبيرة الافتتاح والتعوذ والثناء، قلنا: المشابهة والمشاكلة في الكمية والكيفية فيما يرجع إلى نفس الصلاة وأركانها ، أما التكبيرة فشرط وهـو زائد، والتعوذ والثناء أيضاً زائدان ليسا من أركان الصلاة، فالافتراق فيهما لا يقدح في ثبوت المشاكلة. انتهى. وكذا استدل في « الاختيار » و « المستصفى»؛ لقوله : ( القراءة في الأوليين قـراءة في الأخريين ) (۳) أي: تنوب عنهما كقولهم لسان الوزير لسان الأمير.
(1) أخرجه ابن أبي شيبة في مصنفه (٤٠٨/١).
(۲) أخرجه عبد الرزاق في مصنفه (١٢٦/٢).
(۳) تقدم تخريجه بالحديث السابق.
تنبيه: قال في « البحر » : القراءة فرض عملي في ركعتي الفرض كما في «السراج» للاختلاف بين العلماء فيه انتهى. قلت: هذا ظاهر بالنظر للركعتين جميعاً، وإلا فقدمنا قول الزيلعي: انعقـد الإجماع على فرضيتهما وسند الإجماع قوله تعالى: ﴿فَاقْرَهُوا مَا تَيَسَّرَ [الم : ٢٠]، وقوله : « اقرأ ما تيسر معك من القرآن ) ولم يعتد بخلاف الأصم
Regarding the two rak'ats of the fard (obligatory prayer). Also according to Abu Hanifa, they said: According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), he is obliged to repeat three times, i.e., in each rak'ah. And one who knows three verses — if he repeats one three times, the obligation is not fulfilled according to them, as in al-Mujtaba. And in al-Khulasa: There is a difference of the scholars on their statement. Memorizing what makes prayer valid is fard ayn due to His saying: 'So recite what is easy from the Quran' (al-Mulk: 20). Memorizing the entire Quran is fard kifayah. Memorizing the Fatiha and a surah is wajib upon every Muslim. When you know that, recitation is fard in the two rak'ats of fard, i.e., in two rak'ats of the fard, not specific. So if he recites in only one rak'ah, the prayer is not valid. Zufr and al-Hasan al-Basri said: It is valid because the command does not necessitate repetition. We said: Yes, but it becomes binding in the second also by inference from the first because they resemble each other from every aspect. As for the last two, they differ from them regarding dropping due to travel, the nature and amount of recitation, so they are not analogous. There is an athar from Ali and Ibn Mas'ud that they said: 'Recite in the first two and glorify in the last two,' and they suffice as examples. Al-Zayla'i said it. And in al-Badriyya: Recitation is fard in one of them by explicit text, and in the second by implication of the text, because the second is like the first in obligation, dropping, loudness and softness. He said in al-Kafi: It cannot be said that 'bow' and 'prostrate' are also commands, and yet they are repeated in every rak'ah; because the Prophet (peace be upon him) explained it in all rak'ats. And he said regarding recitation: 'Recitation in the first two is recitation in the last two' narrated by Ali. And in Sharh al-Tahawi: Our companions said: Recitation in the two rak'ats is fard without specifying them; if he wishes he recites in the first two, if he wishes in the last two, if he wishes in the first and fourth, if he wishes in the third and fourth, and the best is in the first two. It appears that the difference between the choice of al-Quduri and al-Tahawi appears in the make-up (qada) and prostration of forgetfulness; reflect, as in Majma' al-Riwayat. I said: It could be said that the option does not negate obligation; rather it is mentioned to clarify validity and the superiority of recitation in the first two does not negate that the act in them is obligatory, so no difference, end. And he said in al-Fawa'id: If it is said: The first rak'ah and the second differ in the opening takbir, ta'awwudh, and thana', we say: The similarity and likeness are in the quantity and quality regarding what pertains to the prayer itself and its pillars. As for the takbir, it is a condition and additional; the ta'awwudh and thana' are also additional and not among the pillars; so the difference in them does not harm the establishment of similarity. End. And similarly it is argued in al-Ikhtiyar and al-Mustasfa due to his saying: 'Recitation in the first two is recitation in the last two,' i.e., it stands for them like their saying: The tongue of the vizier is the tongue of the emir.
(1) Ibn Abi Shayba narrated it in his Musannaf (1/408).
(2) Abd al-Razzaq narrated it in his Musannaf (2/126).
(3) Its source has preceded with the previous hadith.
Warning: He said in al-Bahr: Recitation is a practical fard in the two rak'ats of fard as in al-Siraj due to the difference among scholars, end. I said: This is apparent considering the two rak'ats together; otherwise we have presented al-Zayla'i's statement: Consensus was reached on their fardiyya, and the basis of the consensus is the saying of Allah: 'So recite what is easy' (al-Muzzammil: 20) and his saying: 'Recite what is easy for you of the Quran' and he disregarded the difference of al-Asamm.
Source pages p. 229

Commentary
This passage is a detailed expansion of the ruling that recitation in the two rak'ats of fard prayer is obligatory (fard). The author first addresses an intra-Hanafi issue: according to Abu Hanifa, if a person only knows three verses, he must repeat them in each rak'ah, while according to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), repeating one verse three times does not fulfill the obligation. The text then clarifies that memorizing what is needed for prayer is a personal obligation (fard 'ayn), memorizing the entire Quran is a communal obligation (fard kifayah), and memorizing Surah al-Fatiha and another surah is wajib. The main ruling states that recitation is fard in two rak'ats of fard, not specifying which two, but they must be two rak'ats; if one recites in only one rak'ah, the prayer is invalid. Zufr and Hasan al-Basri disagreed, holding that recitation in one suffices since the command does not require repetition. The Hanafi response acknowledges that the command itself does not require repetition, but the resemblance between the first two rak'ats necessitates it in both. The last two rak'ats are different because they can be dropped in travel and have different recitation norms. Evidence from the Companions Ali and Ibn Mas'ud is cited, instructing recitation in the first two and glorification in the last two. The text then mentions various scholarly views: some say recitation is fard in one by explicit text and in the second by implication; others say the two rak'ats are unspecified and one may choose which two to recite in, with the best being the first two. There is a discussion about apparent differences between al-Quduri and al-Tahawi regarding the effect on make-up prayers and prostration of forgetfulness, but the author resolves that the option does not negate obligation. Another objection that the first and second rak'ats differ in takbir, ta'awwudh, and thana' is refuted by stating that these are external conditions or supererogatory acts, not pillars, so they do not undermine the essential similarity. The passage concludes with a quote from al-Bahr stating that the fardiyya is practical due to scholarly disagreement, and that consensus is established on its being fard based on the Quran and hadith, ignoring the isolated view of al-Asamm.

Key Terms
فرض عين (fard 'ayn): An obligation that every individual must perform personally.
فرض كفاية (fard kifayah): An obligation that is fulfilled if some members of the community perform it; otherwise all are sinful.
ركعتي الفرض (rak'atay al-fard): The two rak'ats of the obligatory prayer in which recitation is required; specifically the first two rak'ats of a four-rak'ah fard.
فرض عملي (fard amali): A ruling that is considered practically obligatory due to overwhelming evidence, but theoretically open to interpretation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, recitation in how many rak'ats of the fard prayer is fard?
A) In every rak'ah
B) In two rak'ats, specifically the first two
C) In one rak'ah only
D) In the last two rak'ats

Key Takeaway
Recitation in two rak'ats of fard prayer is fard, supported by Quran and Hadith, and omission invalidates the prayer.

Salah — Prayer

Recitation in Nafl and Witr: Obligation and No Specific Surah
States rulings on recitation in nafl and witr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that recitation is fard in every rak'ah of nafl and witr, and explain that no specific surah is required for the prayer's validity in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Recitation is fard in every rak'ah of nafl and witr; any part of the Quran suffices.

This passage from Nur al-Idah establishes that recitation in supererogatory (nafl) and witr prayers is obligatory in every rak'ah, and that no specific surah is designated. This ruling is rooted in the general evidence of the Quran and Sunnah, and contrasts with the Shafi'i requirement of al-Fatiha.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and their ruling
Recognize that the passage addresses recitation in nafl (supererogatory) and witr prayers. The ruling is that recitation is fard (obligatory) in every rak'ah.
The text explicitly states: 'القراءة فرض في كل ركعات النفل والوثر'.
2
Understand the reasoning for nafl
Each pair (shaf') of nafl is considered an independent prayer; the second rak'ah is like the first, and standing for the third is like initiating a new prayer. Hence, recitation is fard in every rak'ah.
The analogy with the initiating takbir helps clarify.
3
Understand the reasoning for witr
Even though the evidence for witr being fard is from ahad hadith (less than mutawatir), the Hanafi school rules with precaution (ihtiyat) and thus considers recitation fard in every rak'ah.
Leaving recitation in any rak'ah of nafl or witr invalidates the prayer.
4
Note the ruling on required surah
No specific surah is required for the validity of the prayer; any amount of Quranic recitation suffices. This is based on the generality of texts like 'faqra'u ma tayassara' (recite what is easy).
This contrasts with Imam al-Shafi'i, who requires al-Fatiha as a pillar.
5
Examine the cross-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i school holds that al-Fatiha is a pillar (rukn) in every rak'ah, and omitting it invalidates the prayer. The Hanafi school does not require a specific surah.
The thamarah al-khilaf is practical: Hanafi allows any recitation; Shafi'i requires al-Fatiha.

وَ) القراءة فرض في (كُلِّ) ركعات (النَّفْلِ) لأن كل شفع منه صلاة على حدة وقد علمت افتراضها في الركعة الثانية كالأولى والقيام إلى الثالثة كتحريمة مبتدأة، ولهذا لا يجب بالتحريمة الأولى إلا شفع في المشهور كما سنذكره.(و) القراءة فرض في كل ركعات ( الوثر) أما على القول بسنيته فظاهر، وأما على القول بوجوبه أو فرضيته، فللاحتياط، ويقرأ في جميعه؛ لأن دليل الفرضية لما كان قاصراً لأنه من أخبار الآحاد ظهر أثر المقصود فيما هو من باب الاحتياط، وترك القراءة في ركعة من السنن يفسدها، فقلنا بالفساد هـا هنا احتياطاً ومراعاة لقصور الدليل، ولم يتعيَّن شيء من القرآنِ  ِلصِحَّةِ الصَّلاةِ) لإطلاق مـا تـلونـا وما روينا، وأشرنا إلى قول الإمام الشافعي رحمه الله بتعيين الفاتحة لجواز الصلاة، وقلنـا بتعينـها وجوباً لذلك الدليل، وسنذكره" في الواجبات إن شاء الله تعالى (ولا يقرأُ المؤتم، بلْ يَسْتَمِعُ) في حال جهر الإمام ( ويُنصِتُ) حال إسراره لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِذَا قُرِئَ الْقُرْهَانُ فَاسْتَمِعُوا لَهُ وَأَنصِتُوا [ الأقران : ٢٠٤] قال أبو هريرة له : ( كَانُوا يقرؤون خلف الإمام فنزلت ) وقال الإمام أحمد: أجمع الناس على أن هذه الآية في الصلاة وفي حديث أبي هريرة وأبي موسى: ( وإذا قرأ فأنصتوا ) قال مسلم: هذا الحديث صحيح. وعن عبادة بن الصامت أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام قال: « لا يقرأن أحد منكم شيئاً من القرآن إذا جهرتُ بالقرآن» (۱) قال الدارقطني : رجاله كلهم ثقات، ولا نقول بمفهوم المخالفة إذ ليس حجة عندنا، فلا يقرأ في السرية. وقال الإمام أحمد: ما سمعنا أحداً من أهل العلم يقول: إن الإمام إذا جهر بالقراءة لا تجزئ صلاة من لم يقرأ. وفي مسلم عن عطاء بن يسار أنه سأل زيد بن ثابت عن القراءة يعني: خلف الإمام فقال: « لا قراءة مع الإمام في شيء » .

And) recitation is fard in all rak'ats of nafl because every two rak'ats (shaf') is a separate prayer, and you have known its obligation in the second rak'ah like the first, and standing for the third is like an initiating takbir. Therefore, only a pair is obligatory by the first takbir according to the well-known view, as we will mention. (And) recitation is fard in all rak'ats of witr; as for the view that it is sunnah, it is obvious; as for the view that it is wajib or fard, it is for precaution. He recites in all of it because since the evidence for fardiyya is deficient being from ahad hadith, the effect of the intended appears in what is precautionary. Leaving recitation in one rak'ah of the sunan invalidates it, so we say invalidity here precautionarily and respecting the deficiency of the evidence. And no specific part of the Quran is designated for the validity of prayer due to the generality of what we recited and narrated. We have pointed to the statement of Imam al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him) specifying al-Fatiha for the validity of prayer, and we say its designation is wajib due to that evidence, and we will mention it in the obligations, Allah willing. (And) the follower does not recite, rather he listens in the case of the imam reciting loudly and is silent in the case of his silent recitation due to His saying: 'And when the Quran is recited, listen to it and be silent' (al-A'raf: 204). Abu Hurayra said to him: They used to recite behind the imam, so this verse was revealed. And Imam Ahmad said: The people have agreed that this verse pertains to prayer. And in the hadith of Abu Hurayra and Abu Musa: 'When he recites, be silent.' Muslim said: This hadith is authentic. From Ubadah ibn al-Samit that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Let none of you recite anything from the Quran when I recite loudly.' Al-Daraqutni said: All its narrators are trustworthy. And we do not adhere to the converse implication (mafhum al-mukhalafa) as it is not a proof with us, so he does not recite in silent prayers. And Imam Ahmad said: We have not heard any scholar say that when the imam recites loudly, the prayer of one who does not recite is invalid. And in Muslim from Ata ibn Yasar that he asked Zayd ibn Thabit about recitation behind the imam, and he said: 'No recitation with the imam in anything.'
(1) Its source preceded on p. 226.
(2) p. 405.
(3) p. 257.
(4) Mentioned by al-Tabari in his Tafsir (9/163) and al-Qurtubi in his Tafsir (1/121).
(0) Muslim narrated in al-Salat, chapter: Tashahhud in prayer (404), and Ibn Majah in Iqamat al-Salat, chapter: When the imam recites, be silent (846-847).
(6) Al-Daraqutni narrated in his Sunan (1/319).
(7) Muslim narrated in al-Masajid wa Mawadi' al-Salat, chapter: Sujud al-Tilawa (577).
Source pages p. 230

Commentary
This passage covers three related rulings for prayer. First, recitation in nafl (supererogatory) prayers: it is fard in every rak'ah because each pair (shaf') of nafl is considered an independent prayer. The second rak'ah in a pair is analogous to the first, and beginning the third rak'ah is like a new prayer. Second, recitation in witr prayer: it is fard in every rak'ah. Even though the evidence for witr being fard is from ahad hadith (less than mutawatir), we rule with precaution, so leaving recitation in any rak'ah invalidates the prayer. Third, no specific surah, such as al-Fatiha alone, is required for the validity of the prayer in the Hanafi school; any amount of Quran is sufficient. This is based on the general command 'recite what is easy'. The text explicitly contrasts with Imam al-Shafi'i who requires al-Fatiha as a pillar. Finally, the follower (mu'tam) does not recite when praying behind an imam. Instead, he listens when the imam recites aloud and is silent when the imam recites silently. This is proven by the Quranic verse 'and when the Quran is recited, listen to it and be silent' and several hadith. The text notes that the Hanafi school does not accept the converse implication (mafhum al-mukhalafa) from these texts, meaning the ruling applies to both loud and silent prayers for the follower: he never recites behind the imam. Statements from early scholars like Ahmad (though not Hanafi) and Zayd ibn Thabit are cited in support. The footnotes provide hadith references for these proofs.

Key Terms
النفل (al-nafl): Supererogatory prayer, including both regular sunnah and additional voluntary prayers.
الوثر (al-witr): The odd-numbered prayer performed after Isha, typically three rak'ats.
الفاتحة (al-Fatiha): The opening chapter of the Quran, consisting of seven verses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on recitation in witr prayer?
A) Recitation is sunnah in the first two rak'ahs only
B) Recitation is fard in every rak'ah
C) Recitation is wajib only in the first rak'ah
D) Recitation is not required if one recites in the first rak'ah

Key Takeaway
Recitation is fard in every rak'ah of nafl and witr, and no specific surah is required; any Quranic recitation suffices for the prayer's validity.

The Follower's Silence Behind the Imam
States ruling on follower's silence behind imam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that the follower does not recite behind the imam in either loud or silent prayers, and cite the primary evidence.

Core Idea
The follower must be silent and listen, never reciting behind the imam.

This passage establishes one of the distinctive Hanafi positions: the follower (mu'tam) does not recite any Quran when praying behind an imam. The ruling is based on clear Quranic command and authentic hadith, and applies to both loud and silent prayers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is praying behind an imam as a follower. The ruling is that the follower does not recite any Quran; he listens when the imam recites aloud and is silent when the imam recites silently.
The text explicitly says: 'ولا يقرأ المؤتم، بل يستمع وينصت'.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The primary evidence is the Quranic verse (al-A'raf 7:204): 'When the Quran is recited, listen to it and be silent.' This verse is understood to apply to the prayer context.
The text cites Abu Hurayra that the verse was revealed concerning recitation behind the imam.
3
Examine the supporting hadith
The passage quotes several hadith: 'When he recites, be silent' and 'No recitation with the imam in anything.' These hadith reinforce the ruling.
The text notes that these hadith are authentic (sahih) according to Muslim and al-Daraqutni.
4
Understand the Hanafi response to the opposing view
The Shafi'i school argues that the follower must recite al-Fatiha behind the imam, based on the general hadith 'no prayer for one who does not recite al-Fatiha'. The Hanafi response is that specific texts (Quran 7:204 and the hadith) restrict the general command, and the follower is exempt from recitation.
The text also notes that the Hanafi school does not accept the converse implication (mafhum al-mukhalafa) from these texts, so the ruling applies to both loud and silent prayers.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: according to Shafi'i, the follower must recite al-Fatiha even when the imam recites aloud. According to Hanafi, the follower remains completely silent.
This difference significantly affects congregational prayer practice.

The Follower's Recitation Behind the Imam: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on follower's recitation with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the follower's recitation, identify the key proofs from Quran and hadith, and explain the thamarah al-khilaf with the Shafi'i school.

Core Idea
The imam's recitation suffices for the follower; reciting behind the imam is prohibited and invalidates the prayer.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah addresses one of the most prominent points of difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools: whether a person praying behind an imam must recite al-Fatiha. The Hanafi school firmly holds that the follower must not recite at all; rather, he listens when the imam recites aloud and remains silent when the imam recites silently. The author marshals a wealth of evidence from the Quran, multiple hadiths, and the practice of the Companions to establish this position and to refute the Shafi'i counterargument.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify exactly what the Hanafi school rules regarding the follower's recitation: it is forbidden (haram) to recite behind the imam; the follower must listen and remain silent.
2
Identify the opposing school and their view
Recognise that Imam al-Shafi'i holds the follower must recite al-Fatiha in every rak'ah, even behind an imam.
This is the key point of ikhtilaf.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the Shafi'i dalil: the general hadith 'No prayer except with the Fatiha of the Book' and the principle that recitation is an individual obligation.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Understand how the Hanafi school rebuts this: the general command is specified by the hadith 'Whoever has an imam, his recitation is recitation for him' and the explicit prohibition in 'Let none of you recite when I recite aloud'.
The response uses takhsis (specification) of the general text.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical consequence: in Hanafi prayer, the follower does not recite and the prayer is valid; in Shafi'i prayer, omitting al-Fatiha behind the imam invalidates the prayer.
This difference affects every congregational prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكل النفل، والوثر، ولم يتعين شيء من القرآنِ لصحةِ الصَّلاةِ، ولا يقرأ المؤتم، بل يستمع ويُنصت ......
تنبيه: قال في « البحر » : القراءة فرض عملي في ركعتي الفرض كما في «السراج» للاختلاف بين العلماء فيه انتهى. قلت: هذا ظاهر بالنظر للركعتين جميعاً، وإلا فقدمنا قول الزيلعي: انعقـد الإجماع على فرضيتهما وسند الإجماع قوله تعالى: ﴿فَاقْرَهُوا مَا تَيَسَّرَ﴾ [المزمل : ٢٠]، وقوله : « اقرأ ما تيسر معك من القرآن ) ولم يعتد بخلاف الأصم (وَ) القراءة فرض في (كُلِّ) ركعات (النَّفْلِ) لأن كل شفع منه صلاة على حدة وقد علمت افتراضها في الركعة الثانية كالأولى والقيام إلى الثالثة كتحريمة مبتدأة، ولهذا لا يجب بالتحريمة الأولى إلا شفع في المشهور كما سنذكره.(و) القراءة فرض في كل ركعات ( الوثر) أما على القول بسنيته فظاهر، وأما على القول بوجوبه أو فرضيته، فللاحتياط، ويقرأ في جميعه؛ لأن دليل الفرضية لما كان قاصراً لأنه من أخبار الآحاد ظهر أثر المقصود فيما هو من باب الاحتياط، وترك القراءة في ركعة من السنن يفسدها، فقلنا بالفساد هـا هنا احتياطاً ومراعاة لقصور الدليل، ولم يتعيَّن شيء من القرآنِ  ِلصِحَّةِ الصَّلاةِ) لإطلاق مـا تـلونـا
وما روينا، وأشرنا إلى قول الإمام الشافعي رحمه الله بتعيين الفاتحة لجواز الصلاة، وقلنـا بتعينـهـا وجوباً لذلك الدليل، وسنذكره" في الواجبات إن شاء الله تعالى (ولا يقرأُ المؤتم، بلْ يَسْتَمِعُ) في حال جهر الإمام ( ويُنصِتُ) حال إسراره لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِذَا قُرِئَ الْقُرْهَانُ فَاسْتَمِعُوا لَهُ وَأَنصِتُوا﴾ [الأعراف : ٢٠٤] قال أبو هريرة له : ( كَانُوا يقرؤون خلف الإمام فنزلت ) وقال الإمام أحمد: أجمع
الناس على أن هذه الآية في الصلاة وفي حديث أبي هريرة وأبي موسى: ( وإذا قرأ فأنصتوا ) قال مسلم: هذا الحديث صحيح. وعن عبادة بن الصامت أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام قال: « لا يقرأن أحد منكم شيئاً من القرآن إذا جهرتُ بالقرآن» (۱) قال الدارقطني : رجاله كلهم ثقات، ولا نقول بمفهوم المخالفة إذ ليس حجة عندنا، فلا يقرأ في السرية. وقال الإمام أحمد: ما سمعنا أحداً من أهل العلم يقول: إن الإمام إذا جهر بالقراءة لا تجزئ صلاة من لم يقرأ. وفي مسلم عن عطاء بن يسار أنه سأل زيد بن ثابت عن القراءة يعني: خلف الإمام فقال: « لا قراءة مع الإمام في شيء ) .
وعن جابر بمعناه وهو قول علي وابن مسعود ، وكثير من الصحابة ذكره الماوردي ولا حجة لمن أوجب على المؤتم قراءة الفاتحة مستدلاً بقوله : ( لا صَلاةَ إِلا بِفَاتِحَةِ الكِتَابِ ) لأن قراءة الإمام له قراءة على ما قاله عليه الصلاة والسلام : ( مَنْ كَانَ لَهُ إِمَامٌ فَقِرَاءتَهُ لَهُ قِرَاءَةٌ » (٣) كذا في التبيين» و « الزاهدي وروى أبو حنيفة في مسنده أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: «مَنْ كَانَ لَهُ إِمَامٌ فَقِرَاءَةُ الإمام لَهُ قِرَاءَةٌ » (۳) انتهى. وفي ( المصابيح) وغيره : قال : ( إِنَّمَا جُعل الإمام إماماً ليؤتُم بِهِ، فإذا قَرَأَ فَأَنْصِتُوا ) ولا يعارض بقوله : ( لا صَلاةَ إلا بقراءة ) ولا بقوله: « لا صَلاةَ إِلَّا بِفَاتِحَةِ الكِتَاب» (۱) لأن قراءة الإمام قراءة والصلاة بفاتحته صلاة بالفاتحة لقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم : « مَنْ كَانَ لَهُ إِمَامٌ فَقِرَاءته لَهُ قِرَاءةٌ » ) وذكر الطحاوي في شرح الآثار ) بإسناده عن أنس قال : « ثم أقبل بوجهه فقال: أتقرؤون والإمام يقرأ فَسَكَنُوا، فَسَأَلَهُمْ ثَلَاثَاً، فَقَالُوا إِنَّا لَتَفْعَلُ، قَالَ: فَلا تَفْعَلُوا ) وفيه أيضاً بإسناد متصل إلى ابن مسعوده أنه قال: « ليت الذي يقرأُ خلف الإمـام مـلـى فـوه تـرابـاً ) وعــن ابـن عباس عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه قال: « يَكْفِيكَ قِراءةُ الإمامِ جَهَرَ أَمْ خَافَتَ» (١٠) وروي عـن سـعـد بـن أبـي وقاص له أنه قال : « مَنْ قَرَأَ خَلْفَ الإِمَامِ فَسَدَتْ صَلاتُهُ » (۱۱) وقال محمد بن الحسن في « موطئـه » أخبرنا كثير بن عامر قال: حدثنا إبراهيم النخعي عن علقمة بن قيس قال: « لأن أعض على جَمْرَةٍ أحبَّ إِلَيَّ مِنْ أَنْ أَقْرَأْ خَلْفَ الإِمَامِ ) (۱) وقال فيه أيضاً، أخبرنا داود بن قيس الفراء أخبرنا محمــد بـن
And for every supererogatory prayer, and Witr, and no specific part of the Quran is designated for the validity of prayer, and the follower does not recite, but rather listens and remains silent...... A note: He said in al-Bahr: Recitation is a practical obligation in the two rak'ahs of the obligatory prayer, as in al-Siraj, due to the difference of scholars about it. End. I say: This is apparent with regard to the two rak'ahs together, otherwise we have presented the statement of al-Zayla'i: Consensus was reached on its obligation, and the basis of consensus is His statement: "So recite what is easy [of the Quran]" [al-Muzzammil: 20], and his statement: "Recite what is easy of the Quran with you." And the opposition of al-Asamm is not considered. (And) recitation is obligatory in every rak'ah of the supererogatory prayer, because every pair of it is a separate prayer, and you have known its obligation in the second rak'ah like the first, and standing for the third is like an initial takbir, and for this reason only a pair is obligated by the first takbir, as we will mention. (And) recitation is obligatory in all rak'ahs of Witr. As for the view that it is Sunnah, it is apparent; and as for the view of its being obligatory or mandatory, it is out of precaution, and one recites in all of it; because the evidence for obligation, since it is deficient (being from ahad hadith), the effect of the purpose appears in what is of the nature of precaution, and leaving recitation in a rak'ah of the Sunnahs corrupts it, so we said it is corrupt here out of precaution and due to the deficiency of the evidence. (And no specific part of the Quran is designated for the validity of prayer) due to the generality of what we have recited and what we have narrated, and we have pointed to the statement of Imam al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, regarding the designation of al-Fatiha for the validity of prayer, and we have said it is designated as obligatory due to that evidence, and we will mention it in the obligations if Allah wills. (And the follower does not recite, but listens) when the imam recites aloud, (and remains silent) when he recites silently, due to His statement: "And when the Quran is recited, listen to it and remain silent" [al-A'raf: 204]. Abu Hurayra said: They used to recite behind the imam, so this verse was revealed. And Imam Ahmad said: The people have agreed that this verse is about prayer. And in the hadith of Abu Hurayra and Abu Musa: "And when he recites, be silent." Muslim said: This hadith is authentic. And from Ubadah ibn al-Samit that the Prophet, peace be upon him, said: "Let none of you recite anything of the Quran when I recite aloud." Al-Daraqutni said: All its narrators are trustworthy. And we do not adhere to the converse meaning (mafhum al-mukhalafa) because it is not evidence with us, so he does not recite during silent recitation. And Imam Ahmad said: We have not heard anyone from the people of knowledge say that if the imam recites aloud, the prayer of one who does not recite is invalid. And in Muslim, from Ata ibn Yasar that he asked Zayd ibn Thabit about recitation behind the imam, and he said: "No recitation with the imam in anything." And from Jabir, similar meaning, and it is the statement of Ali and Ibn Mas'ud, and many of the Companions, al-Mawardi mentioned it. And there is no proof for the one who obliges upon the follower the recitation of al-Fatiha, using the hadith: "No prayer except with the Fatiha of the Book," because the imam's recitation is recitation for him, as the Prophet, peace be upon him, said: "Whoever has an imam, his recitation is recitation for him." Thus in al-Tabyin and al-Zahidi. And Abu Hanifa narrated in his Musnad that the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: "Whoever has an imam, the imam's recitation is recitation for him." End. And in al-Masabih and others: He said: "Indeed, the imam was appointed to be followed, so when he recites, be silent." And it is not contradicted by his statement: "No prayer except with recitation" nor by his statement: "No prayer except with the Fatiha of the Book," because the imam's recitation is recitation, and prayer with his Fatiha is prayer with the Fatiha, due to his statement: "Whoever has an imam, his recitation is recitation for him." And al-Tahawi mentioned in Sharh al-Athar with his chain from Anas, he said: "Then he turned his face and said: Do you recite while the imam is reciting? So they became silent. He asked them three times, and they said: Indeed we do. He said: Then do not do so." And in it also with a connected chain to Ibn Mas'ud that he said: "Would that the mouth of the one who recites behind the imam be filled with dust." And from Ibn Abbas from the Prophet, peace be upon him, that he said: "The recitation of the imam suffices you, whether he recites aloud or silently." And it was narrated from Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas that he said: "Whoever recites behind the imam, his prayer is spoiled." And Muhammad ibn al-Hasan said in his Muwatta: Kuthayyir ibn Amir informed us, he said: Ibrahim al-Nakha'i narrated to us from Alqama ibn Qays, he said: "That I should bite on a burning coal is dearer to me than that I should recite behind the imam." And he said in it also: Dawud ibn Qays al-Farra informed us, Muhammad ibn ...
Source pages p. 230

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah, a commentary on Nur al-Idah, addresses the rule of recitation (qira'ah) in prayer from the Hanafi perspective. The author begins by stating that recitation is obligatory in every rak'ah of supererogatory (nafl) and witr prayers, and that no specific verse or surah is required for the validity of the prayer. He then emphasises that the person praying behind an imam (al-mu'tam) must not recite; instead, he should listen attentively when the imam recites aloud and remain silent when the imam recites silently. The proof is taken from the Qur'anic verse 'When the Quran is recited, listen to it and be silent' (al-A'raf 204), which the Companions understood as applying to prayer. The commentary then engages in a detailed inter-madhhab dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i, who maintained that the follower must recite al-Fatiha. The Hanafi refutation relies on multiple hadiths, including 'Whoever has an imam, the imam's recitation is recitation for him' and explicit prohibitions of the follower reciting behind the imam. The author also cites statements of Companions and early scholars to reinforce the Hanafi position that the follower's obligation is fulfilled by the imam's recitation, and that reciting behind the imam is forbidden and invalidates the prayer.

Key Terms
المؤتم (al-mu'tam): The person who prays behind an imam in congregation, i.e., the follower.
الاستماع (al-istimāʿ): Attentive listening to the imam's recitation when he recites aloud.
الإنصات (al-inṣāt): Remaining silent and listening when the imam recites silently or aloud.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which hadith is used by the Hanafi school to support that the follower does not need to recite behind the imam?
A) 'No prayer except with the Fatiha of the Book.'
B) 'Whoever has an imam, his recitation is recitation for him.'
C) 'Pray as you have seen me pray.'
D) 'The best prayer is in congregation.'

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that the follower must not recite behind the imam; the imam's recitation fulfills the obligation, and the follower reciting invalidates the prayer.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
The Follower's Recitation Behind the Imam: Prohibition and Proof
Establishes prohibition of muqtadi reciting behind imam with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on follower recitation behind the Imam, identify the primary evidence, and explain why the narration of istihsan (precaution) is considered weak within the school.

Core Idea
The follower must not recite; the Imam's recitation suffices for both.

A critical question in congregational prayer is whether the follower recites the Qur'an behind the Imam. This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling, which is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked), and unpacks the textual proofs and internal school dispute. You will learn why the Imam's recitation is deemed sufficient and why a weak narration attributed to Imam Muhammad advocating precaution is not operative.

Guided Path
1
State the issue and the Hanafi position
Identify the act: follower reciting behind the Imam. State the Hanafi ruling: makruh tahrimi. Recognize that the follower must remain silent.
The follower is called muqtadi or mu'tamm.
2
Examine the primary evidence
Locate the main proofs: Quran 7:204, the hadith of Ibn Abbas, the statement of Umar, and the consensus of eighty Companions. Understand how these establish prohibition.
The verse commands listening and silence during Qur'an recitation.
3
Address the apparent conflicting evidence
Identify the hadith of 'Ubadah ibn al-Samit and the principle of istihsan (precaution) that seem to permit recitation. Analyze the Hanafi response: the hadith is abrogated and precaution cannot lead to invalidating the prayer.
The Prophet's statement 'Why do I contend with the Qur'an?' shows later prohibition.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Contrast the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf (makruh) and the weak narration from Muhammad (mustahabb). Determine why the narration is weak and that Muhammad's authentic works agree with the majority.
In 'al-Athar', Muhammad explicitly denies recitation behind the Imam.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and its basis
Conclude that the relied-upon position is makruh tahrimi. Understand why it is not called haram: the evidence is not qat'i (decisive) in transmission or indication.
The term 'haraam' is avoided due to the principle that a zanni dalil yields a zanni hukm.

ما رويتم فإن قلت: قال الشيخ الإمام أبو حفص النسفي: إن كان في صلاة الجهر يكره قراءة المأموم عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف، وقال محمد لا يكره بل يستحب وبه ،نأخذ لأنه أحوط ، وهو مذهب الصديق والفاروق والمرتضى، قلت: قال الكمال بـ ( فتح القدير وإنْ قرأَ المؤتم كُرة تَحريماً وفي بعض الروايات: إنها لا تحـل خـلـف الإمام، وإنما لم يطلقوا اسم الحرمة عليهما لما عرف من أصلهم، إذا لم يكن الدليل قطعياً، ومـا يروى عن محمد أنه يستحسن على سبيل الاحتياط فضعيف، والحق أن قول محمد كقولهما، وصرح محمد في كتبه بعدم القراءة خلف الإمام فيما يجهر فيه وما لا يجهر، فإنه في كتاب «الآثار» في باب القراءة خلف الإمام بعدما أسند إلى علقمة بن قيس أنه ما قرأ قط فيما يجهر فيه ولا فيما لا يجهر فيه قال: أي: محمد وبه نأخذ ؛ لأنا لا نرى القراءة خلف الإمام في شيء من | الصلاة يجهر فيه أو لا يجهر، وقال « السرخسي : تفسد صلاته بالقراءة في قول عدة من الصحابة، انتهى. وقال في الكافي : ومنع المقتدي عن القراءة مأثور عن تمانين نفراً من كبار الصحابة منهم المرتضى)،
Similar. (2) 'Ajlan that 'Umar ibn al-Khattab said: 'I wish that the mouth of the one who recites behind the Imam had a stone.' Likewise in 'Sharh al-Kanz' by Imam al-Dayri. And he said in 'Sharh al-Quduri' called 'Majma' al-Riwayat': The follower should not recite behind the Imam due to the hadith of Ibn 'Abbas that he recited and his companions recited with him, then the verse was revealed: 'And when the Qur'an is recited, listen to it and be silent' [7:204]. He said in 'al-Nihaya': It cannot be said that the Imam is silent for the follower to recite, because we say: The dispute is established regarding an Imam who does not remain silent, and because remaining silent without recitation while standing is makruh, and if he remains silent for a long time, he must perform two prostrations of forgetfulness, and the prohibition of the follower reciting behind the Imam is narrated from eighty of the senior Companions, and the hadith scholars have collected their names. And 'Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi' said: His prayer is invalid according to the statement of several Companions, and from 'Abdullah al-Balkhi that he said: I would love to fill his mouth with dust, and we have previously mentioned from Ibn Mas'ud. End. And it is said: It is mustahabb to break his teeth because of the warning. The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: 'Whoever recites behind the Imam has a burning coal in his mouth.' And he said: 'Whoever recites behind the Imam has missed the fitrah.' And what is narrated from the hadith of 'Ubadah ibn al-Samit about the follower reciting behind the Imam is interpreted to mean that it was a pillar initially, then he prohibited them from reciting behind him after that. Do you not see that when he heard a man reciting, he said: 'Why do I contend with the Qur'an?' Recitation is different from other pillars, as the purpose of other pillars is not achieved by the Imam's action, unlike recitation as mentioned in 'al-Mabsut' and 'al-Asrar' in 'Sharh al-Kafi' by al-Bazdawi: Recitation behind the Imam as a precaution is good according to Muhammad, and makruh according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad? Actually 'indahuma'). And from Abu Hanifa that there is no harm in reciting al-Fatihah in Zuhr and 'Asr and whatever he wishes of the Qur'an. End. Similarly in some copies of 'al-Dhakhirah' from the sections of the second chapter of the Book of Prayer, then he mentioned the fourth chapter on issues of the follower with this issue and said: The correct view is that it is makruh. End. And in 'al-Fawa'id': The follower should not perform it because according to Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas, if the follower performs it, his prayer is invalid. So if we say that the follower should perform it as a precaution, it would lead to the invalidity of his prayer according to one who is many degrees superior to a mujtahid who disagrees with him, and precaution is not allowed in a way that leads to the invalidity of his prayer according to one of the Companions, who is one of the ten promised Paradise. End. And Abu Bakr al-Razi al-Jassas said in his commentary on Mukhtasar al-Tahawi from Jabir ibn 'Abdullah that the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: 'Whoever prays a prayer and does not recite the Fatihah in it, it is deficient, except behind an Imam.' And from 'Ali: 'Whoever recites behind the Imam is not upon the fitrah.' And the reports on this are many. And if the recitation of the follower were a pillar, it would not be dropped from him when he catches the Imam in ruku' like other pillars, and we have agreed on its being dropped and that he catches the rak'ah. So if recitation were obligatory upon him, it would not be dropped from him due to such a necessity, like qiyam, for if he says the takbir while leaning, it is not valid unless he says the takbir standing then bows. And in 'al-Hafiziyyah': We have agreed that the Imam bears the extra beyond the Fatihah from the follower; similarly, he bears the Fatihah as well, because his saying, peace be upon him: 'The recitation of the Imam is recitation for him' is absolute. If you say: Qiyam is a pillar and it drops when one catches the Imam in ruku', we say: We do not concede that it drops; rather, it is fulfilled by the takbir while standing, because the obligation of qiyam is fulfilled by the minimum that qualifies as qiyam. As for the hadith, we say: This is a prayer with recitation because the Law has made the Imam's recitation as recitation for him, as we have mentioned, and the reports we have mentioned are prohibitive and specific, and free from specification, so they are preponderant in these respects, unlike what you have narrated. If you say: The Shaykh al-Imam Abu Hafs al-Nasafi said: If the prayer is loud, the follower's recitation is makruh according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad said it is not makruh but rather mustahabb, and we take that because it is more precautionary, and it is the madhhab of al-Siddiq, al-Faruq, and al-Murtada. I say: Al-Kamal said in 'Fath al-Qadir': If the follower recites, it is makruh tahriman, and in some narrations: It is not permissible behind the Imam. They did not explicitly say it is haram because of their principle that when the evidence is not decisive. And what is narrated from Muhammad that he considers it good as a precaution is weak, and the truth is that Muhammad's saying is like theirs, and Muhammad clearly stated in his books the non-recitation behind the Imam in both loud and silent, for in his book 'al-Athar', in the chapter on recitation behind the Imam, after attributing to 'Alqamah ibn Qays that he never recited behind the Imam in loud or silent, he said: Muhammad said: And we take that; because we do not see recitation behind the Imam in any prayer, loud or silent. And al-Sarakhsi said: His prayer is invalid by recitation according to the statement of several Companions, end. And he said in 'al-Kafi': The prohibition of the follower reciting is transmitted from eighty of the senior Companions, among them al-Murtada.
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the ruling on a follower (muqtadi) reciting behind the imam in prayer. The author presents the established Hanafi position that the follower should not recite; rather, the imam’s recitation suffices for both. He supports this with numerous evidences: the Quranic verse 7:204 (And when the Qur’an is recited, listen to it and be silent), which was revealed when Companions recited behind the Prophet; the statement of ‘Umar wishing a stone in the mouth of one who recites behind the imam; and the narration from eighty Companions prohibiting it. Shams al-A’imma al-Sarakhsi is quoted saying that recitation invalidates the prayer according to several Companions. The hadith of ‘Ubadah ibn al-Samit that appears to permit recitation is explained as abrogated: originally it was required, but later the Prophet prohibited it, as evidenced by his objection to a man reciting behind him (‘Why do I contend with the Qur’an?’). The author distinguishes recitation from other pillars: while the imam’s action does not fulfill the follower’s obligation for other pillars (like qiyam), recitation is unique because the Prophet said, ‘The recitation of the imam is recitation for him.’ The internal Hanafi disagreement is then addressed: Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani reportedly considered it mustahabb (recommended) as a precaution, while Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf considered it makruh. However, the author clarifies that this narration from Muhammad is weak. In his established books like al-Athar, Muhammad explicitly denies recitation behind the imam in all prayers, agreeing with the two. Therefore, the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that it is makruh tahriman (prohibitively disliked) — not haram, because the evidence is not absolutely decisive — and the follower should abstain from recitation entirely.

Key Terms
المقتدي / المؤتم (al-muqtadi / al-mu'tamm): The person following the imam in congregational prayer.
القراءة خلف الإمام (al-qira'ah khalf al-imam): Recitation of the follower behind the imam during the prayer.
تحمل الإمام (tahammul al-imam): The imam bearing the recitation on behalf of the follower, i.e., his recitation suffices for the follower.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position presented in this text, what is the ruling on a follower reciting behind the imam?
A) It is wajib (obligatory).
B) It is mustahabb (recommended) as a precaution.
C) It is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked).
D) It is haram (unlawful).

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that the follower must remain silent behind the imam; the imam's recitation suffices for both, and recitation by the follower is makruh tahrimi.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Ma'mum Recitation Behind Imam
Intra-Hanafi dispute on ma'mum recitation, with proofs and resolution.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the follower's recitation behind the imam and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, identifying the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
The follower may not recite behind the imam; doing so is makruh tahriman, not haram.

This lesson examines a key intra-Hanafi dispute: should the follower (ma'mum) recite the Fatiha behind the imam? While the majority of the school, including Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, deem it makruh tahriman, a narration from Muhammad suggests it is mustahabb. We will trace the evidence, resolve the apparent conflict, and clarify the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
State the general Hanafi position
Begin by clearly stating that the follower does not recite behind the imam; recitation is makruh tahriman.
This is the mufta bihi position.
2
Identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Note that Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold it is makruh, while a narration from Muhammad says it is mustahabb.
The ikhtilaf is only apparent.
3
Examine the dalil for the majority view
Look at the hadith: 'Prayer without Fatiha is deficient except behind imam', and the consensus of eighty Companions.
The imam's recitation suffices for the follower.
4
Analyse the response to Muhammad's narration
Muhammad's explicit statement in al-Athar agrees with the majority; the narration of istihbab is weak.
Al-Kamal ibn al-Humam clarifies this.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that follower's recitation is makruh tahriman; caution is in not reciting.
Ibn al-Humam: 'Caution is to refrain.'

الصلاة عند من هو أفضل من مجتهد خالفه بدرجات كثيرة، ولا يجوز الاحتياط على وجه يلزم منه فساد صلاته عند واحد من الصحابة وهو من العشرة المبشرين بالجنة. انتهى. وقال أبو بكر الرازي الجصاص في شرحه لمختصر الطحاوي عن جابر بن عبد الله قال: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: ( من صلى صلاة لم يقرأ فيها بفاتحة الكتاب فهي خداج إلا خلف الإمام ). وعن علي رضي الله عنه: ( من قرأ خلف الإمام فليس على الفطرة )، والأخبار في ذلك كثيرة، ولو كانت قراءة المأموم ركناً لما سقطت عنه إذا أدرك الإمام في الركوع كسائر الأركان، وقد أجمعنا على سقوطها وإدراكه الركعة، فلو كانت القراءة واجبة عليه لما سقطت عنه بمثل هذه الضرورة كالقيام، فإنه لو كبر منحنياً لا يجوز ما لم يكبر قائماً ثم يركع، وفي ( الحافظية ): أجمعنا على أن الإمام يتحمل الزائد على الفاتحة عن المقتدي، كذا يتحمل الفاتحة أيضاً؛ لأن قوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: ( قراءة الإمام قراءة له ) مطلق، فإن قلت: القيام ركن وأنه يسقط إذا أدرك الإمام في الركوع، قلنا: لا نسلم أنه يسقط بل يتأدى بالتكبير قائماً؛ لأنه يتأدى فرض القيام بأدنى ما ينطلق عليه اسم القيام، وأما الحديث فقلنا: هذه صلاة بقراءة لأن الشرع جعل قراءة الإمام له قراءة كما قدمناه وما ذكرناه من الأخبار محرم وخاص، وسليم عن التخصيص، فترجح بهذه الجهات بخلاف ما رويتم. فإن قلت: قال الشيخ الإمام أبو حفص النسفي: إن كان في صلاة الجهر يكره قراءة المأموم عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف، وقال محمد لا يكره بل يستحب وبه نأخذ لأنه أحوط، وهو مذهب الصديق والفاروق والمرتضى، قلت: قال الكمال في فتح القدير: وإن قرأ المؤتم كره تحريماً، وفي بعض الروايات: إنها لا تحل خلف الإمام، وإنما لم يطلقوا اسم الحرمة عليهما لما عرف من أصلهم، إذا لم يكن الدليل قطعياً، وما يروى عن محمد أنه يستحسن على سبيل الاحتياط فضعيف، والحق أن قول محمد كقولهما، وصرح محمد في كتبه بعدم القراءة خلف الإمام فيما يجهر فيه وما لا يجهر، فإنه في كتاب «الآثار» في باب القراءة خلف الإمام بعدما أسند إلى علقمة بن قيس أنه ما قرأ قط فيما يجهر فيه ولا فيما لا يجهر فيه قال: أي محمد: وبه نأخذ؛ لأنا لا نرى القراءة خلف الإمام في شيء من الصلاة يجهر فيه أو لا يجهر، وقال السرخسي: تفسد صلاته بالقراءة في قول عدة من الصحابة، انتهى. وقال في الكافي: ومنع المقتدي عن القراءة مأثور عن ثمانين نفراً من كبار الصحابة منهم المرتضى والعبادلة، وقد دون أهل الحديث أسماءهم. انتهى. ثم قال المحقق ابن الهمام: ثم لا يخفى أن الاحتياط في عدم القراءة خلف الإمام؛ لأن الاحتياط هو العمل بأقوى الدليلين، وليس مقتضى أقواهما القراءة بل المنع. انتهى.
The prayer according to the one who is superior to the mujtahid who disagreed with him by many degrees, and it is not permissible to act cautiously in a way that necessitates the invalidity of his prayer according to one of the Companions who is among the ten promised Paradise. End. And Abu Bakr al-Razi al-Jassas said in his commentary on Mukhtasar al-Tahawi from Jabir ibn Abdullah that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever prays a prayer and does not recite the Fatiha in it, it is deficient except behind the imam.' And from Ali (may Allah be pleased with him): 'Whoever recites behind the imam is not upon the fitrah.' And the reports on this are many. And if the recitation of the follower were a pillar, it would not be dropped when he catches the imam in bowing, like other pillars. And we have consensus that it is dropped and that he catches the rak'ah. And if the recitation were obligatory (wajib) upon him, it would not be dropped by such a necessity, like standing: for if he says the takbir while bent over, it is not valid unless he says it standing then bows. And in al-Hafiziyyah: We have consensus that the imam bears the additional (recitation) beyond the Fatiha from the follower, likewise he bears the Fatiha as well; because the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'The recitation of the imam is a recitation for him' is absolute. If you say: Standing is a pillar and it falls when he catches the imam in bowing, we say: We do not concede that it falls; rather it is fulfilled by saying the takbir while standing, because the obligation of standing is fulfilled by the minimum that can be called standing. As for the hadith, we say: This is a prayer with recitation because the Law has made the imam's recitation a recitation for him, as we have presented. And what we have mentioned from the reports is forbidden and specific, and safe from specification; so it outweighs in these aspects contrary to what you have narrated. And if you say: Shaykh Imam Abu Hafs al-Nasafi said: If it is a loud prayer, the follower's recitation is disliked (makruh) according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad said it is not disliked but rather recommended, and we adopt his view because it is more cautious, and it is the madhhab of al-Siddiq, al-Faruq, and al-Murtada. We say: al-Kamal said in Fath al-Qadir: If the follower recites, it is makruh tahriman, and in some narrations: It is not permissible behind the imam. They did not use the term 'forbidden' (haram) due to their known principle when the proof is not definitive. And what is narrated from Muhammad that he approves out of caution is weak, and the truth is that Muhammad's view is like theirs. And Muhammad explicitly stated in his books not to recite behind the imam in loud and silent prayers. For in the book al-Athar, in the chapter on recitation behind the imam, after he narrated from Alqamah ibn Qays that he never recited in loud or silent prayers, he (Muhammad) said: We adopt this; for we do not consider recitation behind the imam in any prayer, loud or silent. And al-Sarakhsi said: His prayer is invalidated by recitation according to the statement of several Companions. End. And he said in al-Kafi: The prohibition of the follower from recitation is reported from eighty senior Companions, including al-Murtada and the 'Abadilah, and the hadith scholars have recorded their names. End. Then the investigator Ibn al-Humam said: Then it is not hidden that caution lies in not reciting behind the imam, because caution is to act on the stronger of the two proofs, and the implication of the stronger one is not recitation but prohibition. End.
Source pages p. 233

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling of the follower (ma'mum) reciting behind the imam. It opens by stating that acting cautiously in a way that invalidates the prayer according to a Companion who is from the ten promised Paradise is not permissible. Then it brings hadith evidence: the Prophet said that a prayer without Fatiha is deficient except behind an imam, and Ali said that reciting behind the imam is not upon the fitrah. The author then argues by qiyas: if recitation were a pillar, it would not be dropped when catching the imam in bowing, but it is dropped by consensus. And if it were wajib, it would not be dropped by this necessity, like standing is not dropped. This shows recitation is not a pillar nor wajib for the follower. Then he quotes al-Hafiziyyah that the imam bears the recitation for the follower, based on the hadith 'The recitation of the imam is a recitation for him.' He responds to an objection about standing being dropped by explaining that standing is fulfilled by the minimum, so it is not actually dropped. Then he addresses an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf say it is makruh, while Muhammad says it is mustahabb. The author then shows that the truth is that Muhammad's view is the same as theirs, as he explicitly stated in al-Athar that he does not see recitation behind the imam. Al-Sarakhsi says it invalidates the prayer according to several Companions. Al-Kafi reports prohibition from eighty Companions. Ibn al-Humam concludes that the precaution is not to recite, aligning with the stronger proof. This is a detailed discussion of the evidence and the resolution of the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf. The relied-upon position is that the follower does not recite behind the imam, and doing so is makruh tahriman.

Key Terms
خداج (khidāj): Deficiency or defect; specifically referring to the prayer being incomplete due to missing the Fatiha.
مأموم (ma'mūm): The person praying behind an imam in congregational prayer; the follower.
قراءة خلف الإمام (qirā'at khalfa al-imām): Reciting Quranic verses, especially Fatiha, while praying behind an imam.
كراهة تحريمية (karāhat tahrīmiyya): A level of dislike that approaches prohibition; acting upon it is sinful but does not invalidate the act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what is the ruling if a follower recites the Fatiha behind the imam in a loud prayer?
A) It is obligatory (fard).
B) It is recommended (mustahabb).
C) It is prohibitively disliked (makruh tahriman).
D) It is forbidden (haram).

Key Takeaway
The follower's recitation behind the imam is makruh tahriman, not haram; caution is in refraining.

Congregational Prayer: Place of Awe or Intimacy?
Refutation of Shafi'i's argument that congregational prayer is a place of intimacy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi critique of the Shafi'i argument that congregational prayer is a place of intimacy, and apply the Hanafi ruling that the follower does not recite behind the imam.

Core Idea
Congregational prayer is a place of awe, not intimacy; only the imam recites.

Imam al-Shafi'i argued that the follower should recite the Fatiha behind the imam because prayer is a direct conversation with Allah—a place of intimacy. The Hanafi response, presented here, flips the analogy: prayer is like standing before a majestic king, where only one speaks at a time. The author reconciles both views by locating intimacy at the moment of saying 'Amin'. This lesson unpacks the proofs and the practical ruling that the follower remains silent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested issue
The core dispute is whether the follower should recite (specifically the Fatiha) behind the imam. The Shafi'i school holds it obligatory; the Hanafi school holds it prohibited (makruh tahriman).
Both schools agree the imam recites aloud in audible prayers.
2
Examine the Shafi'i proof
Shafi'i argues that prayer is a place of intimacy (inbisat) because Allah says 'And say, praise be to Allah' (27:93) and the hadith 'the one praying converses with his Lord.' This implies the follower should also converse.
The verse is general; Shafi'i deduces that individual supplication is encouraged.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi author responds that congregational prayer is a place of awe (haybah), like subjects before a king: only one speaks. The hadith 'the most proficient should lead' proves the imam alone recites. The intimacy (munajat) occurs collectively through Amin at the end.
The analogy of the king relies on 'urf and qiyas.
4
Understand the reconciliation
Both stations are combined: the prayer itself is awe, but the Amin at the conclusion is a shared intimate moment. This resolves the tension and shows the Hanafi position incorporates the valid element of intimacy.
The author calls this a 'gift' (tuhfah) to the reader.
5
Note the authority of the position
The passage ends with consensus of the three imams (Abu Hanifa, Malik, Ahmad) and implies the strength of the Hanafi ruling. The follower should not recite; if he does, the prayer is valid but makruh tahriman.
The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is silence for the follower.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تتمة لطيفة: قال في كتاب « السنة والجماعة» أن الإمام الشافعي رحمه الله تعالى يقول: المقام مقام الانبساط، ألا يرى إلى قوله تعالى: ﴿وقل الحمد لله﴾ [النمل: 93] والدليل عليه أنهم مأمورون بالصلاة والجماعة خصوصاً لهذه الأمة، وقال عليه الصلاة والسلام: «يقول الله تعالى: المتصدق يقرضني، والمصلي يناجيني، والصوم لي وأنا أجزي به» فثبت أن المكان مكان الانبساط. قلنا: بل مكان هيبة وجلال على مثال جماعة وقفوا بين يدي ملك فإن أحدهم يتكلم معه ولا يتكلمون جميعاً لمقتضى المقام والإجلال حذراً عن التخليط والخطأ، فكذلك لما قاموا بين يدي الملك الجبار فإن إمامهم يقرأ دونهم، لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: «يؤمكم أقرؤكم لكتاب الله»، وفي رواية: «يؤمكم أنوركم» أي: أنوركم بقراءة القرآن فهذا يدل على أن المقام مقام هيبة وجلال، على أنه يحصل مقام الانبساط عند الختام حين يؤمن القوم والإمام، إذ به المشاركة في المناجاة وجمع بين المقامين، وقد أتحفناك بهذا الجمع فاختر أحسن الحسنين، وقد اتفق الإمام الأعظم أبو حنيفة وأصحابه، والإمام مالك والإمام أحمد بن حنبل رضي الله عنهم على صحة صلاة المأموم من غير قراءته شيئاً خلف الإمام، فأرح نفسك من العناء والسلام.
A pleasant supplement: It is said in the book 'al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah' that Imam al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him) says: The place is a place of intimacy. Do you not see the verse: 'And say, praise be to Allah' (27:93). And the evidence is that they are commanded to pray in congregation especially for this nation, and the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Allah Almighty said: The giver of charity lends Me, the one who prays converses with Me, and fasting is for Me and I reward for it.' So it is established that the place is a place of intimacy. We say: Rather it is a place of awe and majesty, like a group standing before a king: one of them speaks with him and they do not all speak, due to the requirements of the situation and veneration, out of fear of confusion and error. Thus, when they stand before the Mighty King, their imam recites and they do not, due to his saying (peace be upon him): 'The one most proficient in the Book of Allah should lead you.' In another narration: 'The most illuminated of you should lead you,' meaning the most illuminated by recitation of the Quran. This indicates that the place is a place of awe and majesty. However, the place of intimacy is achieved at the conclusion when the people and the imam say 'Amin,' as through that there is participation in the intimate conversation, combining both stations. We have gifted you this combination, so choose the better of the two good things. And the Greatest Imam Abu Hanifa and his companions, Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal (may Allah be pleased with them) have agreed upon the validity of the follower's prayer without him reciting anything behind the imam. So put your mind at ease from difficulty, and peace.
Source pages p. 234

Commentary
This is a response to Imam al-Shafi'i's view that congregational prayer is a place of intimacy (inbisat), where the follower is encouraged to recite along with the imam. The author refutes this by arguing that it is rather a place of awe (haybah) and majesty (jalal). He draws an analogy: just as subjects before a king do not all speak at once, but only one addresses him, so in prayer, only the imam recites. This is supported by the hadith that the most proficient in Quran should lead, implying the imam is the sole reciter. The author reconciles by stating that intimacy occurs at the end when saying 'Amin', but during the prayer itself, it is a time of listening. The passage concludes that the four great imams (Abu Hanifa, Malik, Ahmad) agree that the follower does not recite, so one should follow this consensus.

Key Terms
هيبة (haybah): Awe; the reverential fear and respect due to being in the presence of a majestic king or Allah.
انبساط (inbisāṭ): Intimacy; a state of ease and direct conversation, as with a close friend.
أقرؤكم (aqra'ukum): The one among you most proficient in Quran recitation.
أنوركم (anwarukum): The most illuminated (by Quran) among you.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) A group of friends conversing freely
B) Subjects standing before a king, where only one speaks
C) A student reciting in class
D) A solo traveler worshipping alone

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the follower does not recite behind the imam; prayer is a place of awe, and intimacy is reserved for the collective Amin.

Ruling on the Follower's Recitation Behind the Imam
Statement of the ruling that follower's recitation is prohibitively disliked

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on the follower's recitation during congregational prayer and identify which supplications are prohibited.

Core Idea
The follower must remain silent and listen; any recitation or personal supplication is makruh tahriman.

This lesson clarifies the Hanafi position on what the follower (ma'mum) should do when the imam recites aloud in congregational fard prayer. Many Muslims assume that personal supplications during verses of mercy or punishment are recommended, but the Hanafi school considers them prohibitively disliked. We will examine the evidence and the specific exceptions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Locate in the text the explicit ruling on the follower reciting the Fatiha or any other Quran. Note the phrase 'kariha dhalika tahriman'.
The ruling applies to any recitation, including the Fatiha.
2
Note the additional prohibitions
The text also forbids the follower from making ta'awwudh (seeking refuge from Fire) or asking for Paradise (asking for Jannah) when the imam recites verses of threat or mercy.
This applies to both the imam and the follower, but the focus is on the follower.
3
Understand the exception for nafl prayers
The hadith showing the Prophet making these supplications is interpreted as applying only to supererogatory (nafl) prayers performed alone, not to obligatory congregational prayers.
This distinguishes the general sunnah from the specific context of congregation.
4
Summarize the practical implication
During a fard congregational prayer, the follower should listen attentively, remain silent, and avoid any personal recitation or audible supplication.
This ensures focus on the imam's recitation and the prayer itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و) قلنا: إن قرأ المأموم الفاتحة أو غيرها (كره) ذلك (تحريماً) لما قدمناه، ولا يشتغل المأموم بتعوذ من نار، ولا طلب جنة عند قراءة الإمام آية ترغيب أو ترهيب، وكذا الإمام، وما روي أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام « ما مر بآية رحمة إلا سألها وآية عذاب إلا استعاذ منها » محمول على النوافل منفرداً.
And we say: If the follower recites the Fatiha or other (than it), that is disliked (makruh) with prohibition (tahriman) due to what we have presented. And the follower should not engage in seeking refuge from the Fire nor asking for Paradise when the imam recites a verse of mercy or threat, and likewise the imam. And what is narrated that he (peace be upon him) never passed by a verse of mercy except he asked for it, nor a verse of punishment except he sought refuge from it, is interpreted as applying to supererogatory prayers when alone.
Source pages p. 234

Commentary
This is the concluding ruling on the topic: the follower's recitation of any Quranic verse, including the Fatiha, behind the imam is makruh tahriman (prohibitively disliked). This is based on the evidence already discussed. Additionally, the follower should not make personal supplications like asking for Paradise or seeking refuge from Hell when the imam recites verses of mercy or punishment; this applies similarly to the imam. The hadith that describes the Prophet making such supplications during prayer is understood to refer to supererogatory (nafl) prayers performed alone, not to obligatory congregational prayers. This ruling emphasizes the proper demeanor of listening in awe during congregational prayer.

Key Terms
تعوذ (ta'awwudh): The act of seeking refuge with Allah, often by saying 'A'udhu billah min al-shaytan al-rajim' or from the Fire.
ترغيب (targhīb): Verses of mercy and paradise that encourage good deeds.
ترهيب (tarhīb): Verses of warning and punishment that discourage evil.
نافلة (nāfilah): Supererogatory or voluntary prayer, as opposed to obligatory (fard) prayer.

C) It is prohibitively disliked (makruh tahriman)
D) It is required (wajib)

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the follower must remain silent in congregational fard prayers; any recitation or personal supplication is makruh tahriman, as the hadith is restricted to nafl prayers alone.

Recitation Behind the Imam: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab debate on follower's recitation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on recitation behind the imam and explain the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i proof.

Core Idea
Follower's recitation behind the imam is makruh tahriman; the imam's recitation suffices for all.

This lesson addresses one of the classic points of difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools: whether a follower (ma'mum) must recite al-Fatihah behind the imam. You will examine both sides' proofs and understand why the Hanafi school holds it not only unnecessary but prohibitively disliked. The passage also introduces a powerful analogy that clarifies the school's view on the proper attitude in congregational prayer.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Clearly articulate the ruling: it is makruh tahriman for the follower to recite anything behind the imam. Note that the prayer remains valid even if the follower recites.
The ruling is based on the principle that the imam's recitation suffices.
2
Identify the opposing school and their view
Identify that Imam al-Shafi'i holds the follower must recite al-Fatihah (wajib or fard). Understand the practical consequence: omitting it invalidates the prayer in the Shafi'i school.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Analyze the Shafi'i proof: prayer is a place of intimate conversation (munajat) with Allah, and the hadith 'No prayer for one who does not recite al-Fatihah' is general.
The Shafi'i school uses the hadith qudsi about the praying person conversing with Allah.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Understand the Hanafi counter-argument: prayer is a place of awe and majesty (haybah), not uncontrolled intimacy. The analogy of standing before a king: only one speaks. The intimate conversation occurs collectively through the imam's recitation and the followers' 'amin'.
The Hanafi school also cites the hadith 'Let the one most proficient lead you' to show the imam recites for all.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical difference: in the Hanafi school, the follower must not recite (sinful if he does) but the prayer is valid; in the Shafi'i school, the follower must recite or the prayer is invalid.
This difference affects how a Hanafi follower should behave in a mixed congregation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

تتمة لطيفة: قال في كتاب « السنة والجماعة» أن الإمام الشافعي رحمه الله تعالى يقول: الـمـقـام مقام الإنبساط، ألا يرى إلى قوله تعالى: ﴿وَقُلاً تحَمدُ لِلَّهِ ﴾ [النمل: ۹۳] والدليل عليه أنهم مأمورون بالصلاة والجماعة خصوصاً لهذه الأمة، وقال عليه الصلاة والسلام: «يقولُ الله تعالى: المتصدق يقرضني، والمصلّي يناجِينِي، والصومُ لي وأنا أجزي بِهِ » ) فثبت أن المكان مكان الانبساط. قلنا: بل مكان هيبة وجلال على مثال جماعة وقفوا بين يدي ملك فإن أحدهم يتكلم معه ولا يتكلمون جميعاً لمقتضى المقام والإجلال حذراً عن التخليط والخطأ، فكذلك لما قاموا بين يدي الملك الجبار فإن إمامهم يقرأ ،دونهم، لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام : « يؤمكم أقرؤكم لكتاب الله )، وفي رواية: «يؤمكم أنوركم ) أي : أنوركُم بقراءة القرآن فهذا يدل على أن المقام مقام هيبة وجلال، علـى أنه يحصل مقام الانبساط عند الختام حين يؤمن القوم والإمام، إذ به المشاركة في المناجاة وجمع بين المقامين، وقد أتحفناك بهذا الجمع فاختر أحسن الحسنين، وقد اتفق الإمام الأعظم أبو حنيفة وأصحابه، والإمام مالك والإمام أحمد بن حنبل الله على صحة صلاة المأموم مــن غيـر قراءته شيئاً خلف الإمام، فأرح نفسك من العناء والسلام. (وَ) قلنا: ( إن قرأ المأموم الفاتحة أو غيرها (كـره) ذلك (تحريماً) لما قدمناه، ولا يشتغل المأموم بتعوذ من نار، ولا طلب جنة عند قراءة الإمام آيــة ترغيب أو ترهيب، وكذا الإمام، وما روي أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام « مَا مَرَّ بِآيَةٍ رحمةٍ إلا سألها وآية عذاب إلا استعاذ منها ) محمول على النوافل منفرداً.
And if he recites, it is disliked prohibitively. And 'the Abdallas', the people of hadith have recorded their names. End. Then the researcher Ibn al-Humam said: Then it is not hidden that the precaution is in not reciting behind the imam; because precaution is to act by the stronger of the two proofs, and the implication of the stronger of them is not recitation, rather prohibition. End. A beneficial completion: He said in the book 'al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah' that Imam al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, says: The position is a position of expansiveness. Do you not see the saying of Allah Most High: 'And say, Praise be to Allah' [al-Naml 93]? The evidence for it is that they are commanded with prayer and congregation especially for this ummah, and he, peace be upon him, said: 'Allah says: The giver of charity gives Me a loan, the one who prays converses with Me, and fasting is for Me and I reward for it.' So it is established that the place is a place of expansiveness. We said: Rather it is a place of awe and majesty, like the example of a group standing before a king: one of them speaks with him, but they do not all speak out of the requirement of the position and veneration, cautioning against confusion and error. So likewise, when they stand before the King, the Compeller, their imam recites, not them, due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'Let the one most proficient in the Book of Allah lead you in prayer,' and in a narration: 'Let the one with the most light among you lead you,' meaning the most illuminated with recitation of the Quran. This indicates that the position is one of awe and majesty, except that the position of expansiveness occurs at the conclusion when the people and the imam say 'amin', for therein is participation in intimate conversation, combining the two positions. We have gifted you with this combination, so choose the better of the two beauties. And Imam Abu Hanifa and his companions, Imam Malik, and Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal, may Allah have mercy on them, have agreed on the validity of the prayer of the follower without him reciting anything behind the imam. So relieve yourself of trouble, and peace. And we said: If the follower recites al-Fatihah or other than it, that is disliked prohibitively, due to what we have presented. And the follower does not occupy himself with seeking refuge from the Fire, nor with seeking Paradise when the imam recites a verse of encouragement or intimidation, and likewise the imam. And what is narrated that he, peace be upon him, 'never passed by a verse of mercy except he asked for it, nor a verse of punishment except he sought refuge from it' is interpreted as applying to supererogatory prayers when alone.
Source pages p. 234

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the ruling on a follower (ma'mum) reciting behind the imam in congregational prayer. The Hanafi school holds that it is makruh tahriman (prohibitively disliked) for the follower to recite anything, including al-Fatihah, behind the imam. The proof presented is the hadith 'Let the one most proficient in the Book of Allah lead you in prayer,' which places the responsibility of recitation solely on the imam, and the analogy of a group standing before a king where only one speaks. Imam al-Shafi'i argues that the congregational prayer is a place of intimacy (inbisat) between the servant and Allah, citing a hadith qudsi about the praying person conversing with Allah, and that the followers are also commanded to recite. The Hanafi response is that the prayer is a place of awe (haybah) and majesty, not unrestricted intimacy; the follower's participation in the intimate conversation occurs at the end when they say 'amin' together. The passage also notes that the consensus of Abu Hanifa, Malik, and Ahmad supports the Hanafi view. The final ruling is reiterated: if the follower recites, it is makruh tahriman. Additionally, the follower should not engage in supplications for Paradise or seeking refuge from Hell during the imam's recitation, as these are reserved for supererogatory prayers when alone.

Key Terms
العبادلة (al-‘Abādilah): The Companions named ‘Abdullah: Ibn Mas‘ūd, Ibn ‘Umar, Ibn ‘Abbās, and sometimes Ibn al-Zubayr.
مقام الإنبساط (maqām al-inbisāṭ): A state of expansive intimacy and comfort in supplication.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Makruh tahriman (prohibitively disliked)
D) Mubah (permissible)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits the follower's recitation behind the imam, relying on the hadith of the imam's sufficiency and the analogy of awe before a king.
