The Obligation and Minimum of Rukū' in Hanafi Fiqh
Explains the ruling, definition, and minimum bowing for rukū'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the minimum requirement for rukū' and identify the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding tranquility (tuma'nīnah).

Core Idea
The minimum rukū' is any bending customarily called bowing; tranquility is not fard in the Hanafi school.

Rukū' is a pillar of prayer, established by the Quran, Sunnah, and ijma. However, scholars differed on what exactly constitutes its minimum. This lesson examines the Hanafi definition and a significant intra-madhhab disagreement over whether tranquility (tuma'nīnah) is obligatory. Understanding this distinction clarifies when a prayer is valid or requires repetition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Rukū' is fard (obligatory) and a rukn (pillar) of prayer, established by Quran, Sunnah, and ijma.
The Qur'anic evidence is the imperative 'اركوا' (Bow) from Surah al-Hajj.
2
Analyze the minimum definition
The text defines rukū' as bowing the head with bending of the back. The minimum (fard) is any bending that is customarily and linguistically called rukū'.
The complete sunnah form involves bending until the head aligns with the buttocks, but this is not required for validity.
3
Examine the borderline case
If a person bows slightly, the ruling depends on whether the posture is closer to rukū' or to standing. If closer to rukū', it is valid; if closer to standing, it is not.
This is determined by custom and language; the back must bend, not just the head.
4
Evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute on tranquility
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold that tranquility (tuma'nīnah) is not fard; the minimum is the bending itself. Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i hold that tranquility to the extent of one tasbīh is fard.
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is the majority view that tranquility is sunnah, not fard.
5
Apply the ruling to special cases
A hunchbacked person, whose hunch already resembles rukū', gestures with his head for rukū'.
This is due to incapacity; the principle is that the person does what he can.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والسجود. (1) اركوا [ الحج : ۷۷] ولأمر النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم) به ، وللإجماع على فرضيته وركنيته، والركوع: خفض الرأس أي: طأطأة الرأس مع الانحناء بالظهر، وبه يحصل المفروض ، وأما كمالـه ليحصل الواجب والمسنون في: انحناء الصلب حتى يستوي الرأس بالعجز (۳) محاذاة، وهـو حـد الاعتدال فيه، فإن طَأطأ رأسَهُ قليلاً ولم يصل إلى حد الاعتدال، إن كان إلى الركوع الكامل أقرب منه إلى الـقـيـام جـاز ركوعه، لأنه يعد راكعاً لغة وعرفاً، لأن ما يقرب من الشيء يُعطى حكمه، وإن كان إلى القيام أقرب بأن لم يحن ظهره، بل طأطأ رأسه مع ميلان منكبيه لا يجوز ركوعه، لأنه لا يعد راكعاً بل قائماً، إذ قد يكون قيام بعض الناس كذلك كذا في شرح المنية للحلبي ولكن ضعفه في « الاختيار » حيث قال في «شرح المختار » : الركوع يتحقق بما ينطلق عليه الاسم؛ لأنه عبارة عن الانحناء. وقيل: إن كان إلى حال القيام أقرب لا يجوز، وإن كان إلى حال الركوع أقرب جاز. انتهى. وقال في الحاوي» : فرض الركوع انحناء الظهر. انتهى. وفي ( التحفة » : قدر المفروض في الركوع هو أصل الانحناء، وكذلك في السجود وهو أصل الوضع انتهى. والمراد بالأصل: تمام الانحناء لقوله عقبه أما الطمأنينة والقرار في الركوع والسجود ليس بفرض عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد، وقال أبو يوسف والشافعي: إن الفرض هو الركوع والسجود مع الطمأنينة بمقدار تسبيحة واحدة. انتهى. وهذا أيضاً يفيد أنه لا يجوز إذا كان إلى الركوع أقرب. وقال « أبو مطيع البلخي»، تلميذ أبي حنيفة، رحمه الله: لو نقص من ثلاث تسبيحات الركوع والسجود لم تجز صلاته، ذهب في ذلك إلى أنه ركن مشروع، فكان نظير القيام، فوجب أن يحله ذكر مفروض قياساً على القيام، كذا في «مجمــع الـروايــات». انتهى. والأحدب (۳) إذا بلغت حدوبته الركوع يشير برأسه للركوع، لأنه عاجز عما هو أعلى، كذا في « التجنيس والمزيد ».
And prostration. (1) Bow [Surah al-Hajj 22:77] and by the command of the Prophet (peace be upon him) to it, and by consensus on its obligation and pillar-hood. Rukū': lowering the head, i.e., bowing the head with bending of the back, and by that the obligatory is achieved. As for its perfection to achieve the obligatory and recommended: bending the spine so that the head becomes level with the buttocks in alignment, and that is the limit of moderation in it. If one lowers his head a little and does not reach the limit of moderation, if it is closer to complete rukū' than to standing, his rukū' is permissible, because he is considered a rāki' linguistically and customarily, since what is close to a thing is given its ruling. If it is closer to standing, by not bending his back, but lowering his head with a tilt of his shoulders, his rukū' is not permissible, because he is not considered rāki' but standing, as the standing of some people may be like that. Thus in Sharh al-Munyah al-Halabi, but he weakened it in al-Ikhtiyār, where he said in Sharh al-Mukhtār: Rukū' is realized by what the name applies to; because it is an expression of bending. And it was said: If it is closer to the state of standing, it is not permissible; if it is closer to the state of rukū', it is permissible. End. And he said in al-Hāwī: The obligatory of rukū' is the bending of the back. End. And in al-Tuhfah: The measure of the obligatory in rukū' is the essence of bending, and similarly in prostration it is the essence of placing. End. And what is meant by essence is complete bending, because of his statement following: As for tranquility and stillness in rukū' and sujūd, it is not obligatory according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i said: The obligatory is rukū' and sujūd with tranquility to the extent of one tasbīhah. End. This also indicates that it is not permissible if it is closer to rukū'. And Abu Muti' al-Balkhi, a student of Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, said: If one reduces from three tasbīhāt of rukū' and sujūd, his prayer is not valid. He went in that to the view that it is a prescribed pillar, so it is like standing, so it is necessary that it be occupied with an obligatory dhikr by analogy to standing. Thus in Majma' al-Riwāyāt. End. And the hunchbacked person, if his hunch reaches the level of rukū', he gestures with his head for rukū', because he is incapable of what is higher. Thus in al-Tajnīs wa al-Mazīd.
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof for the obligation of rukū' (bowing) in prayer. It opens with the Quranic evidence (Surah al-Hajj 22:77) and the command of the Prophet ﷺ, as well as consensus (ijma) that rukū' is fard and a rukn (pillar). The text then defines rukū' lexically and technically: the minimum (fard) is bowing the head with bending of the back, while the complete sunnah form involves bending the spine so that the head aligns with the buttocks. A key intra-Hanafi dispute appears: whether tranquility (tuma'nīnah) is fard. According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, tranquility is not fard; according to Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i, it is fard to the extent of one tasbīh. The text also discusses the borderline case where a person bows only slightly: if the bow is closer to the state of rukū', it is valid; if closer to standing, it is invalid. The author cites multiple authorities: al-Halabi in Sharh al-Munyah, al-Ikhtiyār, al-Hāwī, and al-Tuhfah. A minority view of Abu Muti' al-Balkhi (student of Abu Hanifa) that three tasbīhāt are necessary is noted but not adopted. Finally, the rule for a hunchbacked person is given: he gestures with his head if his hunch already resembles rukū'.

Key Terms
الركوع (al-rukū'): Bowing in prayer: lowering the head with bending of the back. The minimum (fard) is any bending that qualifies as rukū' linguistically; the complete sunnah is bending until the head aligns with the buttocks.
الطمأنينة (al-tuma'nīnah): Tranquility and stillness in prayer postures; in this passage, it is the pause after assuming the posture.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the minimum required for rukū' to be valid?
A) Bending until the head is level with the buttocks
B) Any bending of the back that is customarily called rukū'
C) Bending with three tasbīhāt
D) Bowing while maintaining tranquility for at least one tasbīh

Key Takeaway
The minimum rukū' in Hanafi fiqh is any bending of the back that is customarily called bowing; tranquility is not obligatory.

Obligation and Minimum Requirements of Sujūd
Obligation, minimal limbs, surface condition, internal dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minimum requirements for a valid prostration (sujūd) and apply the condition of 'feeling the bulk' to determine valid surfaces.

Core Idea
Prostration requires the forehead on a stable surface; the Hanafi minimum is one hand, one knee, part of one foot.

Prostration (sujūd) is a fundamental pillar of prayer, established by the Quran, Sunnah, and consensus. In this lesson, we examine what constitutes a valid sujūd: the minimal required limbs, the condition that the ground must be firm enough to 'feel the bulk', and a notable intra-Hanafi disagreement on whether both feet are required.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage clearly states that sujūd is obligatory (fard). Note the three proofs cited: Quranic command, Prophetic command, and consensus.
The ruling is fard 'ayn, a pillar of prayer.
2
Examine the proof (dalīl)
The primary proof is the Quranic imperative 'wasjudū' (prostrate) from Surah al-Hajj 22:77. In Hanafi usul, an imperative indicates obligation (wujūb) unless there is a contrary indicator.
3
List the minimal limbs for a valid sujūd
According to the chosen opinion, the minimum is: forehead (not the nose), one hand, one knee, and part of the toes of one foot. Placing less than this does not constitute sujūd.
Placing these limbs is wajib (obligatory) for validity; omitting any invalidates the prostration.
4
Understand the condition of 'feeling the bulk'
The ground must be firm enough that the forehead does not sink further when pressed. This excludes soft, unstable surfaces like loose rice or cotton unless encased in a container.
This condition ensures stability and proper performance.
5
Note intra-Hanafi disputes
There is disagreement: (1) whether both feet must be placed (Abu al-Layth) or one suffices (chosen opinion); (2) the minimum area of forehead required (Abu Hanifa: size of the nose). The text sides with the chosen opinion but acknowledges the dispute.
These are legitimate differences within the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(وَ) يفترض (السجود) لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَاسْجُدُوا [ الحج : ۷۷] ولأمر النبي به وللإجماع على فرضيته، والسجدة إنما تتحقق بـ: وضع الجبهة لا الأنف، مع وضع إحدى اليدين وإحدى الركبتين وشيء من أطراف أصابع إحدى القدمين عـلـى [ طـاهـر مـن ] الأرض، فإن لم يوجد وضع هذه الأعضاء لا تتحقق السجدة، فإذا انتقل إلى ركعة أخرى لم تكن السابقة صحيحة، وإذا وضع البعض المذكور صحت على المختار مع الكراهة، وتمام السجود بإتيانه بالواجب فيه، ويتحقق بوضع جميع اليدين والركبتين والقدمين والأنـف مـع الجبهة، كمـا ذكره المحقق وغيره، ومن اقتصر على بعض عبارات أئمتنا مما فيه مخالفة لما قاله الفقيه أبو الليث والمحققون فقد قصر، وإلى ذلك الثانية كالأولى فرضاً، وكيفيته كما سنذكره، ومن شروط صحة السجود كونه عَلَى مَا ) أي شيء (يَجِدُ) الساجد (حَجْمَهُ) وتفسير وجدان الحجم: أن الساجد لو بالغ لا يتسفّلُ رأسه أبلغ مما كان عليـه حـال الـوضـع فـلا يـصــح السجود على الأرز والذرة وبزر الكتان ونحوه لعدم استقرار الجبهة عليها إلا أن يكون في جوالق (1) ونحوها؛ لأنه يجد الحجم حينئذ، وكذا الحشيش والتبن والقطن والثلج، وكل محشو، كالفرش والوسائد إن وجد حجم الأرض بكبسه صح وإلا فلا، والأرز والدخن" لا يصح عليهما، لأن حبتهما لملاستها ولزازتها لا يستقر بعضها على بعض، فلا يمكن انتهاء التسفل فيها واستقرار الجبهة عليها، (وَ) الحنطة والشعير ( تستقر عليه فيجوز السجود؛ لأن حباتهما يستقر بعضها على بعض لخشونة ورخاوة في أجسامها، فتستقر عليها (جبهته)، الجبهة: اسم لما يصيب الأرض ممـا فوق الحاجبين إلى قصاص الشعر حالة السجود، وعرفها بعضهم بأنها ما اكتنفه الجبينان والسجود في اللغة: يطلق على طأطأة الرأس والانحناء والخضوع والتواضع، والميــل كـسـجـدت النخلة: مالت، والتحية كالسجود لآدم تكرمة له كذا في ضياء الحلوم». وفي الشريعة: وضع بعض الوجه مما لا سخرية يجوز، وإلا فلا. وأبو حنيفة يقول: ينبغي أن يضع من جبهته بمقدار الأنف حتى يجوز وإلا فلا ، ووضع جميع أطراف الجبهة ليس بشرط
(And) prostration is obligatory, by His statement: 'Prostrate' [Surah al-Hajj 22:77], and by the command of the Prophet ﷺ, and by consensus on its obligation. Prostration is only realized by: placing the forehead, not the nose, along with placing one hand, one knee, and part of the tips of the toes of one foot on pure ground. If these limbs are not placed, the prostration is not realized. So if he moves to another rak'ah, the previous [rak'ah] is not valid. If he places the mentioned parts, it is valid according to the chosen opinion, though disliked. The complete prostration is achieved by performing what is obligatory in it, and it is realized by placing both hands, both knees, both feet, and the nose along with the forehead, as stated by al-Muhaqqiq and others. Whoever confines himself to some statements of our imams that contradict what al-Faqih Abu al-Layth and the verifying scholars said has fallen short. To that, he pointed in al-Fatāwā al-Sughrā where he said: Placing both feet on the ground during prostration is obligatory; if one places only one foot, it is permissible. Then he said: The apparent from those narrations is what al-Faqih Abu al-Layth adopted. End. We will mention it shortly. The second prostration is like the first in obligation, and its modality as we will mention. Among the conditions for the validity of prostration is that it be on something that the prostrator feels its bulk. The interpretation of feeling the bulk: that if the prostrator presses hard, his head does not sink further than what was upon placement. So prostration is not valid on rice, millet, flaxseed, and the like, due to the lack of stability of the forehead on them, unless they are in a sack etc., because then the bulk is felt. Similarly, grass, straw, cotton, snow, and everything stuffed, like mattresses and pillows: if the bulk of the ground is felt by pressing, it is valid; otherwise not. Rice and millet are not valid because their grains, due to smoothness and stickiness, do not settle on each other, so it is impossible for the head to sink and the forehead to be stable on them. Wheat and barley, however, are stable, so prostration is permissible on them because their grains settle on each other due to roughness and softness in their bodies, so the forehead is stable on them. The forehead: the name for what touches the ground from above the eyebrows to the hairline during prostration. Some defined it as what is between the two temples. Prostration in language: used for lowering the head, bending, humility, submission, and inclining; e.g., the date palm 'sajadat' meaning it bent; and greeting, like the prostration to Adam as an honor. Thus in Diyā' al-Hulūm. In sacred law: placing part of the face that is not mockery. So the cheek, chin, temple, and front of the head are excluded; prostration on them is not permissible, even if there is an excuse, because substitutes are not established by opinion. So with an excuse, gesturing with the head is obligatory. If he places his forehead on a small stone: if he places most of the forehead on the ground, it is permissible; otherwise no. Abu Hanifa says: He should place from his forehead the equivalent of the nose so that it is permissible, otherwise no. Placing all the edges of the forehead is not a condition.
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof for the obligation of sujūd (prostration) in prayer, citing the same Quranic verse as rukū' (Surah al-Hajj 22:77), the Prophet's command, and consensus. It then details the minimal requirements for a valid prostration: placing the forehead (not the nose) on the ground, along with one hand, one knee, and part of the toes of one foot. The text notes a difference: if one places only the minimum, the prostration is valid but makrūh (disliked). The complete sunnah form involves placing all limbs: both hands, both knees, both feet, and the nose along with the forehead. The passage emphasizes that the condition of 'feeling the bulk' of the ground is necessary: the forehead must be stable so that if one presses down, it does not sink further. This excludes soft substances like rice, millet, cotton, snow, etc., unless they are in a container that provides stability. Wheat and barley are acceptable because their grains interlock. The definition of forehead is given as the area between the eyebrows and hairline; prostration on the cheek, chin, temple, or top of the head is invalid. An intra-Hanafi dispute is noted: Abu al-Layth (and others) hold that placing both feet is obligatory, while the chosen opinion allows one foot. Abu Hanifa's view on the amount of forehead required is also mentioned: one should place at least the size of the nose.

Key Terms
السجود (al-sujūd): Prostration: placing the forehead (and in complete form, other limbs) on the ground with humility.
الجبهة (al-jabhah): The forehead: the area between the eyebrows and the hairline.
وجدان الحجم (wijdān al-ḥajm): Feeling the bulk: the condition that the surface is firm enough that the forehead does not sink further when pressed.

Key Takeaway
Sujūd is obligatory upon every praying person; the minimum valid prostration requires the forehead (at least nose-sized), one hand, one knee, and part of one foot on a stable ground where the bulk is felt.

Condition of the Place of Sujood: Wijdan al-Hajm
Definition and conditions for valid prostration: place of sujood must have volume.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the condition of 'finding volume' (wijdan al-hajm) for prostration and determine which surfaces satisfy it.

Core Idea
For sujood to be valid, the ground must be solid enough that the forehead does not sink under pressure.

Prostration is a pillar of prayer, and its validity depends not only on the act itself but also on the place where it is performed. The Hanafi school specifies that the surface must be firm enough to support the forehead without sinking. This condition is called wijdan al-hajm. In this lesson, we examine how this is defined and applied to different materials.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
The passage states that a condition of prostration is that the place must be something on which the prostrator 'finds its volume'. This is the key condition for validity.
The phrase 'على ما يجد حجمه' is the core requirement.
2
Understand the interpretation
The interpretation: if the prostrator exerts pressure, his head should not sink further than the initial placement. This distinguishes firm from compressible surfaces.
The text says: 'لو بالغ لا يتسفل رأسه أبلغ مما كان عليه حال الوضع'.
3
Apply to substances
Use the interpretation to test surfaces: rice and millet are invalid because their grains are smooth and do not stack; wheat and barley are valid because they are rough and interlock. Soft materials like cotton, snow, and stuffed items are invalid unless pressed to find the ground beneath.
The passage explicitly gives examples – classify them correctly.
4
Define the forehead
The forehead (jabhah) is defined as the area from above the eyebrows to the hairline. Prostration on other parts of the face (cheek, chin, temple) is invalid.
This definition is crucial: the 'face' in sujood is limited to this area.
5
Determine the minimum amount
Abu Hanifa holds that at least the size of the nose from the forehead must be placed; other views (mufta bihi) consider any portion sufficient as long as most of the forehead touches the ground (e.g., on a small stone).
The passage ends by settling on the lenient view as the chosen one.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

On something that finds its volume, and his forehead rests upon it. If these limbs are not placed, the prostration is not realized. If he moves to another rak'ah, the previous one is not valid. If he places some of the mentioned limbs, it is valid according to the chosen view with dislike. Complete prostration is by performing its obligatory aspects, and it is realized by placing both hands, both knees, both feet, and the nose with the forehead, as mentioned by the muhaqqiq and others. Whoever restricts himself to some statements of our imams that contradict what Abu al-Layth and the muhaqqiqs said has fallen short. To that, the author of al-Fatawa al-Sughra pointed out, saying: Placing both feet on the ground during prostration is fard; if he places one without the other, it is permissible. Then he said: The apparent from those narrations is what Abu al-Layth held, end. We will mention it soon. The second prostration, like the first, is fard, and its modality is as we will mention. Among the conditions of the validity of prostration is that it be on something on which the prostrator finds its volume. The interpretation of finding volume: if the prostrator strains, his head does not sink further than its state when placed. So prostration is not valid on rice, millet, linseed, and the like because the forehead does not rest on them, unless in a sack or the like because then he finds the volume. Similarly, hay, straw, cotton, snow, and every stuffed thing like mattresses and pillows: if by pressing he finds the volume of the ground, it is valid; otherwise not. Rice and millet are not valid on them because their grains, due to smoothness and stickiness, do not rest on one another, so one cannot sink and rest the forehead on them. Wheat and barley do rest on them, so prostration is permissible because their grains rest on each other due to roughness and softness in their bodies, so his forehead rests on them. Al-jabhah (forehead) is a name for what touches the ground from above the eyebrows to the hairline during prostration. Some defined it as what is flanked by the two temples. Sujood in language means lowering the head, bowing, humility, submission, and inclination – as in ‘the date palm prostrated’ meaning it inclined – and greeting, like the prostration to Adam as an honor. In Sharia: placing part of the face that is not marred by mockery. Thus the cheek, chin, temple, and front of the head are excluded; prostration on them is not permissible, even with an excuse, because alternatives are not established by opinion. With an excuse, pointing with the head is obligatory. If he places his forehead on a small stone: if he places most of the forehead on the ground, it is permissible; otherwise not. Abu Hanifa says: He should place from his forehead the amount of the nose so that it is permissible; otherwise not. Placing all of the edges of the forehead is not a condition.
Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This passage is a definition_ruling that explains the conditions for a valid prostration in prayer. It clarifies that prostration must be performed on a surface that 'finds its volume', meaning it is solid or firm enough that the forehead rests without sinking further. The author provides examples: rice and millet are invalid because their smooth grains do not stack, while wheat and barley are valid due to their roughness. The definition of the forehead (jabhah) is given from the eyebrows to the hairline, and prostration must involve part of the face excluding the cheeks, chin, and temples. The passage also addresses the ruling on a small stone: if most of the forehead touches the ground, it is valid. Abu Hanifa's view is that the area of the forehead placed should be at least the size of the nose. Note that touching all edges of the forehead is not obligatory.

Key Terms
وجدان الحجم (wijdan al-hajm): The condition that the surface is firm enough that the forehead can rest and not sink further when the prostrator presses down.
الجبهة (al-jabhah): The area of the face from above the eyebrows to the hairline, which must be placed on the ground during prostration.
السجود (al-sujood): In Sharia: placing part of the face that is not marred by mockery (i.e., the forehead and nose) on the ground with humility.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, which of the following is NOT valid for prostration because the forehead cannot rest on it?
A) Wheat grains
B) Barley grains
C) Rice grains
D) A small stone

Key Takeaway
A valid prostration requires that the surface be solid enough to support the forehead without sinking; this is the condition of wijdan al-hajm.

Ruling on Sujood on Palm or Garment Edge: Permissibility with Conditions
States the permissibility of sujood on palm or garment with condition and proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sujood on the palm or garment edge, identify the condition of purity, and explain the proof from the Prophet's practice.

Core Idea
Sujood on palm or garment edge is valid but disliked without an excuse; the place of placement must be pure.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah explains the Hanafi position regarding sujood on one's palm or the edge of the garment. While the prayer remains valid, the act is considered disliked (makruh) when done without a valid reason. The author cites hadith evidence from the Prophet's practice and clarifies the essential condition of purity of the part of the palm or garment that touches the ground.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being discussed and the hukm (ruling) according to the Hanafi school. The act is sujood on the palm of the hand or the edge of the garment. The ruling is that the prayer is valid (sahih) but the action is disliked (makruh) without a valid excuse.
Dislike here is tanzihi (lesser dislike), not tahrimi (prohibitory).
2
Locate the condition
Find the condition of purity (ṭahāra) required for the place of sujood. The text states: 'if the place of his placement is pure.' This refers to the part of the palm or the garment edge that contacts the ground.
The condition applies to the actual surface that the forehead touches, not necessarily the entire garment.
3
Examine the proof
Look at the hadith evidence cited from Ibn Abbas and Anas. They report that the Prophet and companions used the excess of their garments to protect from extreme heat or cold during sujood. This establishes permissibility.
The hadith is narrated by multiple sources, including the six major collections, giving it strong support.
4
Understand the dislike
Why is it disliked without an excuse? The text compares it to sujood on the coiled part of the turban. The underlying principle is that direct contact with the ground is the sunnah, and creating a barrier without necessity is departing from the sunnah.
The dislike is removed when there is a valid reason such as extreme heat or cold.
5
Note the intra-school debate
The text discusses a difference: some allow placing the garment over impurity and prostrating on it, but al-Kamal ibn al-Humam rejects this, affirming that the sleeve must be pure because sujood is actually on the ground.
The preferred view is that the sleeve must be pure, as it is part of the body that prostrates.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو على كفّه، أو طرف ثوبِهِ، إِنْ طَهُرَ مَحَلَّ وضعِهِ، وسجدَ وجوباً بما صَلُبَ منْ أَنفَهُ... بالإجماع، (و) يصح السجود و(لَوْ) كان على كفّه :أي: الساجد في الصحيح، (أو) كان السجود على (طرفِ ثَوبِهِ) أي: الساجد، ويكره بغير عذر، كالسجود على كور عمامته، لما رواه ابن أبي شيبة عن ابن عباس : ( أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم صلى في ثوب واحد يتقي بفضولـه حـر الأرض وبردَهَا ) ورواه أحمد وأبو يعلى الموصلي في آخرين، وفي الكتب الستة عن أنس قال: « كُنَّـا مـع النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فيضع أحدنا طرف الثّوبِ في شدّةِ الحرِّ في مكان السجودِ ) كذا في «البرهان» و«معراج الدراية» ( إِنْ طَهُرَ مَحَلُّ وضعِهِ) أي: الكف أو الطرف على الأصح، لأن السجود على الأرض لا عـلـى الـكـم، والكم من جملة المساجد كَيدَهِ كما في ( الدراية» و«الفتح» . وقيل : يجوز أن يضع طرف ثوبـه عـلـى نجس فيسجد عليه، وصححه المرغيناني، وليس بشيء، قاله الكمال، وقد نقله في « الدراية» عن « مبسوط» الإسبيجابي أيضاً، وقال الأصح أنه يجوز لأنه ساجد على الكم، أو الذي وضعه علـى النجس حقيقة وهو أي: الكم طاهر. انتهى. وقد نبه الكمال على أنه ليس بشيء.
And even if on his palm or the edge of his garment, if the place of his placement is pure, and he prostrates obligatorily with the hard part of his nose... by consensus. Sujood is valid even if on his palm (of the prostrator in the correct view) or on the edge of his garment (of the prostrator). It is disliked without an excuse, like sujood on the coiled part of his turban. This is because of what Ibn Abi Shaybah narrated from Ibn Abbas: that the Prophet صلى الله عليه وسلم prayed in a single garment, using its excess to protect himself from the heat and cold of the ground. Ahmad and Abu Ya'la al-Mawsili also narrated it, and it is in the six books on the authority of Anas: 'We were with the Prophet صلى الله عليه وسلم, and one of us would place the edge of his garment (on the ground) in severe heat as a place for sujood.' Thus, in al-Burhan and Ma'raj al-Dirayah. If the place of his placement is pure, meaning the palm or the edge, according to the most correct view, because sujood is on the ground, not on the sleeve, and the sleeve is among the limbs that perform prostration like his hand, as in al-Dirayah and al-Fath. Some say: he may place the edge of his garment on impurity and prostrate on it. Al-Marghinani declared it sound, but al-Kamal said it is nothing. Al-Dirayah also transmitted from the Mabsoot of al-Isbijaabi that the correct view is that it is permissible because he is prostrating on the sleeve, and the sleeve is pure. Al-Kamal stated that it is nothing.
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding sujood on one's palm or garment edge. The Hanafi position is that it is valid in the prayer (sahih) but disliked (makruh) without a valid excuse. The proof comes from hadiths: Ibn Abbas and Anas report that the Prophet and his companions used the edge of their garments to shield from extreme heat or cold during sujood. The text also discusses a key condition: the place of placement (the palm or sleeve) must be pure. There is a difference of opinion: some scholars allow placing the garment over impurity and prostrating on it, but al-Kamal ibn al-Humam rejects this, saying the correct view is that the sleeve must be pure because sujood is actually on the ground, not the sleeve. The obligatory placement of the hard part of the nose (the bone) is also affirmed by consensus.

Key Terms
الكف (al-kaff): The palm of the hand; the text discusses sujood directly on the palm.
طرف الثوب (taraf al-thawb): The edge or end of the garment that is used to cover the ground for sujood.
الكَمّ (al-kamm): The sleeve of the garment; the text distinguishes between sujood on the ground vs. on the sleeve itself.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Permissible (ja'iz)
B) Disliked (makruh)
C) Forbidden (haram)
D) Recommended (sunnah)

Key Takeaway
Sujood on palm or garment edge is valid (sahih) but disliked (makruh) without an excuse, provided the place is pure, and the proof from the Prophet's practice in extreme conditions supports this allowance.

Dispute on Sujood on Knees: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Presents the dispute regarding the validity of sujood on one's knees, with Hanafi and Shafi'i positions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the relied-upon Hanafi ruling on sujood on the knees and explain how the early Hanafi view differed, and how the later position aligns with Shafi'i while allowing gesture for the excused.

Core Idea
Sujood on knees is invalid; with excuse, gesture suffices.

This passage explores a difference within the Hanafi school and between Hanafis and Shafi'is regarding sujood on the knees. While early Hanafis allowed it, the later relied-upon view declares it invalid. Understanding this development clarifies how the school refines rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the core dispute
The act is sujood (prostration) performed on the knees. The dispute is whether this fulfills the obligation of sujood.
Sujood normally requires placing the forehead on the ground.
2
State the early Hanafi position (al-Bazdawi)
Al-Bazdawi is reported to have said that sujood on one knee (or hands/sleeves) is permissible, contrary to al-Shafi'i.
This view did not become the standard.
3
State the later Hanafi position (al-Khulasah, al-Kamal)
Al-Khulasah states sujood on knees is not permissible with or without an excuse. With excuse, gesture (ima') suffices.
Al-Kamal adds that the knee's edge cannot cover the obligatory area of the forehead.
4
Identify the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i opposes permissibility altogether, holding that sujood must be on the forehead and nose.
No alternative gesture is mentioned for Shafi'is.
5
Determine the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
Early Hanafis allowed sujood on knees; later Hanafis and Shafi'is do not. Hanafis uniquely permit gesture as an alternative when excused.
This shows how ikhtilaf is resolved to a final fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تنبيه: قال في « الدراية » : ذكر البزدوي : لو سجد على إحدى ركبتيه أو يديه أو كميه جاز، خلافاً للشافعي رحمه الله ، وقال الحسن: الأصح أنه إذا سجد على فخذيه أو ركبتيه بعــذر جاز وإلا فلا. انتهى. وفي ( الخلاصة لو سجد على فخذيه إن كان بغير عذر المختار أنه لا يجوز، وإن كان بعـذر المختار أنه يجوز، ولو سجد على ركبتيه لا يجوز بعذر أو بغير عذر، لكن إن كان بعذر يكفيه الإيماء. انتهى. وكذا ظاهر عبارة الزيلعي فقد علمت الخلاف في جواز السجود على الركبة، وقد نقل الكمال كلام ( الخلاصة » فقال : ولو سجد على ركبتيه لا يجوز بعذر أو بغير عذر، ثم زاد الكمال فيه : ولم نعلم فيه خلافاً. وكان عدم الخلاف فيه لكون السجود يقع على حرف الركبة، وهـــو لا يأخذ قدر الواجب من الجبهة، وفي ( التجنيس » : لو سجد على حجر صغير إن كان أكثر الجبهة على الأرض جاز وإلا فلا. انتهى كلام الكمال، فيجاب عنه بما نقلناه من الخلاف فليتأمل.
Note: In al-Dirayah, al-Bazdawi said: If he prostrates on one of his knees or his hands or his sleeves, it is permissible, contrary to al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him. Al-Hasan said: The most correct is that if he prostrates on his thighs or his knees with an excuse, it is permissible; otherwise not. End. In al-Khulasah: If he prostrates on his thighs, if without an excuse, the chosen view is that it is not permissible; if with an excuse, the chosen view is that it is permissible. And if he prostrates on his knees, it is not permissible with or without an excuse, but if with an excuse, gesture (ima') suffices him. End. Likewise, the apparent wording of al-Zayla'i: you have known the difference of opinion regarding the permissibility of prostration on the knee. Al-Kamal transmitted the statement from al-Khulasah and said: If he prostrates on his knees, it is not permissible with or without an excuse. Then al-Kamal added: And we do not know of any disagreement in this. The absence of disagreement is because the prostration falls on the edge of the knee, and it does not take the obligatory amount of the forehead. In al-Tajnis: If he prostrates on a small stone, if most of the forehead is on the ground, it is permissible; otherwise not. End of al-Kamal's statement. He responded to it with what we have transmitted of the difference, so let it be considered.
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This passage is an inter_madhhab_dispute about the validity of sujood on one's knees. Al-Bazdawi (Hanafi) is reported to have said that sujood on the knees, hands, or sleeves is permissible, contrary to al-Shafi'i. However, other Hanafi authorities qualify this: Al-Hasan says the most correct is that it is permissible only with an excuse; otherwise not. Al-Khulasah distinguishes between thighs and knees: sujood on thighs is permissible with an excuse, but on knees it is never permissible; with an excuse, one should only gesture (ima'). Al-Kamal ibn al-Humam asserts there is no disagreement that sujood on the knees is invalid because it touches only the edge of the knee and does not cover the obligatory amount of the forehead. The passage ends with a note that the difference of opinion should be considered.

Key Terms
الركبة (al-rukbah): The kneecap; the text discusses whether sujood can be performed on this part of the body.
الإيماء (al-ima'): Gesture; a substitute for sujood when one cannot perform it normally due to excuse, by bowing the head slightly.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position as stated in al-Khulasah, what is the ruling on sujood on the knees without an excuse?
A) Permissible (ja'iz)
B) Disliked (makruh)
C) Not permissible (la yajuz)
D) Gesture suffices

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, sujood on the knees is invalid; with an excuse, one must gesture instead.

Prostration on Palm or Garment Edge: Validity and Dislike
Explains ruling and conditions for prostrating on palm or garment edge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on prostrating on the palm or garment edge, explain the proof from hadith, and identify the intra-Hanafi dispute on impurity under the garment.

Core Idea
Prostration on palm or garment edge is valid but disliked without excuse; impurity underneath is debated.

In this lesson, we examine a commentary from Imdad al-Fattah that clarifies a common scenario: prostrating on one's palm or the edge of one's garment. The passage affirms validity while noting dislike (karahah) when done without excuse. It then delves into conditions of purity and presents internal Hanafi disagreement on whether placing the garment over impurity affects prostration. You will learn the operative ruling and the proof from the Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being discussed (prostration on palm or garment edge) and identify the hukm: it is valid (sahih) but disliked (makruh tanzihi) without a valid excuse.
The text explicitly says 'yajuz wa yukrah' – permissible but disliked.
2
Locate the dalil and its wajh al-dalalah
Identify the proof cited: the hadith of Ibn Abbas and Anas showing the Prophet and Companions used the garment edge to shield from heat/cold. Analyse how this indicates permissibility but also implies dislike when done without necessity.
The hadith demonstrate permissibility in a context of need, implying dislike when no need exists.
3
Trace the condition of purity
Note the condition that the place of placement (palm or garment edge) must be pure. Understand the rationale: prostration is directly on that part, not the ground underneath.
The commentator clarifies that the sleeve is part of the prostration organs (masajid).
4
Analyse the intra-Hanafi dispute on impurity
Examine the disagreement between al-Marghinani (permits placing garment on impurity) and al-Kamal (rejects). Understand each position's basis and which view is relied upon (mufta bihi).
Also consider the related dispute on prostrating on knee/thigh mentioned later in the passage.

And if on his palm or the edge of his garment, if the place of placing it is pure, and he prostrates obligatorily with the hard part of his nose... by consensus. (And) prostration is valid even if on his palm, meaning the prostrator in the correct view, or if prostration is on the edge of his garment, meaning the prostrator, and it is disliked without excuse, like prostrating on the fold of his turban. Due to what Ibn Abi Shaybah narrated from Ibn Abbas that the Prophet prayed in one garment, protecting himself with its extra from the heat and cold of the ground. And Ahmad and Abu Ya'la al-Mawsili and others narrated it, and in the six books from Anas: 'We were with the Prophet; one of us would place the edge of the garment in severe heat on the place of prostration.' (Thus in al-Burhan and Miraj al-Dirayah.) (If the place of its placing is pure) meaning the palm or the edge according to the most correct, because prostration is on the ground, not on the sleeve, and the sleeve is part of the prostration organs like the hand (as in al-Dirayah and al-Fath). And it was said: it is permissible to place the edge of his garment on impurity and prostrate on it, and al-Marghinani affirmed it. But al-Kamal said: It is nothing. And he reported in al-Dirayah from al-Asbijabi's Mabsut also, and he said the most correct is that it is permissible because he is prostrating on the sleeve, and that which he placed on impurity in reality is the sleeve, and it (the sleeve) is pure. End. And al-Kamal pointed out that it is nothing. Caution: It was said in al-Dirayah: al-Bazdawi mentioned: If he prostrates on one of his knees or hands or sleeves, it is permissible, contrary to al-Shafi'i. And al-Hasan said: The most correct is that if he prostrates on his thighs or knees with an excuse, it is permissible, otherwise no. End. And in al-Khulasah: If he prostrates on his thighs without excuse, the chosen position is that it is not permissible; with excuse, the chosen position is that it is permissible. If he prostrates on his knees, it is not permissible with or without excuse, but if with excuse, gesture (ima) suffices him. End. And similar is the apparent wording of al-Zayla'i. You have known the disagreement on the permissibility of prostrating on the knee. Al-Kamal quoted al-Khulasah's statement and said: If he prostrates on his knees, it is not permissible with or without excuse. Then al-Kamal added: We do not know any disagreement in this. The lack of disagreement is because prostration occurs on the edge of the knee, which does not take the obligatory measure from the forehead. It is responded with what we have reported of disagreement, so ponder.
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on a matn ruling about prostration conditions. It opens by stating the ruling: prostration on one's palm or garment edge is valid (sahih) but disliked (makruh) without a valid excuse. The dislike is akin to prostrating on the fold of the turban. The proof cited are two hadith: one from Ibn Abbas showing the Prophet used the edge of his garment to shield from heat/cold, demonstrating permissibility, and another from Anas that the Companions would place the garment edge on the ground during severe heat for prostration. The commentator then addresses the condition that the place of placement must be pure. He notes that according to the most correct view, the purity requirement applies to the garment sleeve itself, not the ground underneath, because the actual prostration is on the sleeve (which is part of the body's prostration organs). There follows an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether it is permissible to place the garment edge on impurity. Some, like al-Marghinani, affirmed it, but al-Kamal rejected this as baseless, arguing the sleeve is pure and the person is prostrating on the sleeve, not the impurity. The text then includes a 'tanbih' (caution) covering rulings on prostrating on other body parts like knees, thighs, and hands. It reports al-Bazdawi's view that prostrating on one knee, hand, or sleeve is permissible, and that this differs from Shafi'i's position. Al-Hasan's view is that it is only permissible with excuse. Al-Khulasah distinguishes between thigh and knee: prostrating on the thigh is permissible only with excuse, while on the knee it is never permissible even with excuse—ima (gesture) suffices instead. Al-Kamal asserts there is no disagreement on the knee's invalidity because the knee's edge does not cover the obligatory area of the forehead. The passage ends with a reminder to ponder the differences.

Key Terms
كره (karaha): Legal dislike (karahah tanzihiyyah) short of prohibition; the act is valid but discouraged.
مساجد (masajid): Parts of the body on which prostration is placed (plural of masjid).
إيماء (ima'): Gesture indication; a minimal substitute for prostration when actual prostration is not possible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on prostrating on the edge of one's garment without a valid excuse?
A) It is invalid and the prayer must be repeated.
B) It is valid and not disliked.
C) It is valid but disliked (makruh).
D) It is obligatory to avoid it.

Key Takeaway
Prostration on palm or garment edge is valid but disliked without excuse; the purity of the prostration place is conditioned on the barrier, not the ground.

Prostration: The Nose as a Wajib Supplement to the Forehead
Ruling with proof on the status of the nose in prostration.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on prostration on the nose and forehead, distinguish between shart sihha and shart kamal, and explain the Hanafi proof and intra-madhhab dispute.

Core Idea
Prostration requires the forehead; the nose is wajib as a supplement, not a substitute — omitting it without excuse renders the prayer deficient.

This lesson examines a key ruling on the posture of sujud: must one place the nose on the ground, or is the forehead sufficient? The Hanafi school holds that the hard part of the nose is wajib (obligatory) but as a condition of perfection (shart kamal), not a condition of validity (shart sihha). We will also explore an important intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf where Imam Abu Hanifa retracted his original view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly does the text rule about placing the nose in prostration? It states 'he prostrates obligatorily with that which is hard of his nose' — thus the hard part (not the tip) is wajib.
The act is placing the hard part of the nose on the ground during sujud.
2
Understand the distinction: shart sihha vs shart kamal
The commentator notes that prostration on the nose is 'wajib' but has no role in validity conditions — it is a 'shart kamal' (condition of perfection). If omitted, the prayer is valid but deficient, requiring sajdah sahw.
Contrast with the forehead, which is a pillar (rukn); its omission invalidates the sujud.
3
Locate the dalil
The hadith 'I have been commanded to prostrate on seven bones, on the forehead...' proves that the forehead is essential. The nose is not mentioned as an independent part but as an adjunct.
The hadith is cited as evidence that confining to the nose alone is impermissible.
4
Trace the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifa initially held that placing only the nose tip (arnabah) invalidates prostration; later he returned (raja'a) to the view of his two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) that it is impermissible to restrict to the nose without an excuse.
This ruju' is part of a broader set of returns regarding Persian in prayer etc.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position (asahh) is that confining to the nose alone is not valid unless there is an excuse on the forehead. The madhhab follows Abu Hanifa's final agreed view.
Thus, the operative ruling: forehead must be placed; nose is wajib as a supplement.

And he prostrates obligatorily with that which is hard of his nose, because its tip is not a place of prostration. Shaykh al-Islam said: He mentioned the nose, and it is a name (1) meaning that which is on his forehead, for it is valid with dislike without excuse. But if it was only on his head and he prostrated on it, confining himself, and nothing of his forehead touches the ground, then it is not valid, due to lack of prostration on its place. And al-kur (with fath al-kaf) is like a garment from the folds of the turban. T. (2) Ahmad transmitted it in his Musnad... (3) Abu Dawud transmitted it... (page 236) [PAGE_238] When it became hard, it is evidence that prostration on the tip does not suffice him, and that he must place what is hard of it. From Abu Hanifa: When he places the tip of the nose, it is not permissible; only if he places the bone of his nose (it is permissible). Thus in al-Dirayah. And since prostration on the nose is wajib, it has no role in the conditions of validity—rather it is a condition of perfection—as we will mention that joining the nose to the forehead is wajib, he addressed that by saying: (And) he prostrates (with his forehead, and confining oneself to the nose is not valid) in the most correct view except due to an excuse on the forehead. Because the most correct is that Imam al-A'zam returned to the agreement of his two companions regarding the impermissibility of commencing prayer in Persian for one not incapable of Arabic, and impermissibility of reciting in Persian etc. for one not incapable, and impermissibility of confining prostration to the nose without excuse in the forehead. The reason for impermissibility of confining to the nose is what we narrated of his saying: 'I have been commanded to prostrate on seven bones, on the forehead... etc.' And in another narration: 'The servant is commanded to prostrate on seven limbs' — the hadith in al-Burhan.
Source pages p. 238

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn ruling that a person must prostrate with the hard part of the nose (not just the soft tip). The commentator explains that the nose tip (ar-nabah) is not a valid place for prostration; rather, the hard bone part must be placed. He then notes that prostrating on the nose is wajib but it is not a condition of validity (shart) but a condition of perfection (shart kamal). This means that if one omits the nose but still places the forehead, the prostration is valid but deficient; compensation (sajdah sahw) may be required. However, one cannot confine prostration solely to the nose; the forehead must also be on the ground, except if there is an excuse (e.g., a wound on the forehead). The commentator mentions an important intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Imam Abu Hanifa's original view was that placing the nose tip is invalid; only placing the nose bone suffices. Later, he returned (ruju') to the position of his two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), adopting the ruling that confining to the nose alone (without excuse) is not permissible. This return is placed alongside similar returns regarding using Persian in prayer. The proof for the ruling is the famous hadith: 'I have been commanded to prostrate on seven bones: the forehead...' indicating the forehead is essential. Thus the nose is not a substitute but a complement.

Key Terms
أرنبة (arnabah): The soft tip of the nose; not a valid place of prostration.
شرط كمال (shart kamal): A condition that perfects the act but does not affect validity; omission requires compensation (sajdah sahw) but does not invalidate.
رجع (raja'a): The act of returning to a previous position; here Abu Hanifa retracted his original view to agree with his companions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position presented, what is the ruling on prostrating solely on the nose tip (arnabah) without any excuse?
A) It is valid and sufficient
B) It is valid but disliked
C) It is not permissible
D) It is recommended

Key Takeaway
The hard part of the nose is wajib in prostration but only as a perfection condition; the forehead remains essential as a pillar.

Salah — Prayer

Conditions of Sujood: Height, Hands, Knees, and Feet
Lists conditions for valid prostration with proof from hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for valid prostration and identify when a height difference invalidates the prostration.

Core Idea
Prostration is invalid if the forehead is more than half a cubit above the feet.

Prostration (sujood) is a pillar of prayer with specific conditions derived from the Sunnah. This passage from Sharh Nur al-Idah explains two key conditions: the height difference between the place of prostration and the feet, and which parts of the body must touch the ground. Understanding these ensures your prayer is valid according to the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first condition
The text begins with the requirement that the place of prostration (forehead) must not be more than half a cubit higher than the feet. Less than half a cubit is excused.
Half a cubit is approximately 30-36 cm.
2
Note the exception for crowding
If there is extreme crowding (zahma), one may prostrate on the back of another person who is in the same prayer. Otherwise, it invalidates the prostration.
This is a dispensation for necessity, e.g., in Hajj or dense congregations.
3
Identify the second condition – hands and knees
At least one hand and one knee must be placed on the ground. The correct view (mufta bihi) is that one each suffices, though both may be considered more complete.
The hadith mentions 'hands' and 'knees' (plural), but the Hanafi school interprets the plural as indicating the genus, so a single instance fulfills the command.
4
Identify the third condition – feet
Some part of the toes (inner side facing qibla) must touch the ground. Placing the top of the foot (zahir al-qadam) is insufficient.
The hadith specifies 'tips of the feet' (atraf al-qadamayn).
5
Locate the dalil
The proof is the well-known hadith: 'I have been commanded to prostrate on seven bones: the forehead, the hands, the knees, and the tips of the feet.' This shows these parts are essential for valid sujood.
The hadith is mutawatir in meaning, agreed upon by Bukhari and Muslim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَ) من شروط صحة السجود (عدم ارتفاع محل السجودِ عن موضع القدمين بأكثر من نصف ذراع) ليتحقق صفة الساجد، والارتفاع القليل لا يضر، (وإن زاد على نصف ذراع لم يَجُزِ السجود)، أي: لم يقع معتداً به، كما في « الدراية» فـإن أتـي بـغـيـره معتبراً صحت، وإن لم يأت به حتى خرج من صلاته فسدت (إلا) أن يكون ذلك (الزحمة، سـجـد فـيـهـا عـلـى ظَهْرٍ مُصَلِّ صلاته للضرورة، فإن لم يكن المسجود عليه مصلياً أصلاً، أو كــان فـي غـيـر صــلاة الساجد عليه، لا يصح السجود، وقيل: إنما يجوز إذا كان سجود الثاني على الأرض كما في «الدراية». (وَ) من شروط صحة السجود (وَضعُ) إحدى اليَدَيْنِ (و) إحدى الرُّكْبَتَينِ في الصَّحِيح) كما قدمناه ولـمــا رويناه (۳) (وَ) وَضعُ ( شيءٍ مِنْ أصَابِعِ الرِّجْلَينِ) موجهاً بباطنه نحو القبلة (حالة السجودِ عـلـى الأرض، ولا يكفي لصحة السجود (وضعُ ظاهر القدم) لأنه ليس محله لقوله : ( أُمِرْتُ أنْ أسْجُدَ عَلَى سَبْعَةِ أَعْظُم عَلَى الْجَبْهَةِ وَالْيَدَيْنِ وَالرُّكْبَتَيْنِ وَأَطْرَافِ الْقَدَمَيْنِ ) متفق عليه.
And from the conditions of valid prostration: (the place of prostration not being higher than the place of the feet by more than half a cubit), so that the attribute of the prostrator is realized. Slight height does not harm. (If it exceeds half a cubit, prostration is not permissible), i.e., it does not count. As in al-Dirayah: If he performs another prostration that is valid, it becomes correct; if he does not perform it until he leaves his prayer, it is invalid. (Except) if that is (due to crowding; he prostrates on the back of someone praying in his prayer out of necessity. If the one prostrated upon is not praying at all, or is in a prayer other than that of the prostrator, then prostration is not valid. It is said: it is only permissible if the second person's prostration is on the ground, as in al-Dirayah). (And) from the conditions of valid prostration: (placing one hand and one knee) according to the correct view, as we have mentioned and as we narrated. (And) placing (something of the toes of both feet), directing their inner side towards the qibla, in the state of prostration on the ground. Placing the upper side of the foot (zahir al-qadam) is not sufficient for valid prostration because it is not the place, due to his saying: 'I have been commanded to prostrate on seven bones: the forehead, the hands, the knees, and the tips of the feet.' (Agreed upon).
Source pages p. 238

Commentary
This passage lists two key conditions (shurut) for valid prostration. First, the place of prostration (where the forehead rests) must not be more than half a cubit higher than the place of the feet. A slight difference is excused, but exceeding half a cubit invalidates the prostration unless one performs another valid prostration. An exception is made for extreme crowding (zahma), where one may prostrate on the back of another person who is also praying, provided the person beneath is in the same prayer; otherwise, it is invalid. Second, the conditions for hands, knees, and feet: one must place at least one hand and one knee on the ground (the correct view), and some part of the toes (the inner side facing qibla) must be placed. Placing the top (upper side) of the foot is insufficient because the hadith specifies 'tips of the feet'. The proof is the well-known hadith from Bukhari and Muslim commanding prostration on seven bones: forehead, hands, knees, and tips of feet. This hadith establishes that these parts must touch the ground for the prostration to be valid.

Key Terms
ذراع (dhira'): A cubit; a unit of measurement approximately the length of forearm; half a cubit is the permissible height difference.
ظاهر القدم (zahir al-qadam): The upper side (top) of the foot; not considered a valid placement for prostration; only the toes (tips) are valid.
زحمة (zahma): Extreme crowding; an excuse allowing prostration on another person's back during prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if the place of prostration is less than half a cubit higher than the feet?
A) The prostration is invalid
B) The prostration is valid
C) It requires compensation (sajdah sahw)
D) It is disliked

Key Takeaway
The validity of sujood depends on the forehead not being more than half a cubit above the feet and the placement of at least one hand, one knee, and the toes on the ground.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Conditions of Sujood: Body Parts and Height
Explaining the required body parts and height conditions for valid sujood

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the required body parts for valid sujood, distinguish the ruling of the forehead (fard) from the nose (wajib), and apply the height condition and placement of limbs.

Core Idea
Sajdah requires seven bones: forehead (fard), hands, knees, and toes; the nose is wajib, and the spot must be within half a cubit of the feet.

In this lesson, we unpack the conditions of sujood (prostration) as established by the Hanafi school. You will learn which body parts must touch the ground, the difference between fard and wajib elements, and the spatial constraint between the place of sujood and the feet. The primary evidence is the prophetic hadith commanding prostration on seven bones.

Guided Path
1
Identify the fard (pillar) body parts
The hadith lists seven bones: forehead, two hands, two knees, and the tips of two feet. The forehead is explicitly mentioned and is the primary pillar. Without the forehead, sujood is invalid.
2
Distinguish the nose as wajib
Unlike the Shafi'i school, the Hanafi school considers the nose wajib (obligatory) but not a pillar. If omitted without excuse, the sujood is valid but the prayer is blameworthy (makruh tahrimi). Abu Hanifa initially allowed sujood on the nose alone but retracted.
The nose is wajib for perfection, not for validity.
3
Apply the height condition
The place of sujood must not be more than half a cubit (approx. 23 cm) higher than the feet. A slight elevation is excused. If it exceeds, sujood is invalid unless due to crowding, then one may prostrate on the back of another praying person.
The exception applies only if the person below is praying and the prostration is on his back.
4
Placement of hands, knees, and toes
At least one hand and one knee are sufficient according to the correct view. For the feet, at least some part of the toes (front part) must touch the ground, directing the inner side toward the qibla. Placing the top of the foot is insufficient.
There is a debate whether both feet are required; the relied-upon position is that at least one toe from each foot must touch.
5
Note the practical differences (thamarah al-khilaf)
The main dispute is whether the nose can replace the forehead. The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is that the forehead is essential; the nose alone invalidates sujood. The retraction of Abu Hanifa settles the matter.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(وَ) من شروط صحة السجود (عدم ارتفاع محل السجودِ عــن موضع القدمين بأكثر من نصف ذراع) ليتحقق صفة الساجد، والارتفاع القليل لا يضر، (وإن زاد على نصف ذراع لم يَجُزِ السجود)، أي: لم يقع معتداً به، كما في « الدراية» فـإن أتـي بـغـيـره معتبراً صحت، وإن لم يأت به حتى خرج من صلاته فسدت (إلا) أن يكون ذلك (الزحمة، سـجـد فـيـهـا عـلـى ظَهْرٍ مُصَلِّ صلاته للضرورة، فإن لم يكن المسجود عليه مصلياً أصلاً، أو كــان فـي غـيـر صــلاة الساجد عليه، لا يصح السجود، وقيل: إنما يجوز إذا كان سجود الثاني على الأرض كما في «الدراية». وتقديم الركوع على السجود .

وقوله : « إِذَا سَجَدَ الْعَبْدُ سَجَدَ مَعَهُ سَبْعَةُ آرَابٍ: وَجْهُهُ وَكَفَّاهُ وَرُكْبَتَاهُ وَقَدْمَاهُ » ) وهو اختيار الفقيه أبي الليث كما في البرهان». ولو سجد ولم يضع قدميه أو إحداهما على الأرض في سجوده لا يجوز سجوده، ولو وضع أحدهما جاز ، كما لو قام على قدم واحدة، وفي « الكفاية » : قال العلامة الزاهدي: ظاهر ما ذكر في «مختصر الكرخي »، و « المحيط»، و « القدوري» يقتضي أنه إذا وضع إحدى القدمين دون الأخرى لا يجوز، وقد رأيت في بعض النسخ أن فيه روايتـيـن كذا في « شــرح المنية»، والمراد من وضع القدم وضع أصابعها. قال الزاهدي: وضع رأس القدمين حالة السجود فرض، وفي «مختصر الكرخي » : سجد ورفع أصابع رجليه عن الأرض لا يجوز، وكذا في «الخلاصة » و « البزازية ) : وضع القدم بوضع أصابعه وإن وضع إصبعـاً واحدة. انتهى. ولا يـكـون وضعاً إلا بتوجيهها نحو القبلة؛ ليتحقق السجود بها، وإلا فهو ووضع ظهـر القـدم سـواء، وهـو غـيـر معتبر وهذا مما يجب التنبيه له والكثير عنه غافلون.
With his forehead, and it is not valid to limit it to the nose, except due to an excuse in the forehead. And [the condition is] that the place of sujood is not higher than the place of the feet by more than half a cubit. If it exceeds half a cubit, sujood is not permissible, except due to crowding, in which case one prostrates on the back of a person who is performing his own prayer. And [the condition is] placing the hands and knees, according to the correct [view], and something of the toes, in the state of sujood, on the ground. And placing the top of the foot is not sufficient.
Because it is solid [bone], it is evidence that sujood on the tip of the nose is not sufficient for him, and that he must place what is solid from it. And from Abu Hanifa: that if he places the tip of the nose, it is not permissible; rather it is permissible only if he places the bone of his nose. Thus in al-Diraya. And since sujood on the nose is wajib, having no part in the conditions of validity—rather it is a condition of perfection—as we will mention that including the nose with the forehead is wajib, he rectified that by saying: (And) he prostrates (with his forehead, and it is not valid to limit it to the nose) according to the most correct [view], except due to an excuse in the forehead. Because the most correct [view] is that the great Imam, may Allah have mercy on him, retracted to agree with his two companions regarding the impermissibility of starting prayer in Persian for one unable to speak Arabic, and the impermissibility of reciting in Persian or any non-Arabic language for one not unable to speak Arabic, and the impermissibility of limiting sujood to the nose without an excuse in the forehead. And the reason for the impermissibility of limiting to the nose is what we narrated: 'I have been commanded to prostrate on seven bones: on the forehead... etc.' And in a narration: 'The servant is commanded to prostrate on seven limbs' (2) the hadith in al-Burhan. (And) from the conditions of validity of sujood (is that the place of sujood is not higher than the place of the feet by more than half a cubit) to achieve the description of the one prostrating, and a small height does no harm. (And if it exceeds half a cubit, sujood is not permissible), i.e., it is not considered valid, as in al-Diraya. If he then performs a valid sujood [elsewhere], his prayer is valid; if he does not do it until he leaves his prayer, it is invalid. (Except) if that (crowding) occurs, he prostrates in it on the back of a person performing his prayer due to necessity. If the one on whom he prostrates is not praying at all, or is not in the prayer of the one prostrating on him, the sujood is not valid. And it is said: it is permissible only if the second sujood is on the ground, as in al-Diraya. (And) from the conditions of validity of sujood (is placing) one of the two hands (and) one of the two knees (according to the correct [view]) as we have mentioned and as we narrated (3) (and) placing (something of the toes), directing its inner side toward the qibla, (in the state of sujood on the ground, and it is not sufficient for the validity of sujood (placing the top of the foot) because it is not its place, due to his saying: 'I have been commanded to prostrate on seven bones: on the forehead, the two hands, the two knees, and the tips of the two feet' agreed upon.

And precedence of ruku over sujood.
(1)
And his saying: 'When the servant prostrates, seven limbs prostrate with him: his face, his palms, his knees, and his feet' ( ) and it is the choice of al-Faqih Abu al-Layth as in al-Burhan. And if he prostrates without placing his feet or one of them on the ground in his sujood, his sujood is not valid. And if he places one of them, it is permissible, just as if he stood on one foot. And in al-Kifaya: al-Allama al-Zahidi said: The apparent meaning of what is mentioned in Mukhtasar al-Karkhi, al-Muhit, and al-Quduri implies that if he places one foot without the other, it is not permissible. And I have seen in some copies that there are two narrations, thus in Sharh al-Munya. And the meaning of 'placing the foot' is placing its toes. Al-Zahidi said: Placing the top of the feet in the state of sujood is fard. And in Mukhtasar al-Karkhi: If he prostrates and raises his toes from the ground, it is not permissible. Similarly in al-Khulasa and al-Bazzaziyya: placing the foot is by placing its toes, even if he places one toe. End. And it is not considered placing except by directing them toward the qibla, so that sujood is achieved with them; otherwise, it is the same as placing the top of the foot, and that is not considered. And this is something that must be noted, and many are heedless of it.
Source pages p. 238

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof discussing the conditions for valid sujood (prostration) in prayer. The author first states the core requirement: sujood is performed with the forehead, and it is not valid to limit it to the nose unless there is an excuse affecting the forehead. This is based on the hadith commanding prostration on seven bones, including the forehead. The commentary clarifies an intra-Hanafi dispute: initially, Abu Hanifa allowed sujood on the tip of the nose alone, but he later retracted to agree with the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) that the forehead is essential. The nose is considered wajib (obligatory) for perfection but not a condition of validity; thus, omitting the nose without excuse does not invalidate sujood but is makruh tahrimi. Next, the passage addresses the height condition: the place of sujood must not be more than half a cubit above the place of the feet. If it exceeds this, sujood is invalid unless due to crowding, where one may prostrate on the back of a praying person. The exception applies only if the person below is praying and the prostrator's sujood is on his back; otherwise, it is invalid. Finally, the passage covers the placement of hands, knees, and toes. The correct view is that placing at least one hand and one knee is sufficient, but placing something of the toes (the front part) on the ground is required. The top of the foot is not sufficient. The hadith about seven bones is cited as proof. The commentary also notes a debate about placing both feet versus one: some sources indicate sujood is valid with one foot, while others require both. The relied-upon position is that at least one toe from each foot must touch the ground, directed toward the qibla.

Key Terms
أرنبة (arnabah): The tip of the nose.
جبهة (jabhah): The forehead, specifically the area between the eyebrows and the hairline.
سجود (sujood): Prostration; a pillar of prayer consisting of placing the specified limbs on the ground.
ذراع (dhira'): A cubit; a unit of length approximately 46.5 cm in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi fiqh, what is the ruling if a person prostrates with his forehead but lifts his toes off the ground?
A) Sujood valid if at least one hand and one knee are placed.
B) Sujood invalid because toes are required to touch.
C) Sujood valid but makruh.
D) Sujood invalid only if both feet are lifted.

Key Takeaway
Valid sujood requires the forehead (fard), at least part of the toes, hands, and knees to touch the ground, and the prostration spot must be within half a cubit of the feet.

The Obligatory Order of Ruku before Sujood
Explaining the obligation to perform ruku before sujood in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the order of ruku before sujood and identify when a violation invalidates the prayer and when it can be rectified.

Core Idea
Order of actions in prayer is fard; missing the sequence invalidates, but a missed second sajdah can be made up.

This lesson examines a key fiqh principle: the prescribed order (tartib) of actions in salah. Using a passage from Nur al-Idah, we will see why ruku must precede sujood, how this relates to other conditions like recitation before ruku, and the exceptional case of the second sajdah. Understanding this helps ensure the validity of your prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage rules that ruku must precede sujood. This is a condition (shart) for the validity of both actions. Violating this order renders the prayer invalid.
This is the central ruling.
2
Understand the legal reasoning (ta'lil)
The author explains that each action has a prescribed 'place' in the prayer sequence. Order must be maintained because the actions are unified in their legislation. Missing the order disrupts the integrity of the prayer.
The rationale is that 'what is unified in its legislation is considered to exist in form and meaning in its place'.
3
Extend to other order requirements
The passage parallels the condition of recitation before ruku: if one bows without reciting the obligatory portion in its proper place, the prayer is invalid. Similarly, the final sitting (qa'dah akhirah) is a condition (or pillar) that must follow the prostrations.
These are additional applications of the same principle.
4
Examine the exception for the second sajdah
If the second sajdah of a rak'ah is missed, it can be performed later (e.g., after standing for the next rak'ah) before any invalidating action. It is then considered to attach to its original place in meaning, preserving the validity of the rak'ah.
This exception applies only to repeated actions like the second sajdah.

Source Text

(And) it is a condition for the validity of ruku and sujood (that ruku precedes sujood), just as it is a condition that recitation precedes ruku in themselves. And if the place of ruku is not specified for recitation as a condition for permissibility, because if the place of recitation is missed, as when one bows in the second rak'ah of Fajr or Maghrib, or the third of the four-rakah [prayer] and he had not recited the obligatory [recitation] in what he performed, it is not valid. Because observing what is not prescribed repeatedly in the rak'ah is a condition for the prayer remaining valid. Similarly, the condition that is later than the pillars, which is the final sitting, is a condition for completing the pillars according to some, and some consider it a pillar. So if one bows before standing, or prostrates before bowing, it is not permissible. Similarly, if one sits for the amount of tashahhud and then remembers that he owes a prostration or recitation, his sitting becomes invalid, because order is obligatory in it. And it is only obligatory because what is unified in its legislation is considered to exist in form and meaning in its place, to avoid missing what is attached to it, whether what is attached is a part or a whole. For example: bowing is a part; if it is missed, what is attached to it is missed, which is the rak'ah. So the prostration after standing and the final sitting are attached to all the rak'ahs. So if it is missed such that it is not corrected by omitting it while its place exists, what is attached is invalidated. As when one prostrates for an extra rak'ah and had not sat for the amount of tashahhud at the end of his prayer. As for missing one repeated action—which is the second prostration—if he leaves it and then performs it in another place before doing anything that invalidates the prayer, then it attaches to its original place, so it is considered to exist in meaning even if not in form. For example: if he prostrates once and then stands for another rak'ah, his previous rak'ah is not invalidated if he performs the missed prostration after that in

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof discussing the obligatory order of actions in prayer: ruku (bowing) must precede sujood (prostration). The author states that this order is a condition for the validity of both ruku and sujood. Parallel to this, recitation (qira'ah) must precede ruku. If one bows without having recited the obligatory portion (e.g., Surah al-Fatihah) in the correct place, the prayer is invalid. The commentary extends this to other order requirements: if one bows before standing, or prostrates before bowing, it is not permissible. Similarly, if one sits for tashahhud and then remembers an omitted prostration or recitation, the sitting is invalidated because the order is fard (obligatory). The author provides a rationale: each action has a prescribed place in the prayer sequence; performing it out of order disrupts the integrity of the prayer. An exception is made for the second prostration (sajdah) within the same rak'ah: if one leaves it and then performs it after standing for the next rak'ah, it attaches to its original place in meaning, thus the earlier rak'ah remains valid as long as no nullifying action occurs in between. The text breaks off while giving an example, but the principle is clear: order is essential, but some omissions can be rectified if caught in time.

Key Terms
ترتيب (tartib): Order; the prescribed sequence of actions in prayer (qiyam, ruku, sujood, etc.).
فرض (fard): Obligatory; something that must be performed and if omitted intentionally invalidates the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) The final sitting (qa'dah akhirah) is unanimously considered a pillar.
D) Observing the order of ruku before sujood is a condition for the validity of both.

Key Takeaway
Order of ruku before sujood is a fard condition in Hanafi prayer; missing it invalidates, but a missed second sajdah can be rectified later.
