Placing the Feet in Sujud
Ruling on foot placement in sujud with proof and dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minimum requirement for placing the feet in sujud and identify the conditions for its validity according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Prostration requires at least one foot placed with toes to the qibla – a disputed but relied-upon view.

The prostration (sujud) is a pillar of prayer, and its validity depends on certain conditions. One of these is placing the feet on the ground. This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on how many feet must be placed and the correct orientation, drawing on a hadith and the commentaries of Hanafi scholars. There is a notable intra-Hanafi dispute on whether one or both feet are required, which we will clarify.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act in question is placing the feet (or foot) on the ground during sujud. The ruling is that this is obligatory (fard) – without it, the prostration is invalid.
The text states: 'if he prostrated and did not place his feet or one of them... his prostration is not valid.'
2
Locate the primary dalil
The commentator quotes the hadith: 'When the slave prostrates, there prostrate with him seven limbs: his face, his palms, his knees, and his feet.' This hadith is the proof for the obligation.
The hadith is ahad, thus zanni al-thubut, but accepted as proof for obligation in Hanafi usul.
3
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute
Some Hanafi texts (Mukhtasar al-Karkhi, al-Muhit, al-Quduri) imply both feet must be placed, while others allow one foot. Al-Zahidi mentions two narrations. The commentator favors the single-foot view, analogizing to standing on one foot.
The dispute is within the school; both positions are from known authorities.
4
Determine the conditions for valid placement
The 'foot' means the front part (toes). Placing the back of the foot or not directing toes to the qibla does not count as placement. Even one toe suffices, as per al-Khulasah and al-Bazzaziyyah.
Direction to the qibla is a necessary condition for the placement to be valid.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that placing at least one foot with toes facing the qibla is sufficient, as this is the view presented by the commentator and supported by Faqih Abu al-Layth and al-Zahidi.
The tarjih authority is the commentator himself, citing the choice of Faqih Abu al-Layth.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقوله : « إِذَا سَجَدَ الْعَبْدُ سَجَدَ مَعَهُ سَبْعَةُ آرَابٍ: وَجْهُهُ وَكَفَّاهُ وَرُكْبَتَاهُ وَقَدْمَاهُ » ) وهو اختيار الفقيه أبي الليث كما في البرهان». ولو سجد ولم يضع قدميه أو إحداهما على الأرض في سجوده لا يجوز سجوده، ولو وضع أحدهما جاز ، كما لو قام على قدم واحدة، وفي « الكفاية » : قال العلامة الزاهدي: ظاهر ما ذكر في «مختصر الكرخي »، و « المحيط»، و « القدوري» يقتضي أنه إذا وضع إحدى القدمين دون الأخرى لا يجوز، وقد رأيت في بعض النسخ أن فيه روايتـيـن كذا في « شــرح المنية»، والمراد من وضع القدم وضع أصابعها. قال الزاهدي: وضع رأس القدمين حالة السجود فرض، وفي «مختصر الكرخي » : سجد ورفع أصابع رجليه عن الأرض لا يجوز، وكذا في «الخلاصة » و « البزازية ) : وضع القدم بوضع أصابعه وإن وضع إصبعـاً واحدة. انتهى. ولا يـكـون وضعاً إلا بتوجيهها نحو القبلة؛ ليتحقق السجود بها، وإلا فهو ووضع ظهـر القـدم سـواء، وهـو غـيـر معتبر وهذا مما يجب التنبيه له والكثير عنه غافلون.
And his saying: 'When the slave prostrates, there prostrate with him seven limbs: his face, his palms, his knees, and his feet.' And this is the choice of Faqih Abu al-Layth as in al-Burhan. And if he prostrated and did not place his feet or one of them on the ground in his prostration, his prostration is not valid. And if he placed one of them, it is permissible, just as if he stood on one foot. And in al-Kifayah: 'Allamah al-Zahidi said: The apparent meaning of what is mentioned in Mukhtasar al-Karkhi, al-Muhit, and al-Quduri requires that if he places one of the feet without the other, it is not permissible. And I have seen in some copies that there are two narrations, thus in Sharh al-Munyah. And the meaning of placing the foot is placing its toes. Al-Zahidi said: Placing the front part of the feet in the state of prostration is obligatory. And in Mukhtasar al-Karkhi: If he prostrates and raises the toes of his feet from the ground, it is not permissible. Similarly in al-Khulasah and al-Bazzaziyyah: Placing the foot is by placing its toes, even if he places one finger. End. And it is not considered placement unless by directing them towards the qibla, so that prostration is realized with them. Otherwise, it is the same as placing the back of the foot, which is not considered. And this is something that must be noted, and many are heedless of it.
Source pages p. 239

Commentary
This passage, from the commentary on Nur al-Idah, addresses a specific condition of sujud: the requirement to place the feet (or at least one foot) on the ground. The commentator begins by quoting the hadith that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said that seven limbs prostrate with the person: the face, the two palms, the two knees, and the two feet. This hadith is used by Faqih Abu al-Layth to support the obligation of placing these limbs. The ruling clarifies that if a person prostrates without placing either foot on the ground, the prostration is invalid. However, placing just one foot suffices, analogous to standing on one foot. Then the commentator mentions a difference: according to the apparent meaning of Mukhtasar al-Karkhi, al-Muhit, and al-Quduri, placing only one foot is not sufficient; rather both feet must be placed. But al-Zahidi mentions that there are two narrations on this point. The correct interpretation of 'placing the foot' is placing the toes (the front part). Al-Zahidi states that placing the front of the feet during prostration is obligatory. Even if one places a single toe, it is considered placement according to al-Khulasah and al-Bazzaziyyah. Finally, an important practical note: the placement is only valid if the toes are directed towards the qibla, because prostration is realized by facing the direction of prayer. Placing the back of the feet is equivalent to not placing them at all. Many people are neglectful of this detail.

Key Terms
آرَابٍ (aaraab): Limbs; specifically, the seven limbs that touch the ground in prostration.
وضع القدم (wad' al-qadam): Placing the front part of the foot (toes) on the ground in sujud.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is required for a valid placement of the foot in sujud?
A) Both feet must be placed flat on the ground.
B) At least one foot must be placed with the toes directed to the qibla.
C) The heel must touch the ground.
D) The foot can be placed in any orientation.

Key Takeaway
Sujud requires at least one foot placed with toes facing the qibla; the Hanafi school relies on the view allowing one foot despite a minority opinion requiring both.

Conditions and Order of Sujud: Feet, Hands, Raising and Returning
Explaining conditions for sujud including order and separation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi conditions for valid sujud, identify the relied-upon view on raising between sujuds, and apply these rules to evaluate the correctness of a prostration in prayer.

Core Idea
Sujud requires proper order, limb placement, and a valid separation between the two prostrations; raising to near sitting is the relied-upon view.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah details several key conditions for sujud in Salah. It begins by clarifying the placement of the feet (and their toes) and the hands, then establishes the mandatory order: ruku must precede sujud, just as recitation precedes ruku. The main focus is on the debated requirement of raising the head and body after the first sujud before performing the second. The commentator reviews four narrations from Imam Abu Hanifa and declares that raising to near sitting (qurb al-qu'ud) is the most correct view, emphasizing that the two sujuds must be clearly separated. Additionally, the obligation to lift and re-place the hands in harmony with the forehead is explained through the hadith of the hands prostrating like the face.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rulings on limb placement
List the conditions for the feet (toes placed, directed to qibla) and hands (obligatory to place at least one, and to raise and replace them with the forehead). Note the specific positions and the ruling that placing the front part of the foot is obligatory.
The passage mentions that merely placing the back of the foot is insufficient.
2
Understand the condition of order
Explain why ruku must come before sujud, and recitation before ruku. Use the example of performing ruku without reciting the obligatory portion: the prayer becomes invalid because each element must occur in its proper place.
The principle of 'ma ittahadat shar'iyyatuha' (unity of legality) is invoked.
3
Analyze the raising requirement
Compare the four narrations from Abu Hanifa on how much to raise: (1) to near sitting (most correct), (2) merely removing the forehead, (3) raising enough for wind to pass, (4) minimum raising. Identify which view al-Hidayah and the commentary support and why.
The key argument: one must be closer to sitting than to prostration to count as having completed the first sujud.
4
Apply the ruling on returning to sujud
State that the second sujud is obligatory (fard) by consensus. Explain that the hands must be lifted and replaced because they follow the forehead, as per the hadith. If the hands are not placed again, the second sujud is not valid.
The commentator cites al-Suyuti's narration that the seven limbs require tranquility and synchronization with the forehead.
5
Evaluate practical consequences
Consider what happens if one violates these conditions. For example, if one only slightly lifts the forehead before the second sujud, the second sujud is invalid. If the toes are not placed, the sujud is invalid. If the hands are not raised and replaced, the second sujud is incomplete.
These are serious issues that affect the validity of the prayer.

Source Text

وتقديم الركوع على السجودِ . (1) وقوله : « إِذَا سَجَدَ الْعَبْدُ سَجَدَ مَعَهُ سَبْعَةُ آرَابٍ: وَجْهُهُ وَكَفَّاهُ وَرُكْبَتَاهُ وَقَدْمَاهُ » ) وهو اختيار الفقيه أبي الليث كما في البرهان». ولو سجد ولم يضع قدميه أو إحداهما على الأرض في سجوده لا يجوز سجوده، ولو وضع أحدهما جاز ، كما لو قام على قدم واحدة، وفي « الكفاية » : قال العلامة الزاهدي: ظاهر ما ذكر في «مختصر الكرخي »، و « المحيط»، و « القدوري» يقتضي أنه إذا وضع إحدى القدمين دون الأخرى لا يجوز، وقد رأيت في بعض النسخ أن فيه روايتـيـن كذا في « شــرح المنية»، والمراد من وضع القدم وضع أصابعها. قال الزاهدي: وضع رأس القدمين حالة السجود فرض، وفي «مختصر الكرخي » : سجد ورفع أصابع رجليه عن الأرض لا يجوز، وكذا في «الخلاصة » و « البزازية ) : وضع القدم بوضع أصابعه وإن وضع إصبعـاً واحدة. انتهى. ولا يـكـون وضعاً إلا بتوجيهها نحو القبلة؛ ليتحقق السجود بها، وإلا فهو ووضع ظهـر القـدم سـواء، وهـو غـيـر معتبر وهذا مما يجب التنبيه له والكثير عنه غافلون. (و) يشترط لصحة الركوع والسجود (تقديـم ع على السجودِ كما يشترط تقديم القراءة على الركوع في حد ذاتها. وإن لم يـتـعـيـن محـل الركوع القراءة عيناً للجواز، لأنه إذا فات محل القراءة، كما إذا ركع في ثانية الفجر أو المغرب، أو ثالثة الرباعية ولم يكن قرأ المفروض فيما أداه لم يصح، لأن رعاية ما لم يشرع مكرراً في الركعة شرط لبقاء الصلاة على الصحة، وكذا الشرط المتأخر عن الأركان، وهو القعود الأخير، فإنه شرط إتمام الأركان عند البعض، وبعضهم يعدّه ركناً حتى لو ركع قبل القيام، أو سـجـد قـبـل الـركـوع لا يجوز، وكذا لو قعد قدر التشهد ثم تذكر أنَّ عليه سجدةً أو قراءةً بطل القعود، لأن الترتيب فيه فرض، وإنما كان فرضاً؛ لأن ما اتحدت شرعيته يراعى وجوده صورة ومعنى في محله، تحرزاً عن تفويت ما تعلـق به، سواء كان ما تعلق به جزءاً أو كلاً مثاله: الركوع جزء إذا فات فات ما تعلق به، وهو الركعة، فـلا د السجود عقب القيام والقعود الأخير متعلق به كل الركعات، فإذا فـات عـن تصح بتركه مع وجود . محله بطل ما تعلق به، كما إذا سجد لركعة زائدة ولم يكن قعد على آخر صلاته قدر التشهد، وأمـا فوات أحد فعلي المتكرر -وهو السجود الثاني - إذا تركه ثم أتى به [ في ] محل آخر قبل إتيانـه بما ينافي الصلاة فإنه يلتحق بمحله الأول، فكان موجوداً فيه معنى، وإن لم يوجد صورة، مثاله: إذا سجد واحدة ثم قام لركعة أخرى، لا تبطل ركعته السابقة إذا أتي بالسجدة المتروكة بعد ذلك في حرمة الصلاة، لكنه إذا أتى بها بعد القعود الأخير يلزمه إعادته لأنه لختم الأركان، فلم يكن فعله قبل إتيانه بالسجدة معتداً ،به إذ لا يمكن استيفاء ما تعلق به جزاً أو كلاً من جنس ما اتحدت شرعيته، لضرورة اتحاده في الشرعية، والأفراد بالشرعية دليل توقف ذلك الذي تعلـق بـه عـلـى وجوده صورة ومعنى (وَ) يشترط (الرَّفْعُ منَ السُّجودِ إلى قُرْبِ القعود، على الأصح) ليصح إتيانه بالسجدة الثانية في الأصح عن أبي حنيفة الله ؛ لأنه يُعَدُّ جالساً بقربه من القعود، فتحققت السجدة الثانية، فلو كان إلى السجود أقرب لم تجز الثانية، لأنه يعد ساجداً، إذ ما قَرُبَ من الشيء له حكمه، كذا في « البرهان»، وهذه إحدى روايات أربع عن الإمام، وصححها في « الهداية» بقوله: وهـو الأصح، احترازاً عما ذكر بعض المشايخ أنه إذا زايل جبهته عن الأرض ثـم أعـادهـا جــاز، وعـن الحسن بن زياد ما هو قريب منه فإنه قال: إذا رفع رأسه بقدر ما تجري فيه الريـــح جــاز، وعمـا ذكـر القدوري: أنه مقدّر بأدنى ما ينطلق عليه اسم الرفع، وهو رواية أبي يوسف كذا في « المحيط»، وجعل شيخ الإسلام هذا القول أصح، وقال محمد بن سلمة: مقدار ما يقع عند الناظر أنه رفع رأسه، فإن فعل ذلك جاز أي: السجود الثاني وإلا فلا، وهذا قريب إلى ما ذكر في « الهداية»، كذا في معراج الدراية». وقال صاحب البحر » : لم أر من صحح رواية الرفع بقدر ما تمر الريح بينه وبين الأرض. (وَ) يفترض ( العَوْدُ إلى السجودِ) لأن السجود الثاني كالأول فرض بإجماع الأمة. تنبيه: قدمنا أن الظاهر من الرواية ما ذهب إليه الفقيه أبو الليث رحمه الله تعالى: من افتراض وضع اليدين في السجود، وأن السجود لا يصح بدون وضع إحديهما ومن المقرر أن العود للسجود فرض ولا يتحقق إلا بما يتحقق به السجدة السابقة، فيلزمه رفع اليدين بعد رفع رأسه من السجدة الأولى، ثم إعادة وضعهما أو إحديهما في السجدة الثانية، لتصح السجدة الثانية، ويتحقق تكــرار السجود، وبه وردت السنّة كما نقله الجلال السيوطي رحمه الله في ( الينبوع» عن ابن العماد في التعقبات بقوله: إذا قلنا بوجوب وضع الأعضاء السبعة فلابد من الطمأنينة بها كالجبهة، ولا بد أن يضعها حالة وضع الجبهة، حتى لو وضعها ثم رفعها ثم وضع الجبهة أو عكس، لم يكن لأنـهـا أعضاء تابعة للجبهة، وإذا رفع الجبهة من السجدة الأولى وجب عليه رفع الكفين أيضاً لقوله : « إِنَّ اليَدينِ يَسْجُدَانِ كَمَا تَسْجُدُ الجَبْهَةُ، فَإِذَا سَجَدْتُمْ فَضَعوهُمَا، وإذا رفعتُم فَارفعوهُمَا » .
And presenting ruku before sujud. And his saying: 'When the slave prostrates, there prostrate with him seven limbs: his face, his palms, his knees, and his feet.' And this is the choice of Faqih Abu al-Layth as in al-Burhan. And if he prostrated and did not place his feet or one of them on the ground in his prostration, his prostration is not valid. And if he placed one of them, it is permissible, just as if he stood on one foot. And in al-Kifayah: 'Allamah al-Zahidi said: The apparent meaning of what is mentioned in Mukhtasar al-Karkhi, al-Muhit, and al-Quduri requires that if he places one of the feet without the other, it is not permissible. And I have seen in some copies that there are two narrations, thus in Sharh al-Munyah. And the meaning of placing the foot is placing its toes. Al-Zahidi said: Placing the front part of the feet in the state of prostration is obligatory. And in Mukhtasar al-Karkhi: If he prostrates and raises the toes of his feet from the ground, it is not permissible. Similarly in al-Khulasah and al-Bazzaziyyah: Placing the foot is by placing its toes, even if he places one finger. End. And it is not considered placement unless by directing them towards the qibla, so that prostration is realized with them. Otherwise, it is the same as placing the back of the foot, which is not considered. And this is something that must be noted, and many are heedless of it. (And) it is a condition for the validity of ruku and sujud (presenting ruku before sujud, just as presenting recitation before ruku is a condition in itself. And although the place of ruku is not determined by recitation per se for validity, because if the place of recitation is missed, as when he performs ruku in the second rak'ah of Fajr or Maghrib, or the third of a four-rak'ah prayer without having recited the obligatory recitation in what he performed, it is not valid, because observing what is not repeated in the rak'ah is a condition for the prayer remaining valid. Similarly, the condition that comes after the pillars, which is the final sitting, is a condition for completing the pillars according to some, and some consider it a pillar. So if he performs ruku before standing, or prostrates before ruku, it is not permissible. Similarly, if he sits for the amount of tashahhud and then remembers that he owes a prostration or recitation, his sitting is invalidated, because order therein is obligatory. And it is obligatory because that which is unified in its legality is observed to exist in form and meaning in its place, to guard against losing that which is attached to it, whether what is attached is a part or a whole. For example: ruku is a part; if it is missed, what is attached to it is missed, which is the rak'ah. So prostration after standing and the final sitting are attached to all the rak'ahs. So if it is missed, the act is not valid by abandoning it while its place exists; rather what is attached to it becomes invalid. As when he prostrates for an extra rak'ah without having sat at the end of his prayer for the amount of tashahhud. And regarding the loss of one of the repeated acts—which is the second prostration—if he leaves it and then performs it in another place before doing something that contradicts the prayer, then it attaches to its original place, so it exists meaningfully though not in form. Example: if he performs one prostration and then stands for another rak'ah, his previous rak'ah does not become invalid if he performs the missed prostration afterwards within the prayer. But if he performs it after the final sitting, he must repeat it because it is for completing the pillars, so his action before performing the prostration is not considered valid. Because it is not possible to fulfill what is attached to it, whether part or whole, from the type of that which is unified in its legality, due to the necessity of its unity in legality. And the individuals by legality are evidence that what is attached to it depends on its existence in form and meaning. (And) it is a condition (raising from sujud to near sitting, on the most correct view) so that he can validly perform the second sujud, on the most correct view from Abu Hanifa—because he is considered sitting by being near sitting, so the second prostration is realized. If he were closer to prostration, the second would not be valid because he is considered prostrating, since what is close to a thing has its ruling. Thus in al-Burhan. And this is one of four narrations from the Imam, which al-Hidayah corrected by saying: it is the most correct, as a precaution against what some mashayikh mentioned: that if he removes his forehead from the ground and then returns it, it is valid; and against what Hasan ibn Ziyad said close to it: that if he raises his head to the extent that the wind passes between it and the ground, it is valid; and against what al-Quduri mentioned: that it is estimated by the minimum that the name of raising applies to, which is the narration of Abu Yusuf, thus in al-Muhit. And Shaykh al-Islam considered this saying more correct. Muhammad ibn Salamah said: the amount that appears to the observer that he has raised his head; if he does that, it is valid—i.e., the second prostration—otherwise not. And this is close to what is mentioned in al-Hidayah, thus in Miraj al-Dirayah. And the author of al-Bahr said: I have not seen anyone who corrected the narration of raising to the extent that the wind passes between him and the ground. (And) returning to prostration is obligatory because the second prostration is obligatory like the first by consensus of the ummah. Caution: We have mentioned that the apparent from the narration is what Faqih Abu al-Layth went to: the obligation of placing the hands in sujud, and that prostration is not valid without placing one of them. And it is established that returning to sujud is obligatory and is only realized by that which realizes the previous prostration. So it is necessary for him to raise his hands after raising his head from the first prostration, then to replace them or one of them in the second prostration, so that the second prostration is valid and the repetition of prostration is realized. And thus the Sunnah has been reported, as al-Jalal al-Suyuti narrated in al-Yanbu' from Ibn al-'Imad in al-Ta'aqqubat: If we say that placing the seven limbs is obligatory, then it is necessary to have tranquility with them like the forehead, and he must place them at the time of placing the forehead. So that if he places them and then raises them and then places the forehead, or the opposite, it is not valid because they are limbs subservient to the forehead. And when he raises the forehead from the first prostration, he must also raise the palms, because of his saying: 'Indeed, the hands prostrate as the face prostrates. So when you prostrate, place them, and when you raise, raise them.'
Source pages p. 239

Commentary
This passage covers multiple conditions for sujud. It begins by repeating the ruling on placing the feet (from the previous lesson), then moves to the condition of order: ruku must precede sujud, just as recitation precedes ruku. The commentator explains that if one performs ruku early without reciting the obligatory portion, the prayer is invalid. Similarly, if one prostrates before ruku, or sits before completing, it invalidates the act. The key point is that each element must occur in its proper place. The passage then discusses the condition of raising from sujud before the second prostration. The relied-upon view (al-ashahh) is that one must raise to near sitting (qurb al-qu'ud), meaning the person is closer to sitting than to prostration. There are four narrations from Abu Hanifa: (1) the most correct: raising to near sitting; (2) some say merely removing the forehead; (3) Hasan ibn Ziyad says raising enough for wind to pass; (4) Abu Yusuf says the minimum that counts as raising. The commentator notes that the author of al-Hidayah corrects the first view. Finally, the obligation of returning to the second sujud is stated by consensus. A note adds that since placing the hands is obligatory (according to the chosen view of Abu al-Layth), one must also lift the hands after the first prostration and then place them again for the second sujud, because the hands follow the forehead in prostration, as per the hadith 'The hands prostrate as the face prostrates.'

Key Terms
الرفع من السجود (al-raf' min al-sujud): Raising the head and body from the first prostration to a state between prostration and sitting, close to sitting, before the second prostration.
العود إلى السجود (al-'awd ila al-sujud): Returning to the second prostration after having raised from the first.
قرب القعود (qurb al-qu'ud): Near sitting: the state after raising from sujud where the person is closer to the sitting posture than to the prostration posture.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the most correct Hanafi view, what is the required state after the first sujud before performing the second?
A) The person must stand upright.
B) The person must sit completely (jalsa).
C) The person must raise to near sitting (qurb al-qu'ud).
D) Only the forehead must be removed from the ground.

Key Takeaway
Valid sujud requires proper order, full limb placement (including toes and hands), and a clear separation between the two prostrations by raising to near sitting.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Rising Between Prostrations: Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Explaining the required action between two prostrations and the obligatory raising of hands

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four Hanafi opinions on the required elevation between prostrations, identify the mufta bihi position, and apply the ruling to determine validity of the second prostration.

Core Idea
Rise to near sitting between prostrations—otherwise the second prostration is invalid.

The transition between the two prostrations (sajdatayn) is more than a mere pause; its proper execution is essential for the validity of the second prostration. Within the Hanafi school, there is a well-known disagreement on how much one must lift the head. This lesson walks through the four narrations from Imam Abu Hanifa and his disciples, the evidence behind each, and the relied-upon position that a worshipper must rise until close to the sitting posture.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what the passage is ruling on: the rising from the first prostration (رفع من السجود) and the returning to prostration (عود إلى السجود). Recognize that the former is a condition (shart) for the latter.
2
Catalog the intra-Hanafi opinions
List the four views: (1) Abu Hanifa: rise to near sitting; (2) Abu Yusuf: minimal lifting; (3) al-Hasan ibn Ziyad: enough for wind to pass; (4) some mashayikh: mere removal of forehead.
Each view has its proponents and textual basis.
3
Trace the tarjih mechanism
Understand why al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah preferred Abu Hanifa's view (al-ashah). Note the principle 'ما قرب من الشيء له حكمه' (whatever is close to something has its ruling).
The tarjih authority is critical for mufta bihi.
4
Apply the mufta bihi to a scenario
Given a person who lifts only a little (e.g., forehead barely leaves ground), determine the validity of the second prostration according to the relied-upon view.
Result: second prostration invalid, prayer incomplete.
5
Note the hand-raising obligation
The passage also discusses the necessity of raising the hands when rising from prostration, based on hadith. Understand this as a separate but related obligation that follows from the ruling on the palms being like the face.
This is linked to the view of al-Faqih Abu al-Layth on the obligation of placing palms.

Source Text

والرفع من السجودِ إلى قُرْبِ القعود على الأصحُ والعَودُ إلى السجودِ . حرمة الصلاة، لكنه إذا أتى بها بعد القعود الأخير يلزمه إعادته لأنه لختم الأركان، فلم يكن فعله قبل إتيانه بالسجدة معتداً ،به إذ لا يمكن استيفاء ما تعلق به جزاً أو كلاً من جنس ما اتحدت شرعيته، لضرورة اتحاده في الشرعية، والأفراد بالشرعية دليل توقف ذلك الذي تعلـق بـه عـلـى وجوده صورة ومعنى (وَ) يشترط (الرَّفْعُ منَ السُّجودِ إلى قُرْبِ القعود، على الأصح) ليصح إتيانه بالسجدة الثانية في الأصح عن أبي حنيفة الله ؛ لأنه يُعَدُّ جالساً بقربه من القعود، فتحققت السجدة الثانية، فلو كان إلى السجود أقرب لم تجز الثانية، لأنه يعد ساجداً، إذ ما قَرُبَ من الشيء له حكمه، كذا في « البرهان»، وهذه إحدى روايات أربع عن الإمام، وصححها في « الهداية» بقوله: وهـو الأصح، احترازاً عما ذكر بعض المشايخ أنه إذا زايل جبهته عن الأرض ثـم أعـادهـا جــاز، وعـن الحسن بن زياد ما هو قريب منه فإنه قال: إذا رفع رأسه بقدر ما تجري فيه الريـــح جــاز، وعمـا ذكـر القدوري: أنه مقدّر بأدنى ما ينطلق عليه اسم الرفع، وهو رواية أبي يوسف كذا في « المحيط»، وجعل شيخ الإسلام هذا القول أصح، وقال محمد بن سلمة: مقدار ما يقع عند الناظر أنه رفع رأسه، فإن فعل ذلك جاز أي: السجود الثاني وإلا فلا، وهذا قريب إلى ما ذكر في « الهداية»، كذا في معراج الدراية». وقال صاحب البحر » : لم أر من صحح رواية الرفع بقدر ما تمر الريح بينه وبين الأرض. (وَ) يفترض ( العَوْدُ إلى السجودِ) لأن السجود الثاني كالأول فرض بإجماع الأمة. تنبيه: قدمنا أن الظاهر من الرواية ما ذهب إليه الفقيه أبو الليث رحمه الله تعالى: من افتراض وضع اليدين في السجود، وأن السجود لا يصح بدون وضع إحديهما ومن المقرر أن العود للسجود فرض ولا يتحقق إلا بما يتحقق به السجدة السابقة، فيلزمه رفع اليدين بعد رفع رأسه من السجدة الأولى، ثم إعادة وضعهما أو إحديهما في السجدة الثانية، لتصح السجدة الثانية، ويتحقق تكــرار السجود، وبه وردت السنّة كما نقله الجلال السيوطي رحمه الله في ( الينبوع» عن ابن العماد في التعقبات بقوله: إذا قلنا بوجوب وضع الأعضاء السبعة فلابد من الطمأنينة بها كالجبهة، ولا بد أن يضعها حالة وضع الجبهة، حتى لو وضعها ثم رفعها ثم وضع الجبهة أو عكس، لم يكن لأنـهـا أعضاء تابعة للجبهة، وإذا رفع الجبهة من السجدة الأولى وجب عليه رفع الكفين أيضاً لقوله : « إِنَّ اليَدينِ يَسْجُدَانِ كَمَا تَسْجُدُ الجَبْهَةُ، فَإِذَا سَجَدْتُمْ فَضَعوهُمَا، وإذا رفعتُم فَارفعوهُمَا » . ولأصحاب مالك في ذلك قولان وقال ابن العماد أيضاً في كتاب آخر : يجب على المصلي إذا رفــع رأسه من السجدة الأولى أن يرفع يديه من الأرض كما يرفع جبهته؛ لأن السجود يكون بهما مرتين كما يكون بالجبهة، وهذا ظاهر نص الإمام الشافعي في «الأم» فإنه قال: إن القول بوجوب السجود على هذه الأعضاء هو الموافق للحديث، والثابت في الحديث أنه صلى الله عليه وسلم كَانَ إِذَا سَجَدَ وَرَفَعَ رَأْسَهُ مِنَ السجدَةِ الأولى رَفَعَ يَديهِ مِنَ الأرض ووَضَعُهُمَا عَلَى فَخِذَيْهِ ) وقال : «صلوا كَمَا رَأَيْتُمُونِي أصلي ) . وروى ابن عمر عنه أنه قال: ( إِنَّ اليدين يسجدان كما يَسْجُدُ الوَجْهُ، فَإِذَا وَضَعَ أَحَدُكُمْ وَجْهَهُ فَلْيَضَعَهُمَا، وإذا رفعه فَلْيَرْفَعهُمَا ). أخرجه أبو داود والنسائي. وروى مالك في « الموطأ » : أن ابن عمر كان يقول: «مَنْ وَضَعَ جَبْهَتَهُ بِالْأَرْضِ فَلْيَضَعْ كَفَّيْهِ عَلَى الَّذِي وَضَعَ عَلَيْهِ جَبْهَتَهُ، وَإِذَا رَفَعَ فَلْيَرْفَعْهُمَا فَإِنَّ الْيَدَيْنِ يَسْجُدَانِ كَمَا يَسْجُدُ الْوَجْهُ ) انتهى عبارة الإمام السيوطي رحمه الله، قلت: فالحاصل أن رفع اليدين عن الأرض لا بد منه ليتحقق تكرار السجود بـهما كالجبهة، وأمـا صـفـة وضعهما على الفخذين حالة الجلوس بين السجدتين فسنّة، ومن أنكر هذا عليه الدليــل لِمَا يَدَّعِيه، وعليه رَدُّ قول الفقيه أبي الليث الذي قد حكيناه بدليله، والمخالف من الشافعية لمـا قـالـه الجـلال السيوطي حيث قال: لا يشترط رفع اليدين عن الأرض لصحة السجدة الثانية، هو كالمخالف مـن الحنفية لما قاله الفقيه أبو الليث. وتكلموا في حكمة تكرار السجود دون الركوع، فمذهب الفقهاء أن هذا تعبدي لا يطلب فيه المعنى، كأعداد الركعات، وفي (المبسوط » : قيل: إنما كان السجود مثنى ترغيماً للشيطان، فإنه أمِرَ بالسجود فلم يفعل، فنحن نسجد مرتين ترغيمـاً لـه، وإليه أشــار النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم في سجود السهو ترغيماً للشيطان. وقيل: السجدة الأولى إشارة إلى أنـه خـلـق مـن الأرض، والثانية إشارة إلى أنه يعود إليها. قال تعالى: مِنْهَا خَلَقْنَكُمْ وَفِيهَا نُعِيدُكُمْ [طه: ٥٥] وفي « مبسوط» شيخ الإسلام أكثر مشايخنا على أنه توقيف غير معقول المعنى، ومنهم من يذكر لذلك حكمة فقال: حكمته ما روي في بعض الأخبار أن الله تعالى لما أخذ الميثاق من ذرية آدم عليه الصلاة والسلام حيث قال: ﴿وَإِذْ أَخَذَ رَبُّكَ مِنْ بَنِي ءَادَمَ ﴾ [الأعراف: ۱۷۲] أمرهم بالسجود تصديقاً لمـا قـالوا، فسجد المسلمون كلهم وبقي الكافرون، فلما رفعوا رؤوسهم رأوا الكفار لم يسجدوا، فسجدوا ثانياً
And the rising from prostration to near sitting is on the most correct [view], and the returning to prostration. [It is] a necessary condition of the prayer, but if he performs it after the final sitting, he must repeat it because it is the seal of the pillars; his action before performing the prostration was not considered valid, because it is not possible to fulfill what pertains to it partially or completely from a type that is unified in its legality, due to the necessity of its unity in legality, and the individuals by legality are evidence of the dependence of that which pertains to it on its existence in form and meaning. (And) it is conditioned (the rising from prostration to near sitting, on the most correct [view]) so that his performance of the second prostration is valid, on the most correct [view] from Abu Hanifa; because he is considered sitting by his proximity to sitting, so the second prostration is verified. If he were closer to prostration, the second would not be valid, because he is considered prostrating, since whatever is close to something has its ruling. Likewise in al-Burhan. This is one of four narrations from the Imam, and it was deemed correct in al-Hidayah by his saying: 'and it is the most correct,' as a precaution against what some mashayikh mentioned that if he removes his forehead from the ground and then returns it, it is permissible, and from al-Hasan ibn Ziyad something close to it, for he said: if he raises his head to the extent that wind passes through it, it is permissible, and from what al-Quduri mentioned: that it is estimated by the least that the name 'raising' applies to, and that is the narration of Abu Yusuf, likewise in al-Muhit. And Shaykh al-Islam made this statement more correct. And Muhammad ibn Salamah said: the amount that appears to the observer that he has raised his head; if he does that, then the second prostration is valid, otherwise not. And this is close to what is mentioned in al-Hidayah, likewise in Mi'raj al-Dirayah. And the author of al-Bahr said: I have not seen anyone who deemed correct the narration of raising to the extent that the wind passes between him and the ground. (And) it is obligatory (the returning to prostration) because the second prostration is like the first, an obligation by consensus of the Ummah. Note: We have previously presented that the apparent from the narration is what al-Faqih Abu al-Layth went to: the obligation of placing the hands in prostration, and that prostration is not valid without placing one of them. And it is established that returning to prostration is an obligation and it is not realized except by what the previous prostration was realized by. So it is necessary for him to raise the hands after raising his head from the first prostration, then to re-place both of them or one of them in the second prostration, so that the second prostration is valid, and the repetition of prostration is realized, and with this the Sunnah has come, as al-Jalal al-Suyuti narrated in al-Yanbu' from Ibn al-'Imad in al-Ta'qibat, saying: If we say the obligation of placing the seven limbs, then tranquility (tuma'ninah) is necessary with them like the forehead, and he must place them at the time of placing the forehead, to the extent that if he places them then lifts them then places the forehead, or vice versa, it is not [valid] because they are limbs subordinate to the forehead. And when he raises the forehead from the first prostration, it is obligatory upon him to raise the palms as well, due to his saying: 'Indeed the hands prostrate as the forehead prostrates; so when you prostrate, place them, and when you rise, raise them.' And the companions of Malik have two sayings regarding that. And Ibn al-'Imad also said in another book: It is obligatory upon the one praying, when he raises his head from the first prostration, to raise his hands from the ground as he raises his forehead, because prostration occurs with both of them twice as it occurs with the forehead. And this is apparent from the text of Imam al-Shafi'i in al-Umm, for indeed he said: The saying of the obligation of prostration upon these limbs is the one agreeing with the hadith, and what is established in the hadith is that when he prostrated and raised his head from the first prostration, he raised his hands from the ground and placed them on his thighs, and said: 'Pray as you have seen me praying.' And Ibn 'Umar narrated from him that he said: 'Indeed the two hands prostrate as the face prostrates; so when any of you places his face, let him place them, and when he raises it, let him raise them.' Narrated by Abu Dawud and al-Nasa'i. And Malik narrated in al-Muwatta' that Ibn 'Umar used to say: 'Whoever places his forehead on the ground, let him place his palms on that which he placed his forehead on, and when he raises, let him raise them, for indeed the two hands prostrate as the face prostrates.' End of the statement of Imam al-Suyuti. I say: The conclusion is that raising the hands from the ground is necessary so that the repetition of prostration with them is realized like the forehead. As for the manner of placing them on the thighs during the sitting between the two prostrations, it is sunnah. Whoever denies this, the evidence is against his claim, and upon this is the refutation of the statement of al-Faqih Abu al-Layth which we have narrated with its evidence. And the opponent from the Shafi'is due to what al-Jalal al-Suyuti said - that he does not require raising the hands from the ground for the validity of the second prostration - is like the opponent from the Hanafis due to what al-Faqih Abu al-Layth said. And they discussed the wisdom of repeating prostration without bowing. The school of the jurists is that this is devotional (ta'abbudi), whose meaning is not sought, like the numbers of rak'ahs. And in al-Mabsut: It was said that prostration is only performed twice to humiliate Satan, for he was commanded to prostrate and did not do so, so we prostrate twice to humiliate him, and the Prophet alluded to this in the prostration of forgetfulness to humiliate Satan. And it was said: The first prostration indicates that he was created from earth, and the second indicates that he will return to it. Allah says: 'From it We created you, and into it We shall return you' [Ta-Ha: 55]. And in Mabsut of Shaykh al-Islam: Most of our mashayikh hold that it is restrictive (tawqif) not comprehensible by reason, and among them is one who mentions a wisdom for it, saying: Its wisdom is what is narrated in some reports that when Allah took the covenant from the offspring of Adam, where He said: 'And when your Lord took from the children of Adam' [al-A'raf: 172], He commanded them to prostrate in confirmation of what they said. So all the Muslims prostrated, and the disbelievers remained. When they raised their heads, they saw the disbelievers had not prostrated, so they prostrated a second time.
Source pages p. 240

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah Sharh Nur al-Idah explains the rulings related to the transition between the two prostrations (sajdatayn) in prayer. The author addresses two key issues: the required degree of rising after the first prostration, and the obligation of returning to prostration, with particular emphasis on the hands. The passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute (ikhtilaf) as it presents multiple opinions within the Hanafi school regarding the amount of elevation needed between prostrations. Abu Hanifa's view, deemed the most correct (al-ashah) in al-Hidayah by al-Marghinani, requires rising to a position near sitting (qurb al-qu'ood). Other opinions include Abu Yusuf's minimum elevation, al-Hasan ibn Ziyad's wind-passing amount, and some mashayikh considering mere removal of the forehead sufficient. The text then discusses the obligation (fard) of returning to prostration by consensus, and the necessity of raising the hands when rising from the first prostration and replacing them for the second, based on hadith evidence. The author concludes by noting the wisdom of two prostrations as devotional (ta'abbudi) and analogizes to the prostration of forgetfulness.

Key Terms
الرفع من السجود إلى قرب القعود (ar-raf' min as-sujood ila qurb al-qu'ood): The action of lifting the head from the first prostration until one is close to the sitting position (i.e., the back is straight and one is nearly in the sitting posture).
العود إلى السجود (al-'awd ila as-sujood): Returning to prostration after the brief sitting, i.e., performing the second prostration. It is obligatory (fard) by consensus.
وضع اليدين (wad' al-yadayn): Placing the hands (palms) on the ground during prostration. According to al-Faqih Abu al-Layth, it is obligatory; hence, for the second prostration, the hands must be lifted and re-placed.
الأصح (al-ashah): The most correct opinion among the narrations, used here for Abu Hanifa's view.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi Hanafi position, what is the required amount of rising between the two prostrations?
A) Simply remove the forehead from the ground.
B) Lift the head enough for wind to pass underneath.
C) Rise until one is close to the sitting posture (qurb al-qu'ood).
D) Any movement that can be called 'raising'.

Key Takeaway
Rise to near sitting between the two prostrations; otherwise the second prostration is invalid according to the relied-upon Hanafi view.
